Dispute in Ijarah Before Possession: Mutual Oaths and Rescission
Ruling on dispute over rent or benefit in ijarah before possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a lessor and lessee dispute the rent or benefit before possession, identify who swears first and whose evidence is preferred, and explain the qiyas proof linking ijarah to sale.

Core Idea
Before possession, ijarah disputes are resolved like sale disputes: mutual oaths and rescission, with asymmetric evidence weighting.

This passage deals with a common contractual dispute in ijarah (lease): the parties disagree about the rent amount or the duration of the benefit before the lessee has taken possession. The Hanafi school prescribes a specific procedure of mutual oaths (tahalluf) and contract rescission (taradd), with the order of oaths and the precedence of evidence depending on the subject of the dispute. The underlying proof is a clear analogy (qiyas jali) to the same scenario in a sale contract before possession of the sold item. Let us walk through the ruling and its justification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two dispute scenarios
The passage distinguishes between a dispute over the rent (badal al-ijarah) and a dispute over the benefit (al-manfa'ah), i.e., the duration or scope of the lease. The ruling differs in each case regarding who swears first and whose evidence is preferred.
Remember: rent is the price, benefit is the subject matter.
2
Determine the order of oaths
If the dispute is about the rent, the lessee (musta'jir) swears first because he is the one who would pay; if the dispute is about the benefit, the lessor (mu'jir) swears first because he claims the lesser benefit.
The oath is taken by the party who would benefit from the standard contract terms.
3
Apply the rules of evidence and refusal
If one party refuses to take the oath, the other's claim is accepted. If one party produces evidence, it is accepted. If both produce evidence, the lessor's evidence prevails for rent (as it increases the rent) and the lessee's evidence prevails for benefit (as it increases the duration).
Evidence is preferred if it aligns with the party who would normally have the burden of proof.
4
Analyze the proof via qiyas
The ruling is derived by analogy to a sale before possession (qiyas jali). Just as in a sale, each party claims against the other before the subject matter is possessed, so too in ijarah before the benefit is possessed, the same procedure applies. The common effective cause (illa) is the mutual denial of claims regarding the countervalue before possession.
The proof is stated in the text: 'because ijarah before possession of the benefit is like a sale before possession of the sold item'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اختلفا في بدل الإجارة، أو المنفعة قبل قبضها تحالفا وترادًا، وحلف المستأجر أولاً إن اختلفا في الأجرة، والمؤجّرُ إن اختلفا في المنفعة، وأي نكل ثبت قول صاحبه، وأي بَرْهَنَ قُبل، وإِن بَرْهَنا فحجَّةُ المؤجر أولى إن اختلفا في الأجرة، وحجَّةُ المستأجر إن اختلفا في المنفعة) ; لأنَّ حجّة المؤجر تُثبت زيادة الأجرة، وحجة المستأجر تثبت المنفعة، والحجج للإثبات بائعه بحكم الإقالة، فلو لم يكونا مقبوضين أو أحدهما فلا يعودُ البيع، والقول قول منكر الزيادة مع يمينه، وإن ردَّ المشتري المبيع إلى بائعه بحكم الإقالة لا تحالف عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف . خلافاً لمحمد ه ; لأنه يرى النص معلولاً بعد القبض أيضاً ; لوجود الإنكار من كل واحدٍ من المتبايعين لما يدعيه الآخر، وهذه العلة لا تتفاوت بين كون المبيع مقبوضاً أو غير مقبوض ، ولما كان النص عنده معلولاً تعدى حكمه من البيع إلى الإقالة، وإن كان بعد قبض البائع المبيع بعد الإقالة. وهما قالا : كان ينبغي أن لا تحالف مطلقاً ; لأنه إنما ثبت في المبيع المطلق بالسنة ، والإقالة فسخ في حقهما إلا أنه قبل القبض على وفق القياس، فوجب القياس كما قسنا الإجارة على البيع قبل القبض، والوارث على العاقد، والقيمة على العين فيما إذا استهلكه في يد البائع غير المشتري.

[١] قوله : ولو اختلفا في بدل الإجارة ... الخ ; تقرير المسألة : إنَّ المؤجر والمستأجر لو اختلفا في قدر الأجرة بأن قال المستأجرُ : درهم ، وقال المؤجر : درهمان، أو المنفعة، بأن ادعى المؤجر أنه أجْرَه شهرا ، وادَّعى المستأجر أنه استأجره .شهرين وهذا الاختلاف يقع قبل استيفاء المعقود عليه، تحالفا وترادًا ; لأنَّ الإجارة قبل قبض المنفعة كالبيع قبل قبض المبيع، في كون كل من المتعاقدين يدعي على الآخر وهو
And if they differ about the rent or the benefit before taking possession, they take mutual oaths and rescind, and the lessee swears first if they differ about the rent, and the lessor if they differ about the benefit. And if either refuses, the word of his opponent is established; and if either produces evidence, it is accepted; and if both produce evidence, the evidence of the lessor is preferred if they differ about the rent, and the evidence of the lessee if they differ about the benefit; because the evidence of the lessor establishes an increase in rent, and the evidence of the lessee establishes the benefit, and evidence is for proving... [Explanation] The summary of the issue: The lessor and lessee, if they differ about the amount of rent—the lessee saying 'one dirham' and the lessor saying 'two dirhams'—or about the benefit—the lessor claiming he rented for one month, the lessee claiming two months—and this difference occurs before enjoyment of the subject matter, they take mutual oaths and rescind, because ijarah before possession of the benefit is like a sale before possession of the sold item, in that each of the two parties claims against the other...
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage deals with disputes in an ijarah (lease) contract regarding the amount of rent or the duration of the benefit, provided the dispute occurs before the lessee has taken possession or started using the benefit. The ruling is that both parties take mutual oaths (tahalluf) and the contract is rescinded (taradd). The order of oaths depends on the subject of dispute: if the dispute is about the rent, the lessee (musta'jir) swears first; if about the benefit (period), the lessor (mu'jir) swears first. If either party refuses to take the oath, the other's claim is accepted. If one party presents evidence, it is accepted. If both present evidence, the evidence of the lessor is given precedence regarding the rent (because his evidence aims to increase the rent, which is more onerous) and the evidence of the lessee regarding the benefit (because his evidence claims a longer benefit period, which is more for him). The commentary explains that ijarah before possession of the benefit is analogous (qiyas) to a sale before possession of the sold item, thus the same rules of mutual oaths apply. The text also repeats the earlier discussion about sale iqalah, but here it is used as a proof for the ijarah ruling, confirming the analogy.

Key Terms
إجارة (ijarah): A lease contract for the use of a benefit (e.g., property, services) in exchange for rent.
بدل الإجارة (badal al-ijarah): The rent or payment due under an ijarah contract.
المنفعة (al-manfa'ah): The benefit or usufruct that is the subject of the ijarah, e.g., residence in a house or service of a worker.
التحالف (al-tahalluf): Mutual oaths taken by both parties when they dispute a contractual term and neither has evidence; each swears to their own claim and then the contract is rescinded.
التراد (al-taradd): Rescission of the contract; both parties restore what they have received (if any) and cancel the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute over the rent amount in an ijarah contract before possession of the benefit, who swears first?
A) The lessor swears first.
B) The lessee swears first.
C) Both swear simultaneously.
D) The one who initiated the dispute swears first.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a dispute over rent or benefit in ijarah before possession is resolved by mutual oaths and rescission, with specific order and evidence precedence, based on analogy to sale.

Tahluf in Ijarah Before Qabd: Ruling and Evidence Priorities
Hanafi ruling on tahluf in ijarah before qabd with evidence priorities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mutual oaths in ijarah before possession and apply the priority rules for oaths and evidence.

Core Idea
Before possession, mutual oaths are wajib; the lessee swears first on rent, the lessor on benefit.

This passage from Al-Hidayah explains the procedure when the lessor and lessee dispute the amount of rent or the duration of benefit before any part of the benefit has been utilized. The ruling establishes mutual oaths (tahluf) and rescission, with clear priorities for who swears first and whose evidence prevails. It also covers disputes after full or partial utilization.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute scenario
Determine whether the parties differ on the rent amount or the benefit duration. This decides the sequence of oaths and evidence preference.
If both are disputed, each party's evidence is accepted for their respective claim.
2
Apply the oath sequence rule
If dispute is over rent: lessee swears first (denier of increase). If over benefit: lessor swears first (denier of increase).
If one refuses (nukul), the other's claim is established.
3
Determine evidence priority
If only one party brings evidence, it is accepted. If both bring evidence, the lessor's evidence is preferred in rent disputes (proves increase), the lessee's in benefit disputes (proves extra duration).
This is because evidence that establishes more (increase) is stronger.
4
Consider the timing of the dispute
If dispute arises after full utilization of benefit: no tahluf, lessee's word accepted. If after partial utilization: tahluf applies to the remainder, and lessee's word prevails for the past period.

Source Text

كتاب الدعوى/باب التحالف

ولو اختلفا في بدل الإجارة، أو المنفعة قبل قبضها تحالفا وترادًا، وحلف المستأجر أولاً إن اختلفا في الأجرة، والمؤجر إن اختلفا في المنفعة، وأي نكل ثبت قولُ صاحبه، وأي بَرْهَنَ قُبل، وإن بَرْهَنا فحجَّةُ المؤجر أولى إن اختلفا في الأجرة، وحجَّةُ المستأجر إن اختلفا في المنفعة

فإنَّهما إذا تحالفا تنفسخُ الإقالة، ويعود البيع، وذا غير ممتنع.

(ولو اختلفا في بدل الإجارة، أو المنفعة قبل قبضها تحالفا وترادًا، وحلف المستأجر أولاً إن اختلفا في الأجرة، والمؤجّرُ إن اختلفا في المنفعة، وأي نكل ثبت قول صاحبه، وأي بَرْهَنَ قُبل، وإِن بَرْهَنا فحجَّةُ المؤجر أولى إن اختلفا في الأجرة، وحجَّةُ المستأجر إن اختلفا في المنفعة)؛ لأنَّ حجّة المؤجر تُثبت زيادة الأجرة، وحجة المستأجر تثبت المنفعة، والحجج للإثبات بائعه بحكم الإقالة، فلو لم يكونا مقبوضين أو أحدهما فلا يعودُ البيع، والقول قول منكر الزيادة مع يمينه، وإن ردَّ المشتري المبيع إلى بائعه بحكم الإقالة لا تحالف عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف. خلافاً لمحمد؛ لأنه يرى النص معلولاً بعد القبض أيضاً؛ لوجود الإنكار من كل واحدٍ من المتبايعين لما يدعيه الآخر، وهذه العلة لا تتفاوت بين كون المبيع مقبوضاً أو غير مقبوض، ولما كان النص عنده معلولاً تعدى حكمه من البيع إلى الإقالة، وإن كان بعد قبض البائع المبيع بعد الإقالة.

وهما قالا: كان ينبغي أن لا تحالف مطلقاً؛ لأنه إنما ثبت في المبيع المطلق بالسنة، والإقالة فسخ في حقهما إلا أنه قبل القبض على وفق القياس، فوجب القياس كما قسنا الإجارة على البيع قبل القبض، والوارث على العاقد، والقيمة على العين فيما إذا استهلكه في يد البائع غير المشتري.

[١] قوله: ولو اختلفا في بدل الإجارة... الخ؛ تقرير المسألة: إنَّ المؤجر والمستأجر لو اختلفا في قدر الأجرة بأن قال المستأجر: درهم، وقال المؤجر: درهمان، أو المنفعة، بأن ادعى المؤجر أنه أجره شهرا، وادَّعى المستأجر أنه استأجره شهرين

وهذا الاختلاف يقع قبل استيفاء المعقود عليه، تحالفا وترادًا؛ لأنَّ الإجارة قبل قبض المنفعة كالبيع قبل قبض المبيع، في كون كل من المتعاقدين يدعي على الآخر وهو ينكر، وكون كل من العقدين معاوضة يجري فيها الفسخ، فالتحقت به، وأقيمت الدار مثلاً مقام المنفعة في حق إيراد العقد عليها، فكأنها قائمة تقديراً، فلا يرد أنَّ قيام المعقود عليه شرط، والمنفعة معدومة، فينبغي أن لا يجري فيها التحالف.

فإن وقع الاختلاف في الأجرة حلف المستأجر أولاً؛ لأنه منكر بوجوب زيادة الأجرة، وإن وقع الاختلافُ في المنفعة حلف المؤجر أوَّلاً؛ لكونه منكراً لوجوب زيادة المنفعة، وأيهما نكل لزمه دعوى صاحبه كما هو مقتضى النكول، وأيهما أقام البينة قبلت بينته، وإن أقاما البيئة فبيّنةُ المؤجر أولى بالقبول؛ لكونها أكثر إثباتاً.

وهذا إذا كان الاختلاف في الأجرة، وإن كان في المنفعة فبينة المستأجر أولى بالقبول، وإن كان الاختلاف في الأجرة والمنفعة كليهما فبيَّنة كل من المؤجر والمستأجر قبلت فيما يدعيه من الفضل.

كما إذا ادعى المؤجر أن مدتها سنةً بمئتين، وادَّعى المستأجر أنَّ مدتها سنتان بمئة، تقضى بمئة للمؤجر، وسنتين للمستأجر؛ نظراً إلى كثرة الإثبات. وإن اختلفا بعد استيفاء المنفعة لم يتحالفا اتفاقاً، والقولُ للمستأجر مع يمينه؛ لأنه منكر الزيادة، وإن اختلفا بعد استيفاء بعض المنفعة [تحالفا وفسخ العقد] فيما بقي اعتباراً للبعض بالكل، والقولُ يكون للمستأجر فيما مضى؛ لأنَّ القول يكون للمنكر.

[١] قوله: وهذا ظاهر... الخ؛ يعني أنَّ عدم التحالف عند الشيخين ظاهر؛ لأنَّ...
Book of Claims / Chapter of Mutual Oaths. If they differ regarding the rent or the benefit before its possession, they take mutual oaths and return (the consideration). The lessee takes the oath first if they differ about the rent, and the lessor if they differ about the benefit. If either refuses, the statement of the other is established. If either produces evidence, it is accepted. If both produce evidence, the evidence of the lessor is preferred if they differ about the rent, and the evidence of the lessee if they differ about the benefit. If they take mutual oaths, the rescission is dissolved and the sale returns, and that is not impossible. (If they differ regarding the rent... repeated) because the evidence of the lessor establishes an increase in rent, and the evidence of the lessee establishes the benefit, and evidence is for proof. The seller by virtue of rescission: if both or one have not taken possession, the sale does not return. The statement of the denier of the increase is accepted with his oath. If the buyer returns the sold item to its seller by virtue of rescission, there is no mutual oath according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad, because he considers the text as having a cause after possession as well, due to the denial by each of the two parties of what the other claims, and this cause does not differ between the sold item being possessed or not. Since the text in his view has a cause, its ruling extends from sale to rescission, even if after the seller's possession of the sold item after rescission. The two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) said: It should be that there is no mutual oath at all, because it is established only in an absolute sale by the Sunnah, and rescission is a cancellation in their view, except that before possession it is in accordance with analogy. So analogy is necessary, just as we analogized hire to sale before possession, and the heir to the contractor, and the value to the thing when it is consumed in the seller's hand by someone other than the buyer. [1] His statement: 'If they differ regarding the rent...' etc.; the explanation of the issue: The lessor and lessee if they differ about the amount of rent, such as the lessee saying 'one dirham' and the lessor saying 'two dirhams', or about the benefit, such as the lessor claiming that he rented for one month and the lessee claiming that he rented for two months. This difference occurs before the utilization of the object of contract; they take mutual oaths and return, because hire before possession of the benefit is like sale before possession of the sold item, in that each contractor claims against the other while the other denies, and each of the two contracts is a commutative contract in which cancellation occurs, so it joined it. The house, for example, is placed in the position of the benefit regarding the application of the contract to it, so it is as if it exists in estimation. So it cannot be objected that the existence of the object of contract is a condition, and the benefit is non-existent, so mutual oaths should not apply. If the difference occurs about the rent, the lessee takes the oath first, because he denies the obligation of an increase in rent. If the difference occurs about the benefit, the lessor takes the oath first, because he denies the obligation of an increase in benefit. Whichever refuses, the claim of the other is binding on him, as required by refusal. Whichever produces evidence, his evidence is accepted. If both produce evidence, the evidence of the lessor is preferred for acceptance, because it is more probative. This is if the difference is about the rent. If it is about the benefit, the evidence of the lessee is preferred for acceptance. If the difference is about both the rent and the benefit, the evidence of each of the lessor and lessee is accepted regarding what he claims of the excess. For example, if the lessor claims that its term is one year for two hundred, and the lessee claims that its term is two years for one hundred, the judgment is for one hundred for the lessor and two years for the lessee, considering greater probativeness. If they differ after utilization of the benefit, they do not take mutual oaths by agreement, and the statement of the lessee is accepted with his oath, because he is the denier of the increase. If they differ after utilization of part of the benefit, they take mutual oaths and the contract is annulled regarding the remainder, considering the part as the whole, and the statement of the lessee is accepted regarding the past, because the statement of the denier is accepted. [1] His statement: 'And this is apparent...' etc.; meaning that the lack of mutual oaths according to the two shaykhs is apparent, because...
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on mutual oaths (tahluf) in the context of ijarah (hire) contracts. It explains the Hanafi ruling when the lessor and lessee disagree about the amount of rent or the duration of the benefit before the benefit has been taken possession of. The source text is Al-Hidayah, and the commentary expands on it. The core ruling: if they dispute before the benefit is used, each party denies the other's claim, so they take mutual oaths (yamin) and the contract is rescinded. The lessee swears first if the dispute is about the rent (he denies owing more), and the lessor swears first if about the benefit (he denies providing more). If one refuses to swear, the other's claim is accepted. If one presents evidence, it is accepted; if both evidence, the lessor's is preferred for rent disputes (proves increase), the lessee's for benefit disputes (proves extra duration). This is based on analogy to sale before possession. The text then discusses the application of these rules to iqalah (rescission of a sale), where Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that no tahluf occurs in iqalah after possession, unlike Muhammad who extends it. The commentary clarifies that iqalah after possession is not analogous to the original sale before possession. Finally, it covers disputes after full or partial utilization of the benefit: after full use, no tahluf and the lessee's word is taken; after partial use, tahluf applies to the remaining period and the lessee's word prevails for the past use. The passage is dense and requires careful parsing of the conditions and priorities.

Key Terms
تحالف (tahāluf): Mutual oaths taken by both parties in a contract when they dispute a claim, each swearing to their own version.
إقالة (iqālah): Rescission of a sale contract by mutual agreement; cancellation.
قبض (qabḍ): Taking possession; in ijarah, possession of the benefit (by using it) or of the object if applicable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In an ijarah contract dispute before possession, both parties bring evidence. If the dispute is about the benefit, whose evidence is preferred?
A) The lessor's evidence
B) The lessee's evidence
C) Both are equally accepted
D) The judge chooses randomly

Key Takeaway
Before possession, tahluf is wajib with clear sequences and evidence priorities; the key is identifying who denies the increase.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Tahluf in Iqalah After Possession
Intra-Hanafi dispute on applying tahluf to iqalah after possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf reject tahluf in iqalah after possession and evaluate Muhammad's opposing argument.

Core Idea
Tahluf in iqalah after possession is not wajib according to the two shaykhs, because iqalah is a cancellation, not a sale.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: whether mutual oaths apply when a rescission of sale (iqalah) occurs after the buyer has taken possession. The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) say no, while Imam Muhammad says yes. The discussion revolves around the cause (illa) of tahluf and the scope of the Sunnah. Understanding this dispute is crucial for correctly applying tahluf rules in post-possession cancellations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the point of disagreement
The dispute is about applying tahluf to iqalah after the sold item has been taken possession of.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
2
State the position of the two shaykhs and their proof
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: no tahluf in iqalah after possession. Their proof: the Sunnah established tahluf only in an absolute sale before possession. Iqalah is a cancellation, not a sale, and after possession the analogy breaks down.
They argue that the Sunnah is specific and cannot be extended.
3
State Muhammad's position and his proof
Muhammad: tahluf applies because the cause (illa) of denial exists equally before and after possession. He argues that the text (Sunnah) is mu'allal (has a cause), so it extends.
This is based on ta'lil (ratio legis).
4
Analyze the Hanafi response and tarjih
The two shaykhs restrict the Sunnah to its specific context. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: no tahluf in iqalah after possession.
Al-Marghinani adopts this view in Al-Hidayah.

Source Text

كتاب الدعوى/باب التحالف

ولو اختلفا في بدل الإجارة، أو المنفعة قبل قبضها تحالفا وترادًا، وحلف المستأجر أولاً إن اختلفا في الأجرة، والمؤجر إن اختلفا في المنفعة، وأي نكل ثبت قولُ صاحبه، وأي بَرْهَنَ قُبل، وإن بَرْهَنا فحجَّةُ المؤجر أولى إن اختلفا في الأجرة، وحجَّةُ المستأجر إن اختلفا في المنفعة

فإنَّهما إذا تحالفا تنفسخُ الإقالة، ويعود البيع، وذا غير ممتنع.

(ولو اختلفا في بدل الإجارة، أو المنفعة قبل قبضها تحالفا وترادًا، وحلف المستأجر أولاً إن اختلفا في الأجرة، والمؤجّرُ إن اختلفا في المنفعة، وأي نكل ثبت قول صاحبه، وأي بَرْهَنَ قُبل، وإِن بَرْهَنا فحجَّةُ المؤجر أولى إن اختلفا في الأجرة، وحجَّةُ المستأجر إن اختلفا في المنفعة)؛ لأنَّ حجّة المؤجر تُثبت زيادة الأجرة، وحجة المستأجر تثبت المنفعة، والحجج للإثبات بائعه بحكم الإقالة، فلو لم يكونا مقبوضين أو أحدهما فلا يعودُ البيع، والقول قول منكر الزيادة مع يمينه، وإن ردَّ المشتري المبيع إلى بائعه بحكم الإقالة لا تحالف عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف. خلافاً لمحمد؛ لأنه يرى النص معلولاً بعد القبض أيضاً؛ لوجود الإنكار من كل واحدٍ من المتبايعين لما يدعيه الآخر، وهذه العلة لا تتفاوت بين كون المبيع مقبوضاً أو غير مقبوض، ولما كان النص عنده معلولاً تعدى حكمه من البيع إلى الإقالة، وإن كان بعد قبض البائع المبيع بعد الإقالة.

وهما قالا: كان ينبغي أن لا تحالف مطلقاً؛ لأنه إنما ثبت في المبيع المطلق بالسنة، والإقالة فسخ في حقهما إلا أنه قبل القبض على وفق القياس، فوجب القياس كما قسنا الإجارة على البيع قبل القبض، والوارث على العاقد، والقيمة على العين فيما إذا استهلكه في يد البائع غير المشتري.

[١] قوله: ولو اختلفا في بدل الإجارة... الخ؛ تقرير المسألة: إنَّ المؤجر والمستأجر لو اختلفا في قدر الأجرة بأن قال المستأجر: درهم، وقال المؤجر: درهمان، أو المنفعة، بأن ادعى المؤجر أنه أجره شهرا، وادَّعى المستأجر أنه استأجره شهرين

وهذا الاختلاف يقع قبل استيفاء المعقود عليه، تحالفا وترادًا؛ لأنَّ الإجارة قبل قبض المنفعة كالبيع قبل قبض المبيع، في كون كل من المتعاقدين يدعي على الآخر وهو ينكر، وكون كل من العقدين معاوضة يجري فيها الفسخ، فالتحقت به، وأقيمت الدار مثلاً مقام المنفعة في حق إيراد العقد عليها، فكأنها قائمة تقديراً، فلا يرد أنَّ قيام المعقود عليه شرط، والمنفعة معدومة، فينبغي أن لا يجري فيها التحالف.

فإن وقع الاختلاف في الأجرة حلف المستأجر أولاً؛ لأنه منكر بوجوب زيادة الأجرة، وإن وقع الاختلافُ في المنفعة حلف المؤجر أوَّلاً؛ لكونه منكراً لوجوب زيادة المنفعة، وأيهما نكل لزمه دعوى صاحبه كما هو مقتضى النكول، وأيهما أقام البينة قبلت بينته، وإن أقاما البيئة فبيّنةُ المؤجر أولى بالقبول؛ لكونها أكثر إثباتاً.

وهذا إذا كان الاختلاف في الأجرة، وإن كان في المنفعة فبينة المستأجر أولى بالقبول، وإن كان الاختلاف في الأجرة والمنفعة كليهما فبيَّنة كل من المؤجر والمستأجر قبلت فيما يدعيه من الفضل.

كما إذا ادعى المؤجر أن مدتها سنةً بمئتين، وادَّعى المستأجر أنَّ مدتها سنتان بمئة، تقضى بمئة للمؤجر، وسنتين للمستأجر؛ نظراً إلى كثرة الإثبات. وإن اختلفا بعد استيفاء المنفعة لم يتحالفا اتفاقاً، والقولُ للمستأجر مع يمينه؛ لأنه منكر الزيادة، وإن اختلفا بعد استيفاء بعض المنفعة [تحالفا وفسخ العقد] فيما بقي اعتباراً للبعض بالكل، والقولُ يكون للمستأجر فيما مضى؛ لأنَّ القول يكون للمنكر.

[١] قوله: وهذا ظاهر... الخ؛ يعني أنَّ عدم التحالف عند الشيخين ظاهر؛ لأنَّ...
Book of Claims / Chapter of Mutual Oaths. If they differ regarding the rent or the benefit before its possession, they take mutual oaths and return (the consideration). The lessee takes the oath first if they differ about the rent, and the lessor if they differ about the benefit. If either refuses, the statement of the other is established. If either produces evidence, it is accepted. If both produce evidence, the evidence of the lessor is preferred if they differ about the rent, and the evidence of the lessee if they differ about the benefit. If they take mutual oaths, the rescission is dissolved and the sale returns, and that is not impossible. (If they differ regarding the rent... repeated) because the evidence of the lessor establishes an increase in rent, and the evidence of the lessee establishes the benefit, and evidence is for proof. The seller by virtue of rescission: if both or one have not taken possession, the sale does not return. The statement of the denier of the increase is accepted with his oath. If the buyer returns the sold item to its seller by virtue of rescission, there is no mutual oath according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad, because he considers the text as having a cause after possession as well, due to the denial by each of the two parties of what the other claims, and this cause does not differ between the sold item being possessed or not. Since the text in his view has a cause, its ruling extends from sale to rescission, even if after the seller's possession of the sold item after rescission. The two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) said: It should be that there is no mutual oath at all, because it is established only in an absolute sale by the Sunnah, and rescission is a cancellation in their view, except that before possession it is in accordance with analogy. So analogy is necessary, just as we analogized hire to sale before possession, and the heir to the contractor, and the value to the thing when it is consumed in the seller's hand by someone other than the buyer. [1] His statement: 'If they differ regarding the rent...' etc.; the explanation of the issue: The lessor and lessee if they differ about the amount of rent, such as the lessee saying 'one dirham' and the lessor saying 'two dirhams', or about the benefit, such as the lessor claiming that he rented for one month and the lessee claiming that he rented for two months. This difference occurs before the utilization of the object of contract; they take mutual oaths and return, because hire before possession of the benefit is like sale before possession of the sold item, in that each contractor claims against the other while the other denies, and each of the two contracts is a commutative contract in which cancellation occurs, so it joined it. The house, for example, is placed in the position of the benefit regarding the application of the contract to it, so it is as if it exists in estimation. So it cannot be objected that the existence of the object of contract is a condition, and the benefit is non-existent, so mutual oaths should not apply. If the difference occurs about the rent, the lessee takes the oath first, because he denies the obligation of an increase in rent. If the difference occurs about the benefit, the lessor takes the oath first, because he denies the obligation of an increase in benefit. Whichever refuses, the claim of the other is binding on him, as required by refusal. Whichever produces evidence, his evidence is accepted. If both produce evidence, the evidence of the lessor is preferred for acceptance, because it is more probative. This is if the difference is about the rent. If it is about the benefit, the evidence of the lessee is preferred for acceptance. If the difference is about both the rent and the benefit, the evidence of each of the lessor and lessee is accepted regarding what he claims of the excess. For example, if the lessor claims that its term is one year for two hundred, and the lessee claims that its term is two years for one hundred, the judgment is for one hundred for the lessor and two years for the lessee, considering greater probativeness. If they differ after utilization of the benefit, they do not take mutual oaths by agreement, and the statement of the lessee is accepted with his oath, because he is the denier of the increase. If they differ after utilization of part of the benefit, they take mutual oaths and the contract is annulled regarding the remainder, considering the part as the whole, and the statement of the lessee is accepted regarding the past, because the statement of the denier is accepted. [1] His statement: 'And this is apparent...' etc.; meaning that the lack of mutual oaths according to the two shaykhs is apparent, because...
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on mutual oaths (tahluf) in the context of ijarah (hire) contracts. It explains the Hanafi ruling when the lessor and lessee disagree about the amount of rent or the duration of the benefit before the benefit has been taken possession of. The source text is Al-Hidayah, and the commentary expands on it. The core ruling: if they dispute before the benefit is used, each party denies the other's claim, so they take mutual oaths (yamin) and the contract is rescinded. The lessee swears first if the dispute is about the rent (he denies owing more), and the lessor swears first if about the benefit (he denies providing more). If one refuses to swear, the other's claim is accepted. If one presents evidence, it is accepted; if both evidence, the lessor's is preferred for rent disputes (proves increase), the lessee's for benefit disputes (proves extra duration). This is based on analogy to sale before possession. The text then discusses the application of these rules to iqalah (rescission of a sale), where Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that no tahluf occurs in iqalah after possession, unlike Muhammad who extends it. The commentary clarifies that iqalah after possession is not analogous to the original sale before possession. Finally, it covers disputes after full or partial utilization of the benefit: after full use, no tahluf and the lessee's word is taken; after partial use, tahluf applies to the remaining period and the lessee's word prevails for the past use. The passage is dense and requires careful parsing of the conditions and priorities.

Key Terms
إقالة (iqālah): Rescission of a sale contract by mutual agreement; cancellation.
علة (illah): The effective cause or ratio legis that connects a ruling to its subject.
قبض (qabḍ): Taking possession; in sale, possession of the sold item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position regarding tahluf in iqalah after the sold item has been taken possession of?
A) Tahluf is wajib
B) Tahluf is not wajib
C) Tahluf is recommended (sunnah)
D) The matter is undetermined

Key Takeaway
In iqalah after possession, the mufta bihi is no tahluf; the ruling is based on the Sunnah's specific application to absolute sale before possession.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
8 min
Mutual Oath in Ijarah After Benefit Receipt
Expansion of mutual oath ruling in ijarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules for mutual oath (tahāluf) in ijarah disputes after benefit receipt, distinguish between full and partial receipt, and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement on the analogy to sale.

Core Idea
After full benefit, no mutual oath; lessee's word. After partial, mutual oath and rescission of remainder.

When a dispute arises over the rent or duration of a hire (ijarah) after the lessee has used the benefit, the Hanafi school has specific rules for mutual oath-taking. This lesson explores the core ruling, the procedure for oath-taking, and the critical difference of opinion between Imam Muhammad and the two elders (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) regarding the applicability of mutual oath after partial utilization.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute scenarios
Note the two scenarios fully addressed: dispute after full receipt of benefit and after partial receipt. Also note disputes over rent vs. benefit.
2
Extract the base ruling for full receipt
The text states that after full receipt, there is no mutual oath; the lessee's statement with oath is accepted because he denies the claim of additional rent.
This is agreed upon by all Hanafi imams.
3
Examine the partial receipt scenario
If only part of the benefit has been received, mutual oath is required for the remaining period and the contract is rescinded for the future, while the lessee's word holds for the past.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
4
Analyze Imam Muhammad's objection
Imam Muhammad argues that no mutual oath is possible after partial receipt because benefits have no independent value. In sale, a perished item is replaced by its value; here, rescission leaves nothing to base the oath on.
This is the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf central to the passage.
5
Understand the analogy to sale
The text compares ijarah to sale but highlights that benefit is a contingent thing ('arad) that does not last, so the analogy is not perfect. The chosen view treats each hour of benefit as a separate subject matter.
This explains why partial receipt allows partial rescission.
6
Apply the procedure for oath-taking
Who swears first depends on the subject of dispute: if rent, lessee swears first (denier); if benefit, lessor swears first. Evidence rules are given.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحجة كل في فضل يدعيه أولى إن اختلفا فيهما، ولا تحالف إن اختلفا بعد قبض المنفعة، والقول للمستأجر

وحجة كل في فضل يدعيه أولى إن اختلفا فيهما، كما إذا قال المؤجر: أجرت إلى سنة بمئتين، وقال المستأخر: لا بل أجرت إلى سنتين بمئة، وأقاما البينة تثبت في سنتين بمئتين.

ولا تحالف إن اختلفا بعد قبض المنفعة، والقول للمستأجر: أي إن اختلفا في قدر الأجرة بعد قبض المنفعة، فلا تحالف عليهما، والقول للمستأجر؛ لأنه منكر للزيادة، وهذا ظاهر عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف له ينكر، وكون كل من العقدين معاوضة يجري فيها الفسخ، فالتحقت به، وأقيمت الدار مثلا مقام المنفعة في حق إيراد العقد عليها، فكأنها قائمة تقديرا، فلا يرد أن قيام المعقود عليه شرط، والمنفعة معدومة، فينبغي أن لا يجري فيها التحالف.

فإن وقع الاختلاف في الأجرة حلف المستأجر أولا؛ لأنه منكر بوجوب زيادة الأجرة، وإن وقع الاختلاف في المنفعة حلف المؤجر أولا؛ لكونه منكرا لوجوب زيادة المنفعة، وأيهما نكل لزمه دعوى صاحبه كما هو مقتضى النكول، وأيهما أقام البينة قبلت بينته، وإن أقاما البينة فبينة المؤجر أولى بالقبول؛ لكونها أكثر إثباتا.

وهذا إذا كان الاختلاف في الأجرة، وإن كان في المنفعة فبينة المستأجر أولى بالقبول، وإن كان الاختلاف في الأجرة والمنفعة كليهما فبينة كل من المؤجر والمستأجر قبلت فيما يدعيه من الفضل.

كما إذا ادعى المؤجر أن مدتها سنة بمئتين، وادعى المستأجر أن مدتها سنتان بمئة، تقضى بمئة للمؤجر، وسنتين للمستأجر؛ نظرا إلى كثرة الإثبات. وإن اختلفا بعد استيفاء المنفعة لم يتحالفا اتفاقا، والقول للمستأجر مع يمينه؛ لأنه منكر الزيادة، وإن اختلفا بعد استيفاء بعض المنفعة تحالفا وفسخ العقد فيما بقي اعتبارا للبعض بالكل، والقول يكون للمستأجر فيما مضى؛ لأن القول يكون للمنكر.

وبعد قبض بعضها تحالفا، وفسخت فيما بقي، والقول للمستأجر فيما مضى؛ لأن التحالف بعد قبض المبيع على خلاف القياس؛ فلا تقاس الإجارة على البيع، فإن التحالف في الإجارة يثبت قياسا على البيع، وأما عند محمد له فإن البيع ينفسخ بقيمة الهالك، وهاهنا ليس للمنافع قيمة.

وبعد قبض بعضها تحالفا، وفسخت فيما بقي، والقول للمستأجر فيما مضى; التحالف بعد قبض المبيع على خلاف القياس فلا تقاس الإجارة هاهنا عليه إذ هلاك المعقود عليه بالاستيفاء يمنع التحالف، والمعقود عليه هاهنا عرض، وهو المنفعة، والعرض لا يبقى زمانين، بخلاف ما في صورة المقيس، حيث وجد المعقود عليه. وكذا على أصل محمد؛ لأن الهلاك إنما لا يمنع عنده في المبيع لما أن له قيمة تقوم مقامه فيتحالفان عليها، ولو جرى التحالف هاهنا وفسخ عقد الإجارة فلا قيمة؛ لأن المنافع لا تتقوم بنفسها بل بالعقد، وبالفسخ يرتفع العقد.

فتبين أنه لا عقد، فحينئذ ظهر أنه لا قيمة للمنفعة، وإذا كان كذلك كان البيع غير قائم، ولا الذي يقوم مقامه فامتنع التحالف، فالقول للمستأجر مع يمينه؛ لأنه هو المستحق عليه، ومتى وقع الاختلاف في الاستحقاق كان القول قول المستحق. صرح به في «الكافي»، وغيره.

وبعد قبض بعضها.... الخ؛ يعني لو اختلفا بعد استيفاء بعض المنفعة تحالفا فيما بقي اعتبارا للبعض بالكل، وتفسخ الإجارة فيما بقي من المنافع، لإمكان الفسخ، وهذا لا ينافي ما مر أن هلاك بعض المعقود عليه يمنع التحالف عند الإمام؛ لأن الإجارة تنعقد ساعة فساعة، على حدوث المنفعة، فكان كل جزء من المنفعة بمنزلة معقود عليه فيما بقي من المنفعة، كمعقود عليه غير مقبوض، فتحالفا في حقه. بخلاف ما إذا هلك بعض المبيع؛ لأنه بجميع أجزائه معقود بعقد واحد، فإذا تعذر الفسخ في بعضه بالهلاك، تعذر في كله ضرورة. والقول للمستأجر مع اليمين فيما مضى؛ لأنه منكر بما يدعيه المؤجر من زيادة الأجرة.
And the evidence of each concerning the excess he claims is given precedence if they differ about both. And there is no mutual oath if they differ after receipt of the benefit, and the lessee's statement is accepted.

And the evidence of each concerning the excess he claims is given precedence if they differ about both, as when the lessor says: I leased for one year for two hundred, and the lessee says: No, you leased for two years for one hundred, and they both produce evidence proving two years for two hundred.

And there is no mutual oath if they differ after receipt of the benefit, and the lessee's statement is accepted: i.e., if they differ about the amount of the rent after receipt of the benefit, there is no mutual oath upon them, and the lessee's statement is accepted because he is the denier of the increase. This is apparent according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, that he denies, and each of the two contracts is compensatory and entails rescission, so it is attached to it. The house, for example, is treated as standing in the place of the benefit with respect to the conclusion of the contract upon it, so it is as if it is extant hypothetically. Thus it cannot be objected that the existence of the subject matter is a condition, and the benefit is nonexistent, so mutual oath should not occur in it.

If the dispute occurs about the rent, the lessee takes the oath first because he is the denier of the obligation of additional rent. If the dispute occurs about the benefit, the lessor takes the oath first because he is the denier of the obligation of additional benefit. Whichever of them refuses (to take the oath), the claim of his opponent is binding upon him, as is the consequence of refusal. Whichever of them produces evidence, his evidence is accepted. If both produce evidence, the lessor's evidence is more worthy of acceptance because it establishes more.

This is when the dispute is about the rent. If it is about the benefit, then the lessee's evidence is more worthy of acceptance. If the dispute is about both the rent and the benefit, then the evidence of each of the lessor and lessee is accepted regarding the excess he claims.

As when the lessor claims that its term was one year for two hundred, and the lessee claims that its term was two years for one hundred, a judgment is given for one hundred for the lessor and two years for the lessee, considering the greater establishment. If they differ after the complete utilization of the benefit, they do not take mutual oaths by agreement, and the lessee's statement with his oath is accepted because he is the denier of the increase. If they differ after utilization of part of the benefit, they take mutual oaths and the contract is rescinded regarding the remaining part by considering the part as analogous to the whole, and the lessee's statement is accepted concerning the past period because the statement of the denier is accepted.

And after receipt of part of it, they take mutual oaths, and the contract is rescinded regarding the remaining part, and the lessee's statement is accepted concerning the past period because mutual oath after receipt of the sold item is contrary to analogy; therefore ijarah is not analogized to sale, for mutual oath in ijarah is established by analogy to sale. According to Muhammad, however, the sale is rescinded with the value of the perished item, but here the benefit has no value.

And after receipt of part of it, they take mutual oaths, and the contract is rescinded regarding the remaining part, and the lessee's statement is accepted concerning the past period. Mutual oath after receipt of the sold item is contrary to analogy, so ijarah is not analogized to it here, since the destruction of the subject matter through utilization prevents mutual oath. And the subject matter here is a contingent thing, namely the benefit, and a contingent thing does not last for two instants, unlike the case of the analogized item where the subject matter exists. Similarly, according to Muhammad's principle, destruction does not prevent mutual oath in sale only because it has a value that stands in its place so they take mutual oaths concerning it. If mutual oath were to occur here and the ijarah contract were rescinded, there would be no value because benefits are not valuable in themselves but by the contract, and with rescission the contract ceases.

Thus it becomes clear that there is no contract, and then it becomes apparent that the benefit has no value. If this is so, the sale is neither existing nor has anything standing in its place, so mutual oath is prevented. Thus the lessee's statement with his oath is accepted because he is the one upon whom the entitlement is claimed, and whenever the dispute concerns entitlement, the statement of the entitled person is accepted. This was clarified in al-Kafi and elsewhere.

And after receipt of part of it... i.e., if they differ after utilization of part of the benefit, they take mutual oaths regarding the remaining part by considering the part as analogous to the whole, and the ijarah is rescinded regarding the remaining benefits because rescission is possible. This does not contradict what preceded that destruction of part of the subject matter prevents mutual oath according to Imam (Abu Hanifa), because ijarah is concluded hour by hour for the coming into existence of the benefit. Thus each portion of the benefit is like a subject matter regarding the remaining portion of the benefit, like an un received subject matter, so they take mutual oaths with respect to it. Unlike when part of the sold item perishes, because it is concluded by a single contract with all its parts. If rescission becomes impossible regarding some of it due to destruction, it becomes impossible regarding all of it necessarily. And the lessee's statement with the oath is accepted concerning the past because he is the denier of what the lessor claims of additional rent.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling on mutual oath-taking (tahāluf) in ijarah (hire) disputes. The base ruling states that when parties differ after the benefit has been fully received, there is no mutual oath; the lessee's word prevails as he denies any additional rent. The commentary explains the reasoning: the lessee is the denier, and since both contracts (sale and hire) are compensatory, the rule is extended. However, unlike sale, benefit is not a tangible thing, so it is treated as hypothetically existing. The text then details sub-scenarios: if dispute is over rent, lessee swears first; if over benefit, lessor swears first. If both produce evidence, the lessor's evidence is preferred in rent disputes as it establishes more. If dispute occurs after partial benefit, mutual oath is required for the remaining period, and the contract is rescinded prospectively, while the lessee's word holds for the past. The passage also highlights an intra-Hanafi difference: Imam Muhammad holds that mutual oath is not applicable here because in sale, a perished item is replaced by its value, but benefits have no value apart from the contract, so rescission would leave nothing to base the oath on. The commentary concludes that the lessee's statement is accepted because he is the one against whom the claim is made.

Key Terms
تحالف (tahāluf): Mutual oath-taking between litigants when both lack evidence; each swears and the case is decided.
منفعة (manfa'ah): The benefit or usufruct, which is the subject matter of ijarah.
مؤجر (mu'jir): The lessor who provides the benefit in exchange for rent.
مستأجر (musta'jir): The lessee who receives the benefit and pays rent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After the lessee has fully utilized the benefit, the lessor claims additional rent. How is the dispute resolved according to the Hanafi school?
A) They take mutual oaths, and the contract is rescinded.
B) No mutual oath; the lessee's word with his oath is accepted.
C) The lessor's claim is accepted because he is the owner.
D) The court determines a fair rent.

Key Takeaway
In ijarah disputes after benefit receipt, the key distinction is between full and partial receipt: full receipt precludes mutual oath (lessee's word), while partial receipt triggers mutual oath and prospective rescission, with an intra-Hanafi disagreement on the latter.

intermediate
8 min
Tahalf in Ijarah After Partial Benefit
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tahalf in ijarah after partial benefit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on tahalf in ijarah after partial benefit and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad regarding the effect of halk on tahalf.

Core Idea
In ijarah, each moment of benefit is a separate contract, so tahalf is valid for the remaining period even after partial use.

This lesson explores a nuanced intra-madhhab dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad regarding the application of mutual oath-taking (tahalf) in lease contracts. While the general rule in sales restricts tahalf after receipt, the unique nature of benefits in ijarah—being accidents that do not persist—leads to a different conclusion. We will unpack the reasoning behind the preferred view and its practical difference from the sale analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue and the Ruling
State the dispute scenario: lessor and lessee disagree after some rent period has passed. The ruling is that they take oaths (tahalf) for the remaining period, and the lessee's word is accepted for the past.
The ruling is explicitly given in the source: 'وبعد قبض بعضها تحالفا، وفُسِخت فيما بقي، والقول للمستأجر فيما مضى'.
2
Understand the Base Analogy with Sale
Recognize that tahalf after receipt in sale is against qiyas (analogy). The text states that ijarah is not analogized to sale in this regard, but tahalf in ijarah is itself established by qiyas to sale under certain conditions.
The default rule in sale: after receipt, tahalf is not allowed because halk (destruction) of part prevents it.
3
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Contrast the positions of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. For Abu Hanifa, halk of some benefit does not prevent tahalf for the remainder because each portion of benefit is a separate contract (saa'atan fa-saa'atan). For Muhammad, halk prevents tahalf because benefits have no independent value to substitute, unlike in sale where the price of destroyed goods can substitute.
The crux: whether the remaining benefit is treated as a separate unreceived contract (Abu Hanifa) or as part of a single contract where partial halk blocks tahalf (Muhammad).
4
Apply the Final Ruling
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) follows Abu Hanifa: for the past period, the lessee's word with his oath is accepted; for the remaining period, the parties take oaths and the lease is rescinded.
The practical outcome: the contract is split—past is settled per lessee's claim, future is rescinded via tahalf.

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the application of oath-taking (tahalf) in lease contracts (ijarah) after partial benefit has been received. The main ruling states that when the parties dispute after some rent period has passed, they take oaths regarding the remaining period, and the lease is rescinded for that future portion, while for the past period the lessee's statement is accepted with his oath. The author explains that this ruling is preserved even though at first glance it seems contrary to the rule in sales, where oath-taking after receipt is not allowed because it violates analogy. Here, lease is considered to be a contract that renews moment by moment, so each portion of benefit is like a separate contract. The commentator highlights the difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad: for Abu Hanifa, destruction of part of the subject matter prevents oath-taking in sale, but in lease, because the contract is instantaneous and the benefit is an accident that does not persist, the remaining benefit is treated as a separate contract not yet received, allowing oath-taking. For Imam Muhammad, in sale the price of the destroyed item stands in its place, so oath-taking is possible; but in lease, benefits have no independent value, so they cannot be replaced, thus oath-taking is not possible. Consequently, for the past period, the lessee's word is taken as he is the defendant, and for the remaining period, oath-taking is valid by analogy to sale. The authoritative position is that after partial benefit, the lease is rescinded for the future and the lessee's word is taken for the past.

Key Terms
تحالف (tahalf): Mutual oath-taking between two parties who dispute, each swearing to his claim, leading to rescission of the contract.
إجارة (ijarah): Lease or hire contract for benefits of a thing or services.
مستأجر (musta'jir): The lessee, the party paying rent to receive benefits.
منفعة (manfa'ah): Benefit or usufruct, the subject matter of ijarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, after partial benefit in ijarah, tahalf is valid for the remaining period and the lessee's word is taken for the past, due to the moment-by-moment renewal of the lease contract.

Qiyas vs. Istihsan: Possession in Lease
Comparing qiyas and istihsan rulings on possession in lease and deposit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply istihsan to differentiate possession in lease from possession in deposit and state the Hanafi ruling on when possession implies ownership.

Core Idea
Possession in lease is incidental; in deposit it is primary — only the latter implies ownership.

This lesson unpacks a classic Hanafi example of istihsan overriding qiyas. A person declares possession of an item known to be his, claiming it is under lease. Does his admission of possession force him to return the item? The answer depends on whether possession is necessary or intentional. Let's see how the Hanafi school reasons through this.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Disputed Case
A person holds an item (e.g., a cloth) that is known to belong to him. He admits possession but claims it is under lease. The question: Does his admission of possession imply ownership, requiring return?
The item is known to be his (المقر) — this is crucial.
2
Examine the Qiyas (Strict Analogy)
Qiyas treats this like deposit or loan: since he admitted possession and possession implies ownership, his subsequent claim of lease is contradictory. Hence, his admission prevails, and he must return the item.
Analogy with wadīʿah and qard.
3
Examine the Istihsan (Juristic Preference)
In lease, possession is only out of necessity to use the benefits. Therefore, beyond the necessary use, the hand remains with the lessor. Admitting possession in lease is not an admission of ownership. So his claim is accepted, and he may keep the item under the lease.
The necessity (ضرورة) makes possession instrumental, not substantive.
4
Analyze the Distinction
The difference is the purpose of possession: in deposit, possession is the main object (مقصودة); in lease, it is incidental to receiving benefits. Only when possession is the main purpose does admission of possession imply ownership.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf – the practical legal difference.
5
Apply the Hanafi Tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is istihsan. The principle: where strict analogy conflicts with the purpose of the contract and necessity, istihsan prevails.
Istihsan is a primary source in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو القياس، ووجه الاستحسان" : إن في الإجارة لم يُقر بيد الآخر مطلقاً، بل يده ضرورية ؛ لأجل الانتفاع فبقي فيما وراءَ الضّرورة في حكم يد المؤجر بخلاف الوديعة، الثوب معروفاً أنه للمقرّ أو الدابةُ أو الدار ، فقال : قبضته فيه، فكان القولُ قولُ المقرّ في قولهم ؛ لأن الملك فيه معروف للمقر. انتهى. [١]قوله : وهو القياس؛ ووجهه أنَّ المقرَّ أقرَّ باليد له ، ثم ادعى عليه الاستحقاق، فيقبلُ إقراره له دون دعواه عليه، فيجب عليه الردّ كما في مسألة الوديعة والقرض على ما تقدم. [٢] قوله : ووجه الاستحسان ...الخ ؛ تقريره : إنَّ اليد في الإجارة تثبت ضرورةً استيفاء المعقود عليه، وهو المنافع، فلا يكون إقراراً باليد لهما مقصوداً فلا يظهر في حق الاستحقاق على المُقِرِّ ، بخلاف الوديعة والقرض ؛ لأنَّ اليد فيهما مقصودة، فيكون الإقرار بهما إقراراً باليد. واجي
And it is the analogy, and the face of juristic preference: Indeed in lease, he is not considered to have admitted the hand of the other absolutely, but his hand is out of necessity for the sake of benefit, so beyond necessity it remains in the ruling of the hand of the lessor, unlike deposit. When the cloth, animal, or house is known to belong to the declarant, and he says: 'I took possession of it in it [the lease],' then the statement is the statement of the declarant in their [scholars'] view, because ownership in it is known for the declarant. End. [1] His saying: And it is the analogy; its manifestation: The declarant admitted the hand for himself, then he claimed entitlement against it, so his admission in favor of himself is accepted, not his claim against himself, so he must return it, as in the case of deposit and loan as previously mentioned. [2] His saying: And the face of juristic preference...etc.; its explanation: The hand in lease is established out of necessity to receive the contracted object, which is benefits, so it is not an intentional admission of hand for them, so it does not appear regarding the entitlement against the declarant, unlike deposit and loan, because the hand in them is intentional, so admitting them is admission of the hand.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage presents two legal reasoning methods—qiyas (strict analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference)—for a case where someone declares possession of an item known to belong to him (e.g., cloth, animal, house) and claims to have taken it on lease. The qiyas view: since the person admitted possession and then claimed entitlement, his admission stands, requiring him to return the item, analogous to deposit or loan. The istihsan view: in lease, possession is only incidental to using the benefits; beyond necessity, it remains with the lessor. Thus, the possession is not an admission of ownership, so the person's claim that he took it on lease is accepted. This contrasts with deposit, where possession is the primary purpose, making admission of possession equivalent to admission of ownership. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is the istihsan view, as it accounts for the intent and necessity in lease contracts.

Key Terms
إجارة (ijārah): A lease contract where possession is transferred for the use of benefits in exchange for rent.
وديعة (wadīʿah): A deposit where possession is the primary purpose for safekeeping.
قياس (qiyās): Strict analogy applying the ruling of a known case to a new case due to a shared effective cause.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that overrides strict analogy due to necessity, custom, or equity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, possession in lease is not an admission of ownership because it exists only out of necessity to receive benefits, unlike deposit where possession is the main purpose.

Sulh with Usufruct is Treated as Ijarah
Ruling that sulh with usufruct is ijarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that sulh with a usufruct as compensation is treated as ijarah and identify the conditions and invalidators.

Core Idea
Sulh with a usufruct is ijarah in meaning – timing is required, death voids it.

When a settlement (sulh) involves a usufruct as compensation, the Hanafi school treats it as a hire contract (ijarah) in its legal effects. This lesson examines the key condition of timing and the effects of death or loss of the usufruct, based on the commentary on the matn by Imam Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal classification
The act is a sulh (settlement) where the compensation (badal) is a usufruct (manfa'ah) – e.g., dwelling in a house for a year. The commentary states it is 'in the meaning of ijarah' because the essence is ownership of a usufruct.
2
Extract the condition for validity
The text explicitly states that timing (tawqīt) is stipulated. If the period is unknown, the contract is not permissible.
3
Identify the invalidating events (mubtilat)
The contract becomes invalid upon (1) death of either party during the period, (2) loss of the usufruct before receipt, (3) loss of the usufruct after partial receipt – invalid to the extent remaining.
After invalidation, the plaintiff returns to his original claim for the unfulfilled portion.
4
Trace the qiyas reasoning
The original case (asl) is ijarah, whose rulings are established by Sunnah and Ijma. The new case (far') is sulh with a usufruct. The effective cause (illah) is that both involve ownership of a usufruct in exchange for consideration. Therefore, the same rulings apply.
This is a clear qiyas jaliy (manifest analogy).
5
Note the authority and tarjih
The commentary reports this as the view of Imam Muhammad, stating 'this is all the saying of Muhammad, and it is the qiyas.' It is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school.
Other schools may differ, but within Hanafi, this is the operative ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكإجارة إن وَقَعَ عن مال بمنفعة، فَشُرِطَ التوقيت فيه، ويبطل بموت أحدهما في المدة [1] قوله : وكإجارة ... الخ ; يعني إنَّ الصلح مع إقرار إن وقع عن مال بمنفعة اعتبر ذلك الصلح إجارة. وصورته : إنَّ زيداً مثلاً ادعى على بكر شيئاً فاعترف به، ثم صالحه على سكنى داره سنة ، أو على ركوب فرسه المعلوم أو على لبس ثوبه، أو على خدمة عبده أو على زراعة أرضه مدة معلومة، فيكون هذا الصلح في معنى الإجارة ; لأن العبرة للمعاني، كذلك. وهذا الصلح والإجارة تمليك المنفعة، [2] قوله : فشرط التوقيت فيه ; حتى لو وقع الصلح على سكنى بيت إلى مدة معلومة جاز وإذا لم تكن المدة معلومة لم يجز. [3] قوله : ويبطل بموت أحدهما ; أي أحد المصالحين في مدة تعينت، فيرجع المدعي في دعواه بقدر ما لم يستوف من المنفعة ; لأنهما كالمؤجر والمستأجر، وكذا يبطل ذلك الصلح بفوات المنفعة قبل الاستيفاء، فيعود إلى الدعوى، ولو كان ذلك بعـد استيفاء بعض المنفعة بطل بقدر ما بقي فيرجعُ في دعواه بقدره، وهذا كله قول محمد ه، وهو القياس ; لأنه إجارة، وهي تبطل بواحد من هذه الأشياء.
And like a hire if it falls on wealth with a usufruct, so timing is stipulated in it, and it becomes invalid upon the death of either party during the period. [1] He said: 'And like a hire... etc.'; meaning that sulh with admission, if it falls on wealth with a usufruct, that sulh is considered a hire. Its example: Zayd, for instance, claimed something from Bakr, and he admitted it, then he settled with him for dwelling in his house for a year, or riding his known horse, or wearing his garment, or service of his slave, or cultivation of his land for a known period; then this sulh is in the meaning of hire, because consideration is given to meanings. And likewise, this sulh and hire are the ownership of a usufruct. [2] He said: 'So timing is stipulated in it'; even if the sulh falls on dwelling in a house for a known period, it is permissible; if the period is not known, it is not permissible. [3] He said: 'And it becomes invalid upon the death of either party'; meaning one of the two parties making the sulh during the specified period; then the plaintiff returns in his claim to the extent of what he has not received of the usufruct, because they are like the lessor and lessee. And similarly, that sulh becomes invalid upon the loss of the usufruct before receipt; then it returns to the lawsuit. And if that was after receipt of some of the usufruct, it becomes invalid to the extent of what remains, so he returns in his claim to that extent. This is all the saying of Muhammad, and it is the qiyas (analogy), because it is a hire, and it becomes invalid by one of these things.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school. The matn states that if a sulh contract involves a usufruct (manfa'ah) as compensation, it is treated like an ijarah (hire) contract. Therefore, the requirement of timing (tawqīt) is imposed, and the contract becomes invalid (bātil) upon the death of either party during the specified period. The commentary elaborates: the sulh is considered ijarah because the substance (meaning) is the exchange of a usufruct for consideration, and the rule in fiqh is that consideration is given to meanings, not just forms. Examples include settling a claim in exchange for dwelling in a house for a year, riding a horse, wearing a garment, service of a slave, or cultivation of land for a known period. The timing must be specified; otherwise, the contract is invalid. If one party dies during the period, the contract becomes invalid, and the plaintiff may resume his original claim for the portion of usufruct not received. Similarly, if the usufruct is lost (e.g., the house burns down) before receipt, the contract is void. If partially received, the remaining part reverts. All this is reported as the view of Imam Muhammad (a student of Abu Hanifa), and it is based on qiyas (analogy) because the contract is essentially ijarah. This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) for the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
إجارة (ijārah): A contract of hire or lease; exchange of a usufruct for consideration for a specified period.
منفعة (manfa‘ah): Usufruct; the benefit derived from an asset, such as dwelling in a house, riding a horse, etc.
توقيت (tawqīt): Specification of time; a condition in contracts involving usufructs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, if a settlement (sulh) is made with a usufruct as compensation, what type of contract does it become?
A) Sale (bay')
B) Hire (ijarah)
C) Gift (hibah)
D) Loan (ariyah)

Key Takeaway
Sulh with a usufruct as compensation is treated as ijarah in the Hanafi school, requiring a specified duration and ending upon death or loss of the usufruct.

Settlement on Benefits: Treated as a Lease – Conditions and Ikhtilaf
Commentary on sulh with benefit treated as lease; conditions and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid sulh on benefits, identify the effect of death or destruction on such a contract, and explain the ikhtilaf between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
A settlement exchanging property for a usufruct is legally a lease, requiring a fixed term and voiding upon death or loss.

This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah explains that when sulh (settlement) involves a benefit (manfa'ah) as compensation, it is treated precisely like an ijarah (lease). Therefore, the contract must specify its duration (tawqit), and it becomes void (batil) upon the death of either party or destruction of the subject matter—just as a lease would. The commentator also details a significant intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding the effect of death, highlighting the practical differences in application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal reclassification
The act is sulh (settlement) where the substitute (badal) is a benefit (manfa'ah). The commentator states this is like ijarah. We need to understand that the ruling follows ijarah.
This reclassification is based on qiyas jali (obvious analogy) because both involve transfer of usufruct.
2
List the conditions for validity
The key condition is specification of time (tawqit). Without it, the sulh is fasid (void). Also, the benefit must be known.
The passage gives examples: service, residence, riding, wearing, cultivation—all require known duration.
3
Follow the effects of death and destruction
According to Imam Muhammad (the relied-upon view), death of either party voids the contract for the remaining period. Destruction of the subject matter (e.g., slave dies) also voids it.
This is the primary ruling based on qiyas to ijarah.
4
Examine Abu Yusuf's dissenting position
Abu Yusuf distinguishes: death of defendant does not void; death of plaintiff voids only for benefits where people differ (e.g., riding/wearing) but not for uniform benefits (service/residence). Destruction of slave: if killed by defendant, voids by consensus; if by plaintiff/third party, differs.
Abu Yusuf's reasoning focuses on the purpose of sulh (cutting dispute) and practicality.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and thamarah al-khilaf
Muhammad's view is considered the stronger (qiyas) and is mufta bihi. The practical consequence is whether the settlement continues after death or reverts to the original claim.
Under Muhammad, the plaintiff can reclaim remaining benefit from the estate; under Abu Yusuf, the settlement often continues, preventing revival of the dispute.

And like a lease: if it occurs in exchange for property with a benefit, then specification of time is required in it, and it becomes void upon the death of one of them during the period. "And like a lease" if it occurs in exchange for property with a benefit, "then specification of time is required in it": meaning if the substitute is a benefit known by timing, like service and residence in a house, unlike when the settlement occurs in exchange for property for transferring this thing from here to a sum. And it becomes void upon the death of one of them during the period. If some or all of the property is found to belong to someone else, the defendant recovers from the plaintiff all or part of the amount paid. Example: Zaid claims a house in the possession of Amr, and Amr admits and settles with Zaid for one hundred dirhams, so the hundred is in Zaid's hand and the house in Amr's hand. Then half or all of the house is claimed by a third party; Amr recovers fifty dirhams in the first case and one hundred in the second. If part or all of the substitute is claimed, the plaintiff recovers from the defendant all or part of the settled property, because each is a substitute for the other. Whoever loses some or all recovers what he paid accordingly. [1] His saying: 'And like a lease' etc., means that a settlement with admission in exchange for property with a benefit is considered a lease. Example: Zaid claims something from Bakr, who admits it, then settles with him for residence in his house for a year, or for riding his known horse, or wearing his garment, or service of his slave, or cultivating his land for a known period; this settlement is in the sense of a lease, because consideration is given to meanings. And this settlement and lease both involve transfer of ownership of a benefit. [2] His saying: 'then specification of time is required in it': if the settlement is for residence in a house for a known period it is valid; if the period is unknown it is not valid. [3] His saying: 'and it becomes void upon the death of one of them': meaning one of the two parties settling during the specified period. Then the plaintiff returns to his claim to the extent of the benefit not yet received, because they are like lessor and lessee. Similarly, this settlement becomes void upon loss of the benefit before receipt, and the claim returns. If some benefit was received, it becomes void to the extent remaining, and he returns to his claim for that amount. All this is the saying of Muhammad, and it is analogy (qiyas), because it is a lease, and a lease becomes void by any of these things. [Page 297] Book of Settlement: Definition and Types. And the other two are an exchange with respect to the plaintiff, and a redemption of oath and termination of dispute with respect to the other. (And the other two): meaning settlement with silence or denial, (an exchange with respect to the plaintiff, and a redemption of oath and termination of dispute with respect to the other). And Abu Yusuf said: The settlement does not become void upon the death of the defendant; rather, the plaintiff receives the benefit as before. If the plaintiff dies, similarly in the service of a slave and residence in a house; the heir stands in his place for these two. It becomes void in the case of riding an animal, because the settlement is to terminate dispute, and voiding it by death of one would reopen it. So it remains where there is no difference between people in absolute terms, because receipt is possible by continuity of the contracting party and by his heir standing in his place. As for things where people differ, like wearing garments and riding an animal, if the defendant dies it remains, as receipt is possible by continuity; if the plaintiff dies it becomes void because the heir cannot take his place. If the slave is killed, the settlement becomes void according to Muhammad absolutely, like a lease. According to Abu Yusuf, he looks: if the plaintiff or a third party kills him, he guarantees his value and buys a slave with the value to serve him, but he has the option due to possible difference in service. Contentment with the first is not contentment with the second. If the defendant kills him, the settlement becomes void by consensus, because the master does not guarantee his own slave, so it is as if he died naturally or the master emancipated him—unlike a mortgaged slave, where the master must guarantee by destruction and emancipation, because the benefit of the contract of mortgage and possession is lost, as they clarified. [1] His saying: 'exchange with respect to the plaintiff': because he claims that what he took is a substitute for his claim. [2] His saying: 'and redemption of oath and termination of dispute with respect to the other': meaning the defendant, because he claims that the plaintiff is lying and wrong in his claim, and he only pays the money to avoid oath and to end the dispute. It is possible for one thing to have different rulings for different persons, just as marriage makes permissible between the spouses but makes forbidden their relatives; and rescission (iqalah) is a cancellation for the contracting parties but a new sale for a third party. Each takes according to his claim. This is apparent in denial, for it becomes clear by denial that what he gives is to end the dispute and redeem the oath.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of al-Wiqayah regarding the section of Sulh (settlement/compromise). The author explains that when a settlement is made in exchange for a benefit (manfa'ah), such as service or residence, it is legally treated as a lease (ijarah). Therefore, it requires specification of time (tawqit) for validity: if the duration is unknown, the settlement is invalid. Additionally, like a lease, it becomes void upon the death of either party during the term. The commentator provides an example: Zaid claims a house from Amr; Amr admits and settles for 100 dirhams. If later the house is found to belong to another, Amr recovers the price. Similarly, if the substitute is claimed by another, the plaintiff recovers the settled property. The author then details the ruling, attributing it to Imam Muhammad, stating that it is based on qiyas (analogy to lease). He notes that death or destruction of the subject matter voids the settlement. The passage then shifts to defining the nature of settlement in the context of denial or silence: from the plaintiff's perspective it is an exchange; from the defendant's perspective it is a redemption of oath and termination of dispute. A significant intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is presented: Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees with Muhammad regarding the effect of death. Abu Yusuf argues that the settlement does not void upon death of the defendant; the plaintiff continues to receive the benefit. If the plaintiff dies, the heir takes over for service of slave and residence, but not for riding an animal. He distinguishes between things that are uniform (like service and residence) and those where people differ (like wearing clothes or riding). The death of the slave is also discussed: according to Muhammad it voids the settlement absolutely; according to Abu Yusuf, if killed by the plaintiff or a third party, the value is used to buy another slave but with an option; if killed by the defendant, it voids by consensus. The passage concludes by illustrating how one transaction can have different legal effects for different parties, comparing to marriage and rescission.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): A contract to end a dispute, where one party gives something to the other in exchange for dropping a claim or to avoid an oath.
إجارة (ijarah): A contract for the transfer of ownership of a known benefit in exchange for known compensation, requiring specification of duration.
توقيت (tawqit): Specification of time; a necessary condition for validity of a settlement that involves a benefit, as it is treated like ijarah.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; here, settlement on benefits is analogized to ijarah because both involve transfer of usufruct.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, what happens to a settlement for a benefit (e.g., house residence for one year) if the defendant dies during the term?
A) The settlement continues and the heir provides the benefit.
B) The settlement becomes void and the plaintiff reclaims the remaining benefit.
C) The plaintiff must accept a monetary substitute.
D) The settlement is automatically extended.

Key Takeaway
A settlement on a benefit must specify its duration and is voided by death or destruction of the subject matter, following the rules of a lease.

Lender's Option in Case of Unauthorized Rental
Commentary on liability when borrowed item is rented out and perishes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the lender's option to claim compensation from either the borrower or the lessee when the borrower rents out the borrowed item and it perishes, and apply the principle of ghurur to determine the lessee's right of recourse.

Core Idea
The lender chooses whom to hold liable; the deceived lessee recourses against the borrower.

What happens when you lend your book to a friend, and that friend rents it to someone else without your knowledge, and the book gets damaged? Islamic law provides a clear remedy. The lender can seek compensation from either the original borrower or the unaware lessee. This lesson unpacks the logic behind this choice and the role of deception (ghurur) in determining who ultimately bears the loss.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the borrower (musta'ir) renting out the borrowed item without the lender's permission, followed by the item's destruction. The ruling concerns the lender's right to claim compensation (daman) and the lessee's right to recourse.
This is a tort-based liability scenario.
2
Locate the lender's option
The text states: 'the lender makes good its value, and he does not recourse against anyone, or the lessee'. The lender is mukhayyar (has a choice) to hold either the borrower or the lessee liable.
This is a clear statement of the Hanafi position.
3
Trace the basis for holding the borrower liable
When the borrower rents out the item, he exceeds the scope of the loan and becomes a usurper (ghasib). As a usurper, he is liable for the value regardless of fault. The rental income he collects must be given in charity.
This follows the principle that unauthorized use of another's property is usurpation.
4
Trace the basis for holding the lessee liable and his recourse
The lessee took possession from the borrower, believing the borrower had authority to lease. If the lessee was unaware that the item was borrowed, he is liable to the lender but can then recourse against the borrower due to deception (ghurur). If he knew, no recourse.
Ghurur is the key maksad: deception induces reliance.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on charity
Abu Yusuf differs on the charity of rental income by the usurper. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold that the borrower must give the rent in charity because it is tainted. Abu Yusuf allows keeping it. The commentary sides with the majority.
This is a minor dispute within the school.
