As for the conditions of formation: 1. Among them is sanity, so it is not formed from the insane or the child who does not understand; puberty is not a condition for it, so the sane child if he leases his property or himself—if he is authorized, it is effective, otherwise it is suspended pending the guardian's permission. Islam is also not a condition at all, so leasing and hiring from a Muslim, a dhimmi, a harbi, and a musta'min is permissible. Soundness. The contracting party being willing and deliberate is also not a condition for formation nor for effectiveness, but it is a condition. Among them is ownership and authority, so the leasing of a fuduli is not effective due to lack of ownership and authority, but it is formed as suspended pending the owner's permission according to us. Among them is the existence of the object of contract, so if a fuduli leases and the owner ratifies the contract after the usufruct has been fully utilized, his lease is not valid, and the rent belongs to the contracting party because the contracted usufruct has ceased to exist, while the agent's lease is valid due to the existence of authority. 4. Among them is delivery of the leased property in the lease of houses and the like if the contract is absolute—immediate delivery according to us. 5. Among them is that the contract be free from the condition of option, for if there is an option, it is not effective during the option period. As for the conditions of validity: 1. Among them is mutual consent of the contracting parties. 2. Among them is that the object of contract, which is the usufruct, be known with a knowledge that prevents dispute; if it is unknown with ignorance that leads to dispute, it prevents the validity of the contract; otherwise not. 3. Among them is specification of the benefit, so if he says 'I lease to you one of these two houses,' it is not valid. 4. Among them is specifying the period for houses, dwellings, and the like, and in hiring a wet nurse. 5. Among them is specifying the work in leasing lands, and likewise specifying the object of work for a common laborer (ajir mushtarak) by indication, designation, or specification of genus, type, quantity, and description in the cloth of laundering and tailoring, and specification of genus and quantity in hiring for herding horses and camels and the like. 6. Among them is that the usufruct be capable of being extracted in reality or legally, so hiring a runaway slave is not permissible, nor hiring for sins like dancing, singing, wailing, and the like. 7. Among them is that the work hired for not be an individual obligation (fard) or obligatory (wajib) upon the employee before the hire; if it was fard or wajib before it, it is not permissible. 8. Among them is that the benefit be intended, customarily extracted by the contract of lease, and transactions among people take place with it; so hiring trees to dry clothes is not permissible. 9. Among them is that the rent be known. 10. Among them is that the rent not be a benefit that is of the same genus as the object of contract, such as leasing dwelling for dwelling. 11. Among them is that the pillar be free from a condition that the contract does not require and does not suit. As for the conditions of bindingness: 1. Among them is that the contract be valid. 2. Among them is that the leased property not have a defect at the time of contract and time of delivery that impairs its use; if so, the contract is not binding. 3. Among them is the leased property's freedom from occurrence of a defect that impairs its use; if such occurs, the contract is no longer binding. This is what I have mentioned to you in summary, so that you may have insight in proceeding; the detail is mentioned in Fatawa Qadikhan, al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya, and other comprehensive works. And the analogical reasoning (qiyas) would be that this contract is not permissible because the object of contract, which is the usufruct, comes into existence after the contract, and attaching ownership to what does not exist is not valid, but it is permitted by the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus.
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage presents the conditions for the Ijarah (lease/employment) contract according to the Hanafi school. The author first lists the conditions for the formation (in'aqad) of the contract, then the conditions for its validity (sihha), and finally the conditions for its bindingness (luzum). The text begins with formation conditions: sanity is required (lunatics and non-comprehending children cannot contract); puberty is not a condition, so a discerning minor's lease is either effective (if authorized) or suspended (pending guardian approval). Islam is not required—leasing to/from non-Muslims is valid. Being free-willed and deliberate is not required for formation but is a condition for other aspects. Ownership and authority are needed; a fuduli (unauthorized agent) lease is suspended. The leased usufruct must exist at the time? Actually 'existence of the object' means the usufruct must be capable of existence; but the text says that if a fuduli's lease is ratified after the usufruct is consumed, it is invalid because the usufruct no longer exists. Delivery of the leased property in absolute leases of houses must be immediate. And the contract must be free from option conditions; if an option period exists, the contract is not effective during that period. Then validity conditions: mutual consent, knowledge of the usufruct (to avoid dispute), specification of benefit (e.g., cannot say 'one of these houses'), specification of period for dwellings and hiring nurses, specification of work for land and for common laborers (tailoring, laundering) with clear description, capability of extraction (cannot hire a runaway slave or for sin), the work must not be already obligatory on the employee (e.g., fard or wajib), the benefit must be intended and customary (trees not for drying clothes), rent must be known, rent cannot be of the same type as the object (e.g., house for house). Bindingness conditions: the contract must be valid, the leased property must be free from defects at contract and delivery, and it must remain free from defects; if a defect arises, the contract becomes non-binding. The author notes that such detail is found in major fatwa collections. Finally, a brief proof: analogical reasoning (qiyas) would oppose this contract because usufruct does not exist at the time of contract (like selling non-existent items), but it is permitted by the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus (ijma), overriding qiyas. This is a key Hanafi principle: istihsan (juristic preference) based on revealed sources overrides strict analogy.

Key Terms
الانعقاد (al-in'aqad): The formation or coming into existence of a contract.
الفضولي (al-fuduli): An unauthorized agent who contracts on behalf of another without permission.
الخيار (al-khiyar): An option or right to rescind a contract within a specified period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for the formation of Ijarah according to the passage?
A) The lessor must own the property or have authority to lease.
B) The contract must be free from an option condition.
C) The lessee must be a Muslim.
D) The usufruct must exist at the time of contract.

Key Takeaway
The formation of an Ijarah contract requires sanity, ownership, existence of usufruct, immediate delivery (for houses), and no option condition; without these, the contract does not come into existence.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

Conditions of Validity (Sihha) in Ijarah
Enumeration of validity conditions for Ijarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list and explain the eleven conditions required for the validity (sihha) of an Ijarah contract according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
An Ijarah contract is valid only when the usufruct is known, permissible, capable of extraction, and the rent is known and not of the same type as the object.

After discussing the formation conditions, the author now turns to the conditions for the validity (sihha) of the Ijarah contract. Even if a contract is formed, it may still be invalid if these conditions are not met. These conditions ensure that the contract is fair, free from ambiguity, and legally permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the eleven validity conditions
Read the Arabic text carefully and list each condition. Note how they are introduced.
The conditions cover consent, knowledge, specification, capability, and legality.
2
Focus on conditions regarding knowledge and specification
The usufruct must be known to prevent dispute. The benefit must be specified (cannot be ambiguous). The period or work must be specified depending on the type of lease.
Ambiguity that leads to dispute invalidates the contract.
3
Understand conditions related to the permissible nature of the benefit
The usufruct must be capable of extraction in reality and legally. Hiring for sin, a runaway slave, or work that is already obligatory on the employee is invalid.
The benefit must be intended and customary.
4
Analyze rent-related conditions
Rent must be known, and it cannot be of the same genus as the object (e.g., cannot rent a house in exchange for dwelling in another house).
This prevents riba-like exchanges.
5
Note the final condition: freedom from incompatible conditions
The contract pillar must be free from a condition that does not suit the contract.
This is a general principle: any condition that contradicts the nature of Ijarah renders it invalid.

Source Text

أما شرائط الانعقاد :
١. فمنها : العقل حتى لا تنعقد من المجنون والصبي الذي لا يعقل، والبلوغ ليس من شرائطها حتى أنّ الصبي العاقل لو أجر ماله أو نفسه فإن كان مأذوناً تنفذ، وإلا تقف على إجازة الولي.
والإسلام أيضاً ليس بشرط أصلاً حتى يجوز الإجارة والاستئجار من المسلم والذمي والحربي والمستأمن.
الصحة.
وكون العاقد طائعاً عامداً أيضاً ليس بشرط للانعقاد ولا للنفاذ، لكنه شرط .
ومنها : الملك والولاية حتى لا تنفذ إجارة الفضولي ؛ لعدم الملك والولاية، لكنه ينعقد موقوفاً على إجازة المالك عندنا. .
ومنها : قيام المعقود عليه، حتى إذا أجر الفضولي فأجاز المالك العقد بعد استيفاء المنفعة لم تجز إجارته، وكانت الأجرة للعاقد ؛ لأنَّ المنافع المعقود عليها قد انعدمت، وإجارة الوكيل بأخذه لوجود الولاية. 
٤. ومنها: تسليم المستأجر في إجارة المنازل ونحوها إذا كان العقد مطلقاً . التعجيل عندنا.
عن شرط
ه. ومنها : أن يكون العقد مطلقاً . عن شرط الخيار، فإن كان فيه خيار لا تنفذ في مدة الخيار.
وأما شرائط الصحة :
١. فمنها : رضاء المتعاقدين.
٢. ومنها : أن يكون المعقود عليه وهو المنافع معلوماً علماً يمنع المنازعة، فإن كان مجهولاً جهالة تفضي إلى المنازعة يمنع صحة العقد، وإلا فلا.
٣. ومنها : محل بيان المنفعة، حتى لو قال : أجرتُك إحدى هاتين الدارين لا تصح. 
٤. ومنها : بيانُ المدَّة في الدور المنازل ونحوها وفي استئجار الظئر.
ه. ومنها : بيان العمل في استئجار الضياع، وكذا بيان المعمول فيه في الأجير المشترك بالإشارة والتعيين أو بيان الجنس والنوع والقدر والصفة في ثوب القصارة والخياطة، وبيان الجنس والقدر في إجارة الرعي من الخيل والإبل ونحوهما. 
٦. ومنها : أن يكون مقدور الاستيفاء حقيقةً أو شرعاً ، فلا يجوز استئجار الآبق ولا الاستئجار على المعاصي كالرقص والغناء والنياحة ونحوها. .
ومنها : أن لا يكون العمل المستأجر له فرضاً ولا واجباً على الأجير قبل الإجارة، فلئن كان فرضاً أو واجباً قبلها لا تجوز.
. ومنها : أن تكون المنفعة مقصودة معتاداً استيفاؤها بعقد الإجارة، ويجري بهـا التعامل بين الناس، فلا يجوز استئجار الأشجار لتجفيف الثياب.
٩. ومنها : أن تكون الأجرة معلومة.
١٠ . ومنها : أن لا تكونَ الأجرة منفعة هي جنس المعقود عليه كإجارة السكني بالسكني. 
١١. ومنها : خلو الركن عن شرط لا يقتضيه العقد ولا يلائمه.
وأما شرائط اللزوم :
١. فمنها : كون العقد صحيحاً.
٢. ومنها : أن لا يكونَ بالمستأجر عيب في وقتِ العقدِ ووقت القبض يخل بالانتفاع به ، فإن كان لم يلزم العقد. 
٣. ومنها : سلامة المستأجر عن حدوث عيب به يخل بالانتفاع به ، فإن حدث لم يبق العقد لازماً، هذا ما ذكرته لك مجملاً ؛ لتكون على بصيرة في الشروع، والتفصيل مذكور في فتاوى قاضي خان»، و«الفتاوى الهندية ) ، وغيرهما من المبسوطات. وكان القياس أن لا يجوز هذا العقد ؛ لأن المعقود عليه وهو المنفعة توجد بعد العقد، وإضافة التمليك إلى ما يوجد لا تصح إلا أنه جاز بالكتاب والسنة والاجماع والمعقود.
As for the conditions of formation: 1. Among them is sanity, so it is not formed from the insane or the child who does not understand; puberty is not a condition for it, so the sane child if he leases his property or himself—if he is authorized, it is effective, otherwise it is suspended pending the guardian's permission. Islam is also not a condition at all, so leasing and hiring from a Muslim, a dhimmi, a harbi, and a musta'min is permissible. Soundness. The contracting party being willing and deliberate is also not a condition for formation nor for effectiveness, but it is a condition. Among them is ownership and authority, so the leasing of a fuduli is not effective due to lack of ownership and authority, but it is formed as suspended pending the owner's permission according to us. Among them is the existence of the object of contract, so if a fuduli leases and the owner ratifies the contract after the usufruct has been fully utilized, his lease is not valid, and the rent belongs to the contracting party because the contracted usufruct has ceased to exist, while the agent's lease is valid due to the existence of authority. 4. Among them is delivery of the leased property in the lease of houses and the like if the contract is absolute—immediate delivery according to us. 5. Among them is that the contract be free from the condition of option, for if there is an option, it is not effective during the option period. As for the conditions of validity: 1. Among them is mutual consent of the contracting parties. 2. Among them is that the object of contract, which is the usufruct, be known with a knowledge that prevents dispute; if it is unknown with ignorance that leads to dispute, it prevents the validity of the contract; otherwise not. 3. Among them is specification of the benefit, so if he says 'I lease to you one of these two houses,' it is not valid. 4. Among them is specifying the period for houses, dwellings, and the like, and in hiring a wet nurse. 5. Among them is specifying the work in leasing lands, and likewise specifying the object of work for a common laborer (ajir mushtarak) by indication, designation, or specification of genus, type, quantity, and description in the cloth of laundering and tailoring, and specification of genus and quantity in hiring for herding horses and camels and the like. 6. Among them is that the usufruct be capable of being extracted in reality or legally, so hiring a runaway slave is not permissible, nor hiring for sins like dancing, singing, wailing, and the like. 7. Among them is that the work hired for not be an individual obligation (fard) or obligatory (wajib) upon the employee before the hire; if it was fard or wajib before it, it is not permissible. 8. Among them is that the benefit be intended, customarily extracted by the contract of lease, and transactions among people take place with it; so hiring trees to dry clothes is not permissible. 9. Among them is that the rent be known. 10. Among them is that the rent not be a benefit that is of the same genus as the object of contract, such as leasing dwelling for dwelling. 11. Among them is that the pillar be free from a condition that the contract does not require and does not suit. As for the conditions of bindingness: 1. Among them is that the contract be valid. 2. Among them is that the leased property not have a defect at the time of contract and time of delivery that impairs its use; if so, the contract is not binding. 3. Among them is the leased property's freedom from occurrence of a defect that impairs its use; if such occurs, the contract is no longer binding. This is what I have mentioned to you in summary, so that you may have insight in proceeding; the detail is mentioned in Fatawa Qadikhan, al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya, and other comprehensive works. And the analogical reasoning (qiyas) would be that this contract is not permissible because the object of contract, which is the usufruct, comes into existence after the contract, and attaching ownership to what does not exist is not valid, but it is permitted by the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus.

Key Terms
الأجير المشترك (al-ajir al-mushtarak): A common laborer who works for the public, not exclusively for one employer.
الجهالة (al-jahalah): Ignorance or ambiguity regarding the object of contract.

Conditions of Bindingness (Luzum) and the Proof of Ijarah's Permissibility
Enumeration of bindingness conditions and proof of permissibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for the bindingness of an Ijarah contract and explain how the Hanafi school justifies the permissibility of Ijarah despite the qiyas objection.

Core Idea
Ijarah is binding only if the contract is valid and the leased property remains defect-free; its permissibility is established by Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma, overriding the qiyas objection.

After discussing formation and validity, the author concludes with the conditions for bindingness (luzum). Even a valid Ijarah may not be binding if defects arise. The passage ends with a proof that Ijarah is permissible despite the logical objection that the usufruct does not exist at the time of contract.

Guided Path
1
List the three conditions for bindingness
Read the text and identify the three conditions for luzum.
The conditions are: (1) valid contract, (2) no defect at contract and delivery, (3) no defect arising thereafter.
2
Understand the consequence of defects
If a defect exists at the time of contract or delivery that impairs use, the contract is not binding. Similarly, if a defect arises later, the contract ceases to be binding.
Non-binding means the lessee may have the option to cancel or seek reduction in rent.
3
Analyze the proof for Ijarah
The author states that qiyas would not permit Ijarah because the usufruct does not exist at contract, but it is permitted by the Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma. This istihsan overrides the qiyas.
This is a classic Hanafi application of istihsan based on primary sources.
4
Identify the sources cited
The proof cites the Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma collectively, without specifying individual verses or hadith. The author assumes the reader knows them.
Major proofs include verses like 'فاستأجرهم' (al-Qasas:26) and hadith about hiring laborers.

Among them is specifying the work in leasing lands, and likewise specifying the object of work for a common laborer (ajir mushtarak) by indication, designation, or specification of genus, type, quantity, and description in the cloth of laundering and tailoring, and specification of genus and quantity in hiring for herding horses and camels and the like. 6. Among them is that the usufruct be capable of being extracted in reality or legally, so hiring a runaway slave is not permissible, nor hiring for sins like dancing, singing, wailing, and the like. 7. Among them is that the work hired for not be an individual obligation (fard) or obligatory (wajib) upon the employee before the hire; if it was fard or wajib before it, it is not permissible. 8. Among them is that the benefit be intended, customarily extracted by the contract of lease, and transactions among people take place with it; so hiring trees to dry clothes is not permissible. 9. Among them is that the rent be known. 10. Among them is that the rent not be a benefit that is of the same genus as the object of contract, such as leasing dwelling for dwelling. 11. Among them is that the pillar be free from a condition that the contract does not require and does not suit. As for the conditions of bindingness: 1. Among them is that the contract be valid. 2. Among them is that the leased property not have a defect at the time of contract and time of delivery that impairs its use; if so, the contract is not binding. 3. Among them is the leased property's freedom from occurrence of a defect that impairs its use; if such occurs, the contract is no longer binding. This is what I have mentioned to you in summary, so that you may have insight in proceeding; the detail is mentioned in Fatawa Qadikhan, al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya, and other comprehensive works. And the analogical reasoning (qiyas) would be that this contract is not permissible because the object of contract, which is the usufruct, comes into existence after the contract, and attaching ownership to what does not exist is not valid, but it is permitted by the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus.
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage presents the conditions for the Ijarah (lease/employment) contract according to the Hanafi school. The author first lists the conditions for the formation (in'aqad) of the contract, then the conditions for its validity (sihha), and finally the conditions for its bindingness (luzum). The text begins with formation conditions: sanity is required (lunatics and non-comprehending children cannot contract); puberty is not a condition, so a discerning minor's lease is either effective (if authorized) or suspended (pending guardian approval). Islam is not required—leasing to/from non-Muslims is valid. Being free-willed and deliberate is not required for formation but is a condition for other aspects. Ownership and authority are needed; a fuduli (unauthorized agent) lease is suspended. The leased usufruct must exist at the time? Actually 'existence of the object' means the usufruct must be capable of existence; but the text says that if a fuduli's lease is ratified after the usufruct is consumed, it is invalid because the usufruct no longer exists. Delivery of the leased property in absolute leases of houses must be immediate. And the contract must be free from option conditions; if an option period exists, the contract is not effective during that period. Then validity conditions: mutual consent, knowledge of the usufruct (to avoid dispute), specification of benefit (e.g., cannot say 'one of these houses'), specification of period for dwellings and hiring nurses, specification of work for land and for common laborers (tailoring, laundering) with clear description, capability of extraction (cannot hire a runaway slave or for sin), the work must not be already obligatory on the employee (e.g., fard or wajib), the benefit must be intended and customary (trees not for drying clothes), rent must be known, rent cannot be of the same type as the object (e.g., house for house). Bindingness conditions: the contract must be valid, the leased property must be free from defects at contract and delivery, and it must remain free from defects; if a defect arises, the contract becomes non-binding. The author notes that such detail is found in major fatwa collections. Finally, a brief proof: analogical reasoning (qiyas) would oppose this contract because usufruct does not exist at the time of contract (like selling non-existent items), but it is permitted by the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus (ijma), overriding qiyas. This is a key Hanafi principle: istihsan (juristic preference) based on revealed sources overrides strict analogy.

Key Terms
اللزوم (al-luzum): Bindingness; a contract is lazim when both parties are bound to perform without option to rescind unless by mutual agreement.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning in Islamic law; extending a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a shared effective cause (illa).
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference; departing from a qiyas ruling in favor of a stronger evidence or public interest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a leased house has a major defect at the time of delivery that the lessee discovers on the first day, what is the status of the contract according to the passage?
A) The contract is void because the defect was not disclosed.
B) The contract is valid and binding because the defect is minor.
C) The contract is not binding; the lessee may choose to cancel.
D) The contract is binding but the lessee must accept the defect.

Key Takeaway
An Ijarah contract is binding only if valid and free from defects that impair use; its permissibility is established by Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma, overriding the qiyas objection.

Conditions and Proofs of Ijara: Validity, Bindingness, and Evidences
Ruling with proof: conditions of ijara and evidences for its validity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the conditions of validity (shurut al-sihha) from conditions of bindingness (shurut al-luzum) in an ijara contract, and explain the Hanafi proofs from Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and rational need that establish its permissibility.

Core Idea
Ijara is valid despite the benefit not existing at contract—Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and need override the qiyas objection.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi framework for ijara (hire/lease). We will first explore the conditions that make an ijara contract valid, then the conditions that make it binding. Finally, we examine the evidences—Quran, Sunnah, consensus, and rational necessity—that establish its permissibility and refute the objection that the nonexistence of benefit at the time of contract invalidates it.

Guided Path
1
List the conditions of validity (shurut al-sihha)
Identify each condition mentioned: specification of work, possibility of exacting benefit, not hiring for fard/wajib, customary benefit, known wage, wage not same genus as object, no unsuitable conditions.
These conditions ensure the contract is valid and enforceable.
2
Distinguish conditions of bindingness (shurut al-luzum)
These include the contract being valid, no defect in the hired object at contract/delivery, and safety from later defects. If any condition is missing, the contract is not binding.
Bindingness relates to enforceability, not validity.
3
Recognize the qiyas objection
The passage states that analogy would reject ijara because the benefit does not exist at contract. This is a hypothetical objection that the Hanafi school addresses.
The qiyas is based on the principle that the object of sale must exist.
4
Trace the Hanafi response: four proofs
The passage cites: Quran (Surah al-Qasas 27), Sunnah (hadith of cupping and order to give wage), Ijma (consensus), and rational need (people need housing/transport). These override the qiyas.
These proofs establish the permissibility and validity of ijara.
5
Understand 'contracting moment by moment'
Clarify the Hanafi concept that the contract's effect applies continuously as benefit arises, not that a new contract is formed each moment.
The initial offer and acceptance bind the entire duration.

وأما شرائط اللزوم :
١. فمنها : كون العقد صحيحاً.
٢. ومنها : أن لا يكونَ بالمستأجر عيب في وقتِ العقدِ ووقت القبض يخل بالانتفاع به ، فإن كان لم يلزم العقد. ٣. ومنها : سلامة المستأجر عن حدوث عيب به يخل بالانتفاع به ، فإن حدث لم يبق العقد لازماً، هذا ما ذكرته لك مجملاً ؛ لتكون على بصيرة في الشروع، والتفصيل مذكور في فتاوى قاضي خان»، و«الفتاوى الهندية ) ، وغيرهما من المبسوطات. وكان القياس أن لا يجوز هذا العقد ؛ لأن المعقود عليه وهو المنفعة توجد بعد العقد، وإضافة التمليك إلى ما يوجد لا تصح إلا أنه جاز بالكتاب والسنة والاجماع والمعقود.
أما الكتاب : فقوله له : عَلَى أَن تَأْجُرَنِي ثَمَى حِجَع ) ، وشريعة من قبلنا لازمة ما لم يظهر نسخها. وأما السنّة : فما رواه الشيخان (۲) من حديث ابن عباس : «إنَّ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم احتجم وأعطى الحجام أجره»، وما أخرجه ابن ماجة من حديث ابن عمر الله إن رسول الله قال : أعطوا الأجير أجره قبل أن يجف عرقه (۳). والظاهرُ أنَّ الأمر بإعطاء الأجرِ دليل على صحة العقد، وما رواه محمد له في کتاب «الآثار» من قوله عليه : «من استأجر أجيراً فليعلمه أجره فأما المعقول ؛ فلأن بالناس حاجة إليه ولا مفسدة فيه، فيجوز وينعقد ساعة فساعة على حسب حدوث المنفعة، والمراد من انعقاد العلة ساعة فساعة في كلام الفقهاء ، وهو حمل لعلّة ونفاذها في المحلّ ساعة فساعة لارتباط الإيجاب والقبول كلّ ساعة. وإن كان ظاهر كلامهم يوهم ذلك فلا يراد أنَّ الانعقاد هو ارتباط القبول بالإيجاب، فإذا حصل الارتباط بإقامته الدَّارَ مقام المنفعة يتحقق الانعقاد، فما معنى الانعقاد ساعة فساعة بعد ذلك ، فتأمل.
ومن محاسن الإجارة دفع الحاجة بقليل من البدل، فإن كل أحد لا يقدر على دار يسكنها وحمام يغتسل فيها، وإبل يحمل أثقاله الى بلد لم يكن يبلغه إلا بمشقة النفس ؛ فلذا أجمعوا على جوازها واتفقوا على نفاذها.

Book of Ijara / Its definition, conditions, and forms. 5. Among them: specification of the work in hiring lands, and similarly specification of the work in the common worker (ajir mushtarak) by indication and designation, or specification of type, kind, quantity, and description in the cloth of washing and sewing, and specification of type and quantity in hiring for grazing of horses, camels, and the like. 6. Among them: that it be possible to exact the benefit actually or legally, so it is not permissible to hire a runaway slave, nor to hire for sinful acts like dancing, singing, lamentation, and the like. 7. Among them: that the work hired for not be an obligation (fard) or duty (wajib) upon the employee before the hire; if it was fard or wajib before it, it is not permissible. 8. Among them: that the benefit be intended and customarily exacted through the contract of hire, and dealings occur among people through it, so it is not permissible to hire trees for drying clothes. 9. Among them: that the wage be known. 10. Among them: that the wage not be a benefit that is the same genus as the object of contract, like renting a dwelling for a dwelling. 11. Among them: that the pillar be free from a condition that does not necessitate the contract nor suit it. As for conditions of bindingness (shurut al-luzum): 1. Among them: that the contract be valid. 2. Among them: that the hired object not have a defect at the time of the contract and the time of taking possession that impairs the benefit; if it does, the contract is not binding. 3. Among them: safety of the hired object from the occurrence of a defect that impairs the benefit; if it occurs, the contract is no longer binding. This is what I have mentioned to you in summary so that you may have insight at the beginning; the details are mentioned in Fatawa Qadi Khan, Al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya, and other extensive works. The analogy (qiyas) would be that this contract is not valid because the object of contract, which is the benefit, comes into existence after the contract, and adding ownership to what comes into existence is not valid. However, it is permitted by the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus (ijma). As for the Book: His statement, '...on that you hire me...' (Qasas 27), and the law of those before us is binding as long as it is not abrogated. As for the Sunnah: what the two Shaykhs (Bukhari and Muslim) narrated from Ibn Abbas: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, cupped himself and gave the cupper his wage,' and what Ibn Majah narrated from Ibn Umar: 'The Messenger of Allah said: Give the worker his wage before his sweat dries.' Apparently, the command to give the wage is evidence of the validity of the contract. And what Muhammad (al-Shaybani) narrated in his book 'Al-Athar' from his saying: 'Whoever hires a worker, let him inform him of his wage.' As for rational proof: because people have a need for it and there is no harm in it, so it is permissible and is contracted moment by moment according to the occurrence of the benefit. The meaning of 'contracting moment by moment' in the speech of the jurists is the application of the cause and its effect on the locus moment by moment due to the linkage of offer and acceptance every moment. Although the apparent meaning of their speech might suggest that, it does not mean that contracting is the linkage of acceptance to offer. For if the linkage is achieved by substituting the house for the benefit, then contracting is realized. So what is the meaning of 'contracting moment by moment' after that? Contemplate. Among the beauties of ijara is fulfilling need with little compensation, because not everyone is able to have a house to live in or a bath to bathe in, or camels to carry his loads to a town he could not reach without hardship. Therefore they agreed on its permissibility and concurred on its effectiveness. His saying: 'Al-Ijara' – ijara with kasra on the hamza is the well-known pronunciation, and al-Rafi'i narrated also damma.
Source pages p. 503

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya is a commentary expanding on the legal framework of ijara (hire/lease) within the Hanafi school. It begins by listing the conditions of validity (shurut al-sihha) for an ijara contract. These include: specifying the work or subject matter clearly (e.g., land to be worked, or tasks for a common worker like washing or sewing, and specifying the type and quantity for grazing animals); the benefit must be possible to exact either physically or legally (thus hiring a runaway slave is invalid, as is hiring for sinful acts like dancing, singing, or lamentation); the work must not be already a fard or wajib upon the worker before the contract (e.g., you cannot hire someone to pray for you because prayer is a personal obligation); the benefit must be a customary, intended benefit that people deal in (hence hiring trees just to dry clothes is not permissible because it is not a customary form of benefit); the wage must be known; the wage must not be of the same type as the object (e.g., renting a dwelling for a dwelling is invalid because it leads to ambiguity); and the contract must be free from conditions that are not inherent or suitable to the contract. Next, it mentions conditions of bindingness (shurut al-luzum): the contract must be valid to begin with; the hired object must be free from defects at the time of contract and delivery that impair its use; and no new defect should arise afterwards that impairs use—if such a defect occurs, the contract ceases to be binding. The commentator then notes that these are summarized points, with details available in larger works like Fatawa Qadikhan and Al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya. Importantly, the text addresses a potential qiyas objection: since the benefit (manfa'a) comes into existence gradually after the contract, one might argue that it cannot be the object of a sales-like transfer. However, the Hanafi school upholds the validity of ijara based on stronger evidences: the Quran (Surah al-Qasas, verse 27, where Musa is hired), the Sunnah (the Prophet himself hired a cupper, and he commanded giving the worker his wage before his sweat dries), consensus (ijma) of the companions, and rational need (people require housing, transport, etc., and no harm is involved). The commentator clarifies that the phrase 'contracting moment by moment' does not mean a separate contract each moment; rather it means the effect of the contract applies continuously as the benefit is realized, but the initial offer and acceptance bind the entire duration. Finally, he praises ijara as a means of fulfilling needs with minimal cost, which is why the community unanimously accepted its permissibility.

Key Terms
الإجارة (al-ijāra): A contract for the transfer of a permissible, specified benefit in exchange for a known wage.
الأجير المشترك (al-ajīr al-mushtarak): A worker who is hired by multiple parties for a shared service, e.g., a laundry worker or tailor serving the public.
المنفعة (al-manfaʿa): The benefit or utility that is the object of the ijara contract; it must be permissible, intended, and customarily valued.
شرائط اللزوم (shurūṭ al-luzūm): Conditions that make the contract binding, i.e., neither party can unilaterally rescind.

A) The work must not be fard or wajib upon the worker before the contract.
B) The wage must be known (ma'lum).
C) The hired object must be free from defects at the time of contract and delivery.
D) The benefit must be a customary, intended benefit.

Key Takeaway
Ijara is valid by Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and need, despite the qiyas objection that the benefit is not present at contract.

Proofs for the Validity of Ijarah
Proof passage establishing ijarah's validity via Quran, Sunnah, reason, and ijma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three categories of proofs for the validity of ijarah (Quran, Sunnah, and aql) and explain the Hanafi position that ijarah is mubah based on these proofs.

Core Idea
Ijarah is permissible because divine texts, prophetic practice, rational need, and scholarly consensus all affirm its validity.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah presents the classical Hanafi proof structure for why ijarah (hiring/leasing contracts) is legally valid. The author systematically cites the Quran, multiple hadiths, rational necessity, and unanimous consensus. Understanding this multi-layered dalil framework is essential for appreciating how Hanafi jurists establish a ruling as mubah (permissible) rather than wajib or haram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three proof categories
Recognize that the passage divides proofs into al-Kitab (Quran), al-Sunnah (Prophetic traditions), and al-Ma'qul (rational reasoning). Note the order: Quran first, then Sunnah, then reason.
Hanafi proofs typically prioritize naqli (scriptural) over aqli (rational) evidence.
2
Examine the Quranic verse
Verse 27 of Surah al-Qasas shows Prophet Musa contracting to work for eight years. The Hanafi principle: laws of previous prophets are binding unless abrogated; no abrogation exists here, so this establishes permissibility.
The imperative 'ta'juranī' indicates a contract of hire.
3
Examine the Sunnah proofs
Three hadiths: (a) The Prophet paid the cupper (implies contract validity), (b) command to pay wages before sweat dries (implies wage is due, confirming the contract), (c) command to inform the worker of his wage (ensures transparency). The command to pay is taken as evidence of the underlying contract's validity.
The second hadith is from Ibn Majah; the third is from Kitab al-Athar by Imam Muhammad.
4
Analyze the rational proof
People need to benefit from assets they cannot own (houses, baths, transport). There is no harm in ijarah; it fulfills needs and prevents hardship. The passage clarifies that the contract is concluded immediately but the benefit is realized gradually, so the contract takes effect moment by moment.
This rational argument addresses potential objections about the non-existence of benefit at the time of contract.
5
Note the consensus
The passage concludes that scholars have unanimously agreed on the permissibility and effectiveness of ijarah. This ijma' solidifies the ruling.
Ijma' is a binding proof in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الكتاب : فقوله تعالى : عَلَى أَن تَأْجُرَنِي ثَمَانِيَ حِجَجٍ [القصص:27]، وشريعة من قبلنا لازمة ما لم يظهر نسخها. وأما السنّة : فما رواه الشيخان من حديث ابن عباس : «إنَّ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم احتجم وأعطى الحجام أجره»، وما أخرجه ابن ماجة من حديث ابن عمر أن رسول الله قال : «أعطوا الأجير أجره قبل أن يجف عرقه». والظاهرُ أنَّ الأمر بإعطاء الأجرِ دليل على صحة العقد، وما رواه محمد في كتاب «الآثار» من قوله عليه السلام : «من استأجر أجيراً فليعلمه أجره». وأما المعقول ؛ فلأن بالناس حاجة إليه ولا مفسدة فيه، فيجوز وينعقد ساعة فساعة على حسب حدوث المنفعة، والمراد من انعقاد العلة ساعة فساعة في كلام الفقهاء ، وهو حمل العلة ونفاذها في المحلّ ساعة فساعة لارتباط الإيجاب والقبول كلّ ساعة. وإن كان ظاهر كلامهم يوهم ذلك فلا يراد أنَّ الانعقاد هو ارتباط القبول بالإيجاب، فإذا حصل الارتباط بإقامته الدَّارَ مقام المنفعة يتحقق الانعقاد، فما معنى الانعقاد ساعة فساعة بعد ذلك، فتأمل. ومن محاسن الإجارة دفع الحاجة بقليل من البدل، فإن كل أحد لا يقدر على دار يسكنها وحمام يغتسل فيها، وإبل يحمل أثقاله الى بلد لم يكن يبلغه إلا بمشقة النفس ؛ فلذا أجمعوا على جوازها واتفقوا على نفاذها.
As for the Book: His statement, the Exalted: 'That you hire me for eight years' [Al-Qasas:27], and the law of those before us is binding unless abrogated. As for the Sunnah: what the two Shaykhs narrated from Ibn Abbas: 'The Messenger of Allah ﷺ got cupped and gave the cupper his wage', and what Ibn Majah narrated from Ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Give the hired worker his wage before his sweat dries.' And it is apparent that the command to give the wage is evidence for the validity of the contract. And what Muhammad narrated in the book 'Al-Athar' from his statement ﷺ: 'Whoever hires a worker, let him inform him of his wage.' As for the rational: because people have need of it and there is no harm in it, so it is permissible and is contracted moment by moment according to the occurrence of the benefit. And what is meant by the contract being concluded moment by moment in the speech of the jurists is the application of the cause and its effect in the place moment by moment due to the connection of offer and acceptance every moment. And if the apparent meaning of their speech suggests that, it is not meant that the conclusion is the connection of acceptance with offer; so if connection is established by substituting the house in place of the benefit, the conclusion occurs, so what is the meaning of conclusion moment by moment after that? Reflect. And among the merits of ijarah is fulfilling need with little compensation, for not everyone can afford a house to live in, a bath to bathe in, or camels to carry his loads to a land he could not reach except with hardship; therefore they have unanimously agreed on its permissibility and concurred on its effectiveness.

Commentary
This passage is a proof passage (dalil) establishing the validity of ijarah (hiring/leasing). It begins with a Quranic verse from Surah al-Qasas (28:27) where Prophet Musa contracts to work for eight years, which is taken as a proof since previous laws are binding unless abrogated. Then two hadiths: the Prophet ﷺ paid the cupper, implying the contract was valid; and the command to pay wages before sweat dries indicates the contract's validity (since payment is due after work, but promptness is recommended). A third narration from Muhammad al-Shaybani's Kitab al-Athar commands informing the worker of his wage, which implies a valid contract. Rational proof follows: people need to benefit from assets they cannot own temporarily (houses, baths, transport), and there is no prohibition, so it is permissible. The passage clarifies that the contract is concluded instantaneously but the benefit is realized gradually, hence the contract takes effect over time. The final remark notes that ijarah fulfills need with minimal cost, and there is consensus on its permissibility.

Key Terms
الإجارة (al-ijarah): A contract for benefit (manfa'ah) in exchange for compensation, such as hiring a worker or renting a property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary rational proof (dalil 'aqli) for the validity of ijarah according to this passage?
A) It is mentioned in the Quran
B) People need it and there is no harm in it
C) The Prophet ﷺ paid the cupper
D) There is consensus on its prohibition

Key Takeaway
Ijarah is valid and mubah based on Quranic permission, prophetic practice, rational necessity, and unanimous consensus.

Linguistic Definition of Ijarah: Etymology and Verbal Forms
Etymology and correct verbal forms of 'ijarah'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three vowel pronunciations of 'ijarah' and state the Hanafi position on its correct verbal derivation (af'ala vs. fā'ila).

Core Idea
The term 'ijarah' is a noun for the wage, not the contract; the correct verbal noun is 'ijar'.

This lesson unpacks the linguistic debate surrounding the term 'ijarah'. While it is commonly used as the name of the hire contract, Hanafi scholars insist on a precise derivation: the verb is 'ājara yūjiru ījāran' (from af'ala), and 'al-ijārah' itself refers to the wage. Understanding this distinction is crucial for proper legal terminology.

Guided Path
1
Identify Pronunciation Variants
Locate the three vowel patterns of the hamzah in 'ijarah' mentioned: kasra (famous), damma (Rafi'i), and fatha (Tha'lab). Understand that these are purely linguistic variations.
The kasra form is the standard in Hanafi texts.
2
Analyze the Verb Form Dispute
Some grammarians consider the verb from fā'ila (mufā'alah pattern), yielding 'ājara yu'ājiru mu'ājarah'. Others, including Hanafi authorities, insist on af'ala, giving 'ājara yūjiru ījāran'.
The Hanafi stance relies on Al-Misbah al-Munir and Al-Azhari.
3
Examine the Argument for 'Ījār'
The passage notes that 'al-ījār' (verbal noun) is more precise for the sale of benefits, while 'al-ijārah' is the wage itself. Qadizada denies that 'ijārah' is ever a verbal noun.
This distinction is maintained in Hanafi fatwa writing.
4
Summarize the Hanafi Position
The relied-upon view: the contract is called 'ijārah' by convention, but its verbal noun is 'ījār'. The verb is from af'ala, not fā'ila, and 'mu'ājarah' is incorrect for leasing.
No practical effect on contract validity, but important for legal precision.

His saying: 'Al-Ijarah'; al-ijarah with kasra of the hamzah is the famous (pronunciation), and al-Rafi'i narrated damma. And the author of 'Al-Muhkam' said: they both (with damma) are a noun for what is taken, derived from ajr, which is the compensation of a dissolve, and it is transmitted from Tha'lab: fatha, so it has three pronunciations of the hamzah. Some Arabic experts said: al-ijarah is a fu'alah from mufa'alah, and 'ājara is on the pattern of fā'ila, not af'ala, because al-ījār has not come; so the imperfect is yu'ājiru, and the active participle is al-mu'ājir. The detail is in what is said in 'Al-Misbah al-Munir': 'I gave (ājartu) the house on lease, so I am a mu'jir, and it is not said mu'ājir, that is wrong; it is said ajartuhu mu'ājarah, like 'āmaltuhu mu'āmalah, and 'āqadtuhu mu'āqadah; because what is of fā'ila in the sense of mufā'alah, like musāraka and muzāra'ah, only takes one object, and mu'ājarah of the hired worker is of that kind. So ājartu al-dāra wal-'abda is from af'ala, not from fā'ila. And some say ājartu al-dāra on the pattern of fā'ila, so they say ājartuhu mu'ājarah. Al-Azhari confined himself to ājartuhu so he is mu'jir, and al-Akhfash said: among the Arabs are those who say ājartuhu mu'ājarah.
Source pages p. 504

Commentary
This passage is a definition and linguistic analysis of the term 'ijarah'. It begins by noting the famous pronunciation: with kasra on the hamzah, but Rafi'i reported damma, and some say fatha, giving three possible vowel patterns. It then discusses the verb form: some Arabic grammarians consider it from the pattern of mufā'alah (mutual action) with the verb 'ājara (yu'ājiru), while others insist it is from af'ala (ājara yūjiru). The author cites several lexicons: 'Ayn al-Khalil uses ājartu (ījāran) meaning 'I leased out'; 'Takmilat al-Bahr' prefers al-ījār (the verbal noun) as it specifically means the sale of benefits, whereas al-ijārah more commonly refers to the wage itself. Qadizada denies that al-ijārah is a verbal noun. The gloss then summarizes a dispute: some argue that the verb is from mufā'alah (so the verbal noun should be mu'ājarah), but reliable sources like al-Misbāh al-Munīr confirm that the correct verb for leasing a house is ājara (from af'ala) and that mu'ājir is a mistake, though some Arabs do use it. The upshot: the standard technical term in Hanafi fiqh is al-ijārah, derived from the verb ājara (ījāran), and the verbal noun mu'ājarah is incorrect for this context.

Key Terms
الإجارة (al-ijarah): A noun derived from 'ajr' meaning wage; used as the name of the contract for hiring or leasing.
الإيجار (al-ijar): The verbal noun from the verb 'ajara' meaning the act of letting or hiring out.

Definition of Ijarah: Sale of Known Benefit
Matn and commentary defining ijarah and expanding on its conditions and implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of ijarah, identify its essential elements (benefit, compensation, exchange), and apply the definition to determine the validity of a simple ijarah contract.

Core Idea
Ijarah is the exchange of a known benefit for a known compensation—a sale of utility, not property.

This lesson presents the foundational Hanafi definition of ijarah (leasing or hiring). The matn from Al-Wiqaya defines it as a sale of a known benefit for a known compensation. The commentary from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya clarifies that 'sale' here means exchange, not a transfer of property, because benefit is not property in the strict sense. Understanding this definition is key to distinguishing ijarah from other contracts and to applying its rules of validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Contract and its Ruling
Start by reading the matn: 'وهي بيع نفع معلوم بعوض' (It is the sale of a known benefit for a known compensation). Recognize that this defines ijarah as a valid commutative contract.
The contract is sahih (valid) when conditions are met.
2
Break Down the Definition into Three Elements
The definition contains three key components: (1) sale (بيع) – meaning exchange, (2) benefit (نفع) – must be known in type and amount, (3) compensation (عوض) – must be known, can be mithli or qimi.
Sale here is metaphorical—not a transfer of property, since benefit is not property literally.
3
Understand the Implication of ‘Sale’ in the Definition
The commentary explains that mentioning sale indicates ijarah requires offer and acceptance (like sale) and can be concluded by mutual delivery (ta'ati). This distinguishes ijarah from gratuitous contracts.
This implication is derived from the word 'بيع'.
4
Examine the Conditions of Knowledge for Benefit and Compensation
Both the benefit and the compensation must be known (معلوم) to avoid uncertainty (gharar). Benefit is known by specifying type and amount (e.g., duration, location). Compensation is known by specifying the rent or wage.
The example of renting a pot without specification shows uncertainty invalidates the contract, but if specific pots are later brought and accepted, a new valid contract arises.
5
Apply the Definition to a Practical Scenario
Use the definition to test a scenario: renting a car for a week for $200. The benefit (transport for a week) is known, the compensation ($200) is known, and offer/acceptance is present. Therefore, the contract is valid.
If any element is unknown, the contract becomes fasid (defective).

(1) And ijarah is a verbal noun from ajar yu'ajir in the sense of wage, but in shari'ah it is transferred to the contract. He said: [1] (It is the sale of a known benefit for a known compensation). [1] His statement: 'It is the sale of a benefit...' meaning ijarah is a sale of a benefit known in type and amount for a financial compensation, or a benefit of a different type than the subject matter, known, whether that compensation is mithli like measured and weighed items, or qimi like clothes and animals, etc. And the meaning of 'sale' here is exchange of one thing for another, not exchange of property for property, because benefit is not called property except metaphorically. Benefit is that by which a person reaches his objective. It is said: nafa'ani al-shay' naf'an - it benefitted me. As in al-Misbah. And in al-Sirah: naf' means profit and gain, opposite of harm. End. So what al-Qahistani said: 'Benefit is pleasure and comfort from repelling heat and cold, etc.' has no basis in language books except as an individual part of its general concept. And the mention of 'sale' indicates that ijarah requires offer and acceptance just like sale, and it is concluded by mutual give-and-take (ta'ati) like sale, as when one rents a pot without specification, and that it is not permissible due to variation in size, except if one brings pots and accepts them on the first rent, it is valid as a new contract. As stated in al-Dhakhirah and others. (Footnotes: disagreement on whether the verb is af'ala or fa'ala, with the correct view that both are used; al-Mubarrad said: ajartu dari wa-mamluki (without madd) and ajartu fulanan (with madd) meaning I rewarded him.)
Source pages p. 507

Commentary
This passage states the definition of ijarah according to the Hanafi school: it is the sale of a known benefit for a known compensation. The commentary expands, emphasizing that 'sale' here means exchange, not necessarily of property for property, since benefit is not property literally. The benefit must be known in type and amount, and the compensation can be mithli or qimi. The author notes that mentioning 'sale' in the definition implies that ijarah requires offer and acceptance (like sale) and can be concluded by mutual delivery (ta'ati). A practical example is renting unspecified pots: the initial contract is invalid due to variation, but if the renter brings specific pots and the lessor accepts, a new valid contract arises. The footnotes also discuss the linguistic debate on the verb forms, concluding that both أفعل and فاعل are used for 'to rent out', with specific nuances. This definition firmly places ijarah within the category of commutative contracts (uqud mu'awadat) akin to sale.

Key Terms
الإجارة (al-ijarah): The contract of hiring or renting; defined as the sale of a known benefit for a known compensation.
بيع (bay'): Exchange of one thing for another; here used metaphorically for the exchange of benefit for compensation, not literal sale of property.
نفع (naf'): Benefit or utility; the object of the ijarah contract. It must be known (ma'lum) in type and amount.
عوض ('iwad): Compensation or countervalue given in exchange for the benefit in ijarah.
جهالة (jahalah): Uncertainty or ignorance; a defect that invalidates the ijarah contract if it affects the benefit or compensation.
تعاطي (ta'ati): Mutual give-and-take; a method of concluding a contract without verbal offer and acceptance, considered valid in Hanafi law.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of ijarah as a sale of a known benefit for a known compensation underscores its nature as a commutative contract and imposes conditions of knowledge of the benefit and compensation, with offer and acceptance required.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
10 min
Definition of Ijarah: Sale of a Known Benefit
Defines ijarah and clarifies its conditions and scope

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of ijarah, explain why knowledge of benefit and compensation is required for validity, and identify the relied-upon position regarding the contract's attachment to property rather than benefits.

Core Idea
Ijarah is a sale of benefits, not property; its validity requires knowledge of both the benefit and the wage.

This lesson unpacks the foundational definition of ijarah (rental/lease) in the Hanafi school. The passage presents a precise legal definition, proves a key condition from the Sunnah, addresses a conceptual objection, and resolves a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute about the contract's locus. Mastering this definition will equip you to distinguish valid leases from invalid ones and to appreciate how the Hanafi school treats benefits as non-property objects of exchange.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and its components
Read the Arabic definition: 'وهي بيع نفع معلوم بعوض'. Break it into three parts: (1) it is a sale (بيع), (2) of a known benefit (نفع معلوم), (3) for a known compensation (بعوض معلوم). Note that 'sale' here means exchange, not transfer of property, because benefits are not property.
The term 'بيع' is used broadly; ijarah is a sub-type of sale in Hanafi classification.
2
Understand the condition of knowledge and its proof
The text cites the hadith: 'من ستأجر أجيراً فليعلمه أجره' (Whoever hires a worker, let him inform him of his wage). The author argues this implies both wage (compensation) and benefit (the object) must be known, because the benefit is the principal and the wage is secondary. Knowledge prevents dispute.
The hadith is the primary dalil naqli. In Hanafi usul, the imperative 'فليعلمه' indicates obligation (wujub).
3
Analyze the objection and response
An objector says: if this definition is for valid ijarah, it fails to exclude invalid ones; if for general ijarah, the condition of knowledge is misplaced. The author responds: the condition of knowledge is precisely to exclude invalid ijarah due to ignorance, signaling that the Shar'i valid contract is one that avoids dispute.
This objection-and-response is a standard dialectical move in Hanafi texts (i'tirad wa jawab).
4
Examine the locus (mahall) issue
The contract must have a locus. Benefits are non-existent at contract time, so the property (e.g., house) is substituted as the locus for conclusion. However, attaching the contract directly to benefits (e.g., 'I lease you the benefits of this house') is invalid according to the majority (al-Zayla'i, Qadi Khan). Khawahir Zadah permits it.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position follows the majority: attach to the property, not the benefit.

كتاب الإجارة / تعريفها وشروطها وصورها وهي بيع نفع معلوم بعوض
[1] (وهي بيع نفع معلوم بعوض) قوله : وهي بيع نفع ... الخ ؛ يعني إنّ الإجارة بيع منفعة معلومة جنساً وقدراً لعوض مالي، أو نفع من غير جنس المعقود عليه معلوم سواء كان ذلك العوض مثليّاً كالمكيل والموزون، والعددي المتقارب، أو قيمياً كالثياب والدواب وغيرهما. والمراد بالبيع هاهنا مبادلة شيء بشيء، لا مبادلة مال بمال، فإنَّ النفع لا يسمّى مالاً إلا مجازاً، والنفع ما يوصل به الإنسان إلى مطلوب، يقال: نفعني الشيء نفعاً فهو نافع. كذا في «المصباح»، وقال في «الصراح»: نفع : سود وسود كردن، وهو ضد الضرّ، صلة بالباء منفعة، سود مندی. انتهى. فما قال القهستاني : «النفع : المنفعة، وهي عبارة عن اللذة والراحة من دفع الحرّ والبرد وغيرهما». انتهى. لا أثر له في كتب اللغة إلا أن يكون من أفراد مفهومه الكلي. وفي ذكر البيع إشارة إلى أنه لا بد في الإجارة من الإيجاب والقبول كما في البيع، وينعقد بالتعاطي كالبيع، كما إذا استأجر قدوراً بغير عينها ، وأنه لا يجوز للتفاوت بينها من حيث الصغر والكبر، إلا أنه لو جاء بقدور وقبلها على الكراء الأول جاز، إجازة مبتدأة. كما صرح به في «الذخيرة» وغيرها.
وإنما اشترط معلومية أجرة المنافع ؛ لما تقدّم من الحديث، وهو قوله : «من ستأجر أجيراً فليعلمه أجره». فإنه كما يدلُّ بعبارته على اشتراط معلوميّة الأجرة يدلُّ بإشارته على اشتراط كون المنافع معلومة ؛ إذ المعقود عليه في الإجارة هو المنافع وهو الأصل، والمعقود به وهو الأجرة، كالبيع والثمن، فإذا كانت معلومية البيع شرطاً كان معلومية الأصل أولى بذلك ؛ ولأنَّ جهالة الأجرة والمنافع تفضي إلى المنازعة ، كجهالة الثمن والمبيع في عقدِ البيع.
وأورد على هذا التعريف أنه إن كان تعريفاً للإجارة الصحيحة لم يكن مانعاً ؛ لتناوله الفاسدة بالشرط الفاسد، وبالشيوع الأصلي، وإن كان تعريفاً للأعمّ لم يكن تقييد النفع والعوض بالمعلومية صحيحاً.
قلنا : قيد البدلين بالمعلومية لإخراج الإجارة الفاسدة بالجهالة عن التعريف ؛ تنبيهاً على أن المعتبر في الشرع هي الإجارة الغير المفضية إلى النزاع.
اعلم أن عقد الإجارة ينعقد بإقامة العين مقام المنفعة في حق الانعقاد لا في حق الملك ؛ لأنَّ العقد لا بد له من محل ؛ لأنه شرط للصحة لما صرحوا من أن المحال شروط، ومحل العقد هاهنا المنافع، وهي معدومة. والمعدوم لا يصلح محلاً، فجعلت الدار محلاً بإقامتها مقام المنافع ؛ ولهذا لو أضاف العقد إلى المنافع لا يجوز ، بأن قال : أجرتك منافع هذه الدار شهراً هكذا، وإنما يصح بإضافته إلى العين، صرح به الزيلعي (١) ، وابن ملك وغيرهما.
لكن قال قاضي خان في «فتاواه»: ولو قال : أجرت منك منفعة هذه الدار شهراً، كذا ذكر في بعض الروايات أنه لا يجوز، وإنّما تجوزُ الإجارة إذا أضيفت إلى الدار لا إلى المنفعة، وذكر الشيخ الإمام المعروفُ بخواهر زَادَه : إنه إذا أضاف الإجارة إلى المنفعة جاز أيضاً.
Book of Ijarah: Its definition, conditions, and forms. It is a sale of a known benefit for a known compensation. [1] (It is a sale of a known benefit for a known compensation) His statement: 'It is a sale of a known benefit...' means that ijarah is a sale of a benefit known in type and quantity for a financial compensation or a benefit of a different type than the object of contract, known, whether that compensation is fungible (mithli) like mensurable, weighable, and approximately countable items, or non-fungible (qimi) like clothes, animals, and others. The intended meaning of 'sale' here is the exchange of one thing for another, not exchange of property for property, because benefit is not called property except metaphorically. Benefit (naf') is what conveys a person to their desired goal. It is said: 'The thing benefited me (nafani) with benefit, so it is beneficial.' This is in al-Misbah. And in al-Sirah: 'Naf': benefit and benefit-giving, it is the opposite of harm, connected with the letter ba to mean manfa'ah, benefit.' End. So what al-Qahistani said: 'al-Naf': al-manfa'ah, which is expression of pleasure and comfort from repelling heat, cold, etc.' End. This has no basis in language books unless it is among the individuals of its universal concept. And mentioning 'sale' indicates that in ijarah, offer and acceptance are necessary as in sale, and it is concluded by mutual exchange (ta'ati) like sale, as when one leases unspecified pots, and it is not permissible due to variation in smallness and largeness, except that if he brings pots and accepts them on the first hire, it is permissible as a new permission. As clarified in al-Dhakhira and others. The condition that the consideration for benefits be known is due to the hadith mentioned: 'Whoever hires a worker, let him inform him of his wage.' For just as it indicates by its wording the condition of knowledge of the wage, it indicates by its implication the condition of benefits being known, because the object of contract in ijarah is benefits, which is the principal, and the means of contract is the wage, like sale and price. So if knowledge of the price is a condition, then knowledge of the principal is more deserving. And because ignorance of wage and benefits leads to dispute, like ignorance of price and commodity in the contract of sale. An objection was raised against this definition: if it is a definition of valid ijarah, it is not exclusive because it includes invalid ones with invalid conditions and original commonality; and if it is a definition of the general, then restricting benefit and compensation to being known is not correct. We say: the restriction of the two countervalues to being known is to exclude invalid ijarah due to ignorance from the definition, indicating that what is considered in law is ijarah that does not lead to dispute. Know that the contract of ijarah is concluded by substituting the property (ayn) in place of the benefit regarding conclusion, not regarding ownership, because the contract must have a locus (mahall), since it is a condition for validity as they stated that loci are conditions, and the locus of the contract here is benefits, which are non-existent. And the non-existent is not suitable as a locus, so the house is made a locus by substituting it in place of benefits. Hence, if one attaches the contract to benefits, it is not valid, such as saying: 'I lease to you the benefits of this house for a month like this.' Rather, it is valid by attaching it to the property, as stated by al-Zayla'i, Ibn Malik, and others. However, Qadi Khan said in his Fatawa: 'If he said: I lease to you the benefit of this house for a month, it is mentioned in some narrations that it is not valid, and ijarah is only valid when attached to the house, not to the benefit.' And the Shaykh al-Imam known as Khawahir Zadah mentioned that if he attaches ijarah to the benefit, it is also permissible.
Source pages p. 507

Commentary
This passage opens the book of Ijarah (rental/lease law) in the Hanafi madhhab by providing a comprehensive definition and discussing its conditions. The author defines ijarah as 'the sale of a known benefit for a known compensation.' This is a ruling statement, as it lays down the essential nature of the contract. The commentary then unpacks each element: 'sale' here does not mean the transfer of property (mal) but rather an exchange of something for something else, since benefits are not legally considered property except metaphorically. The benefit must be known in type and quantity, and the compensation must be known as well. This is proven by the hadith: 'Whoever hires a worker, let him inform him of his wage,' which indicates by its wording the knowledge of wage and by implication the knowledge of the benefit, since the benefit is the primary subject matter. The condition of knowledge for both countervalues is to prevent disputes, similar to the sale contract. An objection is raised that if this definition is for valid ijarah, it fails to exclude invalid ijarah (e.g., those with invalid conditions or general shares). The response is that the condition of knowledge is precisely to exclude invalid ijarah due to ignorance, thereby clarifying that the valid contract is one that avoids disputes. Finally, the passage addresses the technicality of the contract's locus: since the actual benefits are non-existent at the time of contract, the property (e.g., house) is substituted as the locus for conclusion. However, a difference of opinion arises: the majority (al-Zayla'i, Ibn Malik, Qadi Khan) hold that the contract must be attached to the property itself, not to the benefits. Khawahir Zadah, however, permits attaching it to the benefits. This intra-Hanafi dispute, though later in the text, shows that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the majority view, as the contract's validity depends on a tangible object at the time of agreement.

Key Terms
إجارة (ijārah): A contract for the sale of a known benefit for a known compensation, as defined in the text.
نفع (naf‘): Benefit or utility that is the object of contract in ijarah, such as residing in a house or riding an animal.
عوض (‘iwaḍ): Compensation paid in exchange for the benefit, which can be fungible (mithli) or non-fungible (qimi).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition, what is ijarah?
A) A sale of a physical object.
B) A sale of a known benefit for a known compensation.
C) A gift of a benefit.
D) A loan of an object.

Key Takeaway
Ijarah is a sale of benefits, requiring knowledge of both benefit and wage to avoid dispute, and the contract is attached to the property, not directly to benefits.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

6 min
Condition of Knowledge of Compensation and Usufruct in Ijarah
Establishes the condition of knowledge for both parties in Ijarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that both the compensation (ujrah) and the usufruct (manfa'ah) must be known in an ijarah contract, and explain the proof from the hadith and the analogy to sale.

Core Idea
Ijarah requires known wage and known benefit; ignorance invalidates the contract.

This lesson examines a key condition for the validity of an ijarah (hire) contract in the Hanafi school. The author establishes that both the compensation (ajr) and the usufruct (manfa'ah) must be clearly known to both parties. He provides proof from a hadith and an analogy to sale, and then addresses an objection to this definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Recognize that the passage explicitly requires knowledge (ma'lumiyyah) of both the hire (ajr) and the usufruct (manafi') for a valid ijarah contract.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith: 'Whoever hires a worker, let him inform him of his wage.' Note that this is a direct textual proof (dalil naqli).
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), so the obligation (wujub) it indicates is also zanni.
3
Understand the implication (isharah)
The author argues that while the hadith's wording ('ibarah) explicitly requires knowledge of the wage, its implication (isharah) also requires knowledge of the usufruct, because the usufruct is the actual object of the contract (ma'qud 'alayh).
This is a Hanafi usul principle: the explicit text implies the conditions of the subject matter.
4
Follow the analogy to sale
The author compares ijarah to sale: in sale, both the price (thaman) and the sold item (muthman) must be known; similarly, in ijarah, both the hire (ujrah) and the usufruct (manfa'ah) must be known. Knowledge of the principal (usufruct) is even more necessary.
This is a qiyas (analogical reasoning) that reinforces the condition.
5
Analyze the objection and response
An objection is raised: if the definition is for valid ijarah, it includes invalid ones with unknown terms; if for general ijarah, knowledge is not a universal condition. The author replies that the restriction to knowledge is intended to exclude ijarah that leads to dispute, emphasizing that Shari'ah aims for dispute-free contracts.
This clarifies that the condition is specifically to prevent jahalah that causes conflict.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما اشترط معلومية أجرة المنافع ؛ لما تقدّم من الحديث، وهو قوله : «من ستأجر أجيراً فليعلمه أجره». فإنه كما يدلُّ بعبارته على اشتراط معلوميّة الأجرة يدلُّ بإشارته على اشتراط كون المنافع معلومة ؛ إذ المعقود عليه في الإجارة هو المنافع وهو الأصل، والمعقود به وهو الأجرة، كالبيع والثمن، فإذا كانت معلومية البيع شرطاً كان معلومية الأصل أولى بذلك ؛ ولأنَّ جهالة الأجرة والمنافع تفضي إلى المنازعة ، كجهالة الثمن والمبيع في عقدِ البيع. وأورد على هذا التعريف أنه إن كان تعريفاً للإجارة الصحيحة لم يكن مانعاً ؛ لتناوله الفاسدة بالشرط الفاسد، وبالشيوع الأصلي، وإن كان تعريفاً للأعمّ لم يكن تقييد النفع والعوض بالمعلومية صحيحاً. قلنا : قيد البدلين بالمعلومية لإخراج الإجارة الفاسدة بالجهالة عن التعريف ؛ تنبيهاً على أن المعتبر في الشرع هي الإجارة الغير المفضية إلى النزاع.
The condition of knowledge of the hire of usufructs is stipulated because of the hadith mentioned earlier, which is his saying: 'Whoever hires a worker, let him inform him of his wage.' For just as its wording indicates the condition of knowledge of the hire, its implication indicates the condition of the usufructs being known, since the object of the contract in ijarah is the usufructs (al-manafi'), which is the principal (al-asl), and the subject of the contract (the hire) like the sale and its price. Thus, if knowledge of the sale is a condition, then knowledge of the principal is more deserving of that. And because ignorance of the hire and the usufructs leads to dispute, like ignorance of the price and the sold item in the contract of sale. An objection was raised against this definition: if it is a definition of valid ijarah, it is not restrictive (mani') because it includes the invalid ijarah with an invalid condition and with original commonality; if it is a definition of the general term, the restriction of the benefit and the countervalue to knowledge is not correct. We say: the restriction of the two counterparts to knowledge is to exclude invalid ijarah due to ignorance from the definition, as a hint that what is considered in the Shari'ah is the ijarah that does not lead to dispute.
Source pages p. 508

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof discussing the condition that both the compensation and the usufruct must be known in an ijarah contract. The author cites a hadith: 'Whoever hires a worker, let him inform him of his wage.' He then uses an analogy to sale, arguing that knowledge of the principal (usufruct) is even more important than knowledge of the price. The objection and response clarify that the definition is intended to exclude invalid ijarah caused by ignorance, not all invalid forms.

Key Terms
أجرة (ujrah): The compensation paid in an ijarah contract, which must be known (ma'lum) for validity.
منفعة (manfa'ah): The usufruct or benefit derived from an asset in ijarah, which is the actual object of the contract (معقود عليه).
جهالة (jahalah): Ignorance of essential terms (compensation or usufruct) that leads to dispute and invalidates the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in the passage, what is the condition for hiring a worker?
A) The worker must be Muslim
B) The worker must be informed of his wage
C) The work must be specified in detail
D) The wage must be paid in advance

Key Takeaway
For a valid ijarah contract under Hanafi fiqh, both the compensation and the usufruct must be known to prevent dispute.

The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute on Ijarah Formation: Adding to Asset or Usufruct?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ijarah formation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority position on ijarah formation, identify the minority view, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).

Core Idea
Ijarah must be added to the asset, not the usufruct — but a later Hanafi minority allows it by istihsan.

This passage delves into a nuanced dispute within the Hanafi school: is the ijarah contract formed by linking it to the physical asset ('ayn) or directly to the usufruct (manfa'ah)? The majority holds that the usufruct is non-existent at contract time, so the asset serves as a constructive subject matter. However, some later Hanafi authorities, citing istihsan, permit adding the contract to the usufruct. Understanding this dispute sharpens your grasp of contractual formation (in'iqad) and the role of fictional constructs in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The dispute is about formation (in'iqad) of ijarah: must the contract be added to the physical asset or directly to the usufruct?
This affects validity, not ownership.
2
Understand the majority's reasoning
The majority (al-Zayla'i, Ibn Malik, Qadi Khan) argue that the usufruct is non-existent (ma'dum) at contract time, so it cannot be a valid subject matter (mahall). The asset is substituted (iqamah al-'ayn maqam al-manfa'ah) only for formation, not for ownership.
This is a special legal construct to allow ijarah despite the non-existence of usufruct.
3
Examine the minority's counter-argument
Khwaharzadah and Sahib al-Bahr argue that adding to the usufruct is permissible, citing a precedent from al-Kitab where a gift of usufruct (hibat al-manfa'ah) for a month for a dirham is valid. They also note that usufruct can be known by specifying duration.
They rely on istihsan (juristic preference) over qiyas.
4
Analyze the majority's response
The majority distinguish ijarah from gift: in a gift of usufruct, ownership of the usufruct is transferred, whereas ijarah is a hire contract that requires the asset as the subject matter for formation. The gift analogy is thus inapplicable.
The gift of usufruct is a transfer of ownership (tamlik), not a contract for hire.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a contract phrased 'I lease to you the usufruct of this house for a month' is invalid according to the majority, but valid according to the minority. The mufta bihi is the majority view.
Most Hanafi fatwa works follow the majority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم أن عقد الإجارة ينعقد بإقامة العين مقام المنفعة في حق الانعقاد لا في حق الملك ; لأنَّ العقد لا بد له من محل ; لأنه شرط للصحة لما صرحوا من أن المحال شروط، ومحل العقد هاهنا المنافع، وهي معدومة. والمعدوم لا يصلح محلاً، فجعلت الدار محلاً بإقامتها مقام المنافع ; ولهذا لو أضاف العقد إلى المنافع لا يجوز ، بأن قال : أجرتك منافع هذه الدار شهراً هكذا، وإنما يصح بإضافته إلى العين، صرح به الزيلعي (١) ، وابن ملك وغيرهما. لكن قال قاضي خان في «فتاواه»: ولو قال : أجرت منك منفعة هذه الدار شهراً، كذا ذكر في بعض الروايات أنه لا يجوز، وإنّما تجوزُ الإجارة إذا أضيفت إلى الدار لا إلى المنفعة، وذكر الشيخ الإمام المعروفُ بخواهر زَادَه : إنه إذا أضاف الإجارة إلى المنفعة جاز أيضاً. كذلك دين أو عين، ويُعْلَمُ النفعُ : بذِكْرِ المدَّةِ كسكنى الدار، وزراعة الأرض مدة، كذا طالت أو قصرت. فإنه ذكر في «الكتاب»: إنه لو قال : وهبتُ منك منفعة هذه الدار شهراً بدرهم جاز، وإنما لا يجوز إذا أضاف البيع إلى منفعة الدار ; لأنَّ الإجارة لا تنعقد بلفظ البيع». انتهى. وقال صاحب «البحر»: «إضافةُ الإجارة إلى منافع الدار جائزة». انتهى.
Know that the contract of ijarah is concluded by putting the asset ('ayn) in the place of the usufruct (manfa'ah) in terms of formation (in'iqad) not in terms of ownership (milk), because a contract must have a subject matter (mahall) since it is a condition for validity as they stated that subject matters are conditions. The subject matter here is the usufructs, which are non-existent (ma'dum). And the non-existent is not suitable as a subject matter, so the house is made a subject matter by putting it in the place of the usufructs. For this reason, if he adds the contract to the usufructs, it is not permissible, such as saying: 'I have leased to you the usufructs of this house for a month thusly'; rather it is valid only by adding it to the asset ('ayn), as stated by al-Zayla'i and Ibn Malik and others. But Qadi Khan said in his Fatawa: 'If he said: I have leased to you the usufruct of this house for a month, thus it is mentioned in some narrations that it is not permissible, and ijarah is only valid if added to the house not to the usufruct.' And the scholar known as Khwaharzadah mentioned that if he adds the ijarah to the usufruct, it is also permissible. Similarly (the compensation must be known as) a debt or a specific item. And the usufruct is known by mentioning the duration, such as renting a house for dwelling, and land for cultivation for a specified period, be it long or short. For it is mentioned in 'al-Kitab' that if he said: I have gifted to you the usufruct of this house for a month for a dirham, it is permissible, but not if he added the sale to the usufruct of the house, because ijarah is not concluded with the word of sale. End quote. And the author of al-Bahr said: 'Adding the ijarah to the usufructs of the house is permissible.' End quote.
Source pages p. 508

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the formation of the ijarah contract. The majority view (al-Zayla'i, Ibn Malik) holds that the contract must be added to the asset (e.g., 'I rent you this house') because the usufruct is non-existent at the time of contract, so the asset serves as a constructive subject matter. Qadi Khan agrees. However, Khwaharzadah and the author of al-Bahr allow adding the contract directly to the usufruct, citing a precedent from al-Kitab where a gift of usufruct for a specific compensation is valid. The passage also mentions that the compensation can be a debt or a specific item, and the usufruct is known by specifying the duration.

Key Terms
محل العقد (mahall al-'aqd): The subject matter of the contract; for ijarah, ideally the usufruct, but because it is non-existent, the asset is treated as the subject matter for formation.
إقامة العين مقام المنفعة (iqamah al-'ayn maqam al-manfa'ah): The legal construct where the asset (e.g., house) is treated as the subject matter of the contract instead of the actual usufruct, but only for the purpose of formation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view in the passage, how must the ijarah contract be phrased to be valid?
A) 'I lease to you the usufruct of this house'
B) 'I lease to you this house'
C) 'I gift to you the usufruct of this house'
D) 'I sell to you the usufruct of this house'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi majority requires that the ijarah contract be added to the asset, not the usufruct, to ensure a valid subject matter; a minority allows addition to the usufruct by istihsan.
