Hanafi Refutation of Shafi'i on Deferred Wages in Ijara
Hanafi refutation of Shafi'i's legal fiction in ijara

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rejects the Shafi'i argument that non-existent benefits can be treated as existent in hire contracts, and state the Hanafi alternative principle of making the cause stand in place of the effect.

Core Idea
The non-existent benefit is not made existent; rather the existing asset stands in its place by a known Shari'ah principle.

In this passage, the author responds to a Shafi'i argument that the Lawgiver sometimes treats non-existent things as existent, so the same should apply to usufruct in hire. The Hanafi response is careful and principled: usufructs are accidents that cannot be contracted upon at all, so the contract attaches to the asset itself. This avoids a legal fiction that would invert realities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والشارع جعل المعدوم حقيقة موجوداً حكماً ، كما جعل النطفة في الرحم كالحي في حق الأحكام من الوصية والإرث ، وكذا يجعلُ الموجود حقيقة كالمعدوم حكماً ، كما يجعل المرتد الملتحق بدار الحرب ميتاً في حق الأحكام كالإرث وعتق أمهات أولاده، والدليل على أنه كالموجود جواز الاستئجار بالدين، ولو كان معدوماً لما جاز ؛ لأنه يصير ديناً بدين، وهو حرام شرعاً.
ولنا : إنّ هذا عقد معاوضة فيقتضي المساواة بينهما، وذلك بتقابل البدلين في الملك والتسليم وأحد البدلين وهو المنفعة، لم تصر مملوكة بنفس العقد ؛ لاستحالة ثبوتِ الملك فكذا في البدل الآخر، ولو ملك الأجرة لملكها بغير بدل، وهو ليس من قضيّة المعاوضة، فتأخر الملك فيه ضرورة.
وجواز العقد ليس باعتبار أن المعدوم جعل موجوداً حكماً، وكيف يقال ذلك والموجودُ من المنفعة لا يقبلُ العقد ؛ لأنه عرض لا يبقى زمانين ، فلا يتصور فيه التسليم، فلا يكون محلاً للعقد.
بل باعتبار أن العين التي هي سبب وجودِ المنفعة أقيمت مقام المنفعة في حق صحة الإيجاب والقبول، وفي حق وجوب التسليم ؛ إذ العين هي التي يمكن تسليمهما دون العرض، فإنعقد في حقها في الحال فوجب عليه تسليمها.
وصار العقد مضافاً غير منعقد للحال في حق المنفعة ؛ لأنَّ أقصى ما يتصور العقد على المنفعة أن يكون العقد مضافاً إلى وقت حدوثها ، فينعقد العقد في كل جزء من المنفعة على حسب وجودها شيئاً فشيئاً، وهو معنى قولنا : إنَّ عقد الإجارة في حكم عقود متفرّقة يتجدّد انعقادها على حسب حدوث المنافع.
وإنما قامت العين مقامَ المنفعة تصحيحاً للعقد في حق الانعقاد، والتسليم ضرورة عدم تصورهما في المنفعة، ولا ضرورةً في حق الملك في البدل إذما يثبت للضرورة يثبتُ بقدرها، فلا يظهر في حق ملك البدل، كما لا يظهرُ في حق ملك المنفعة، فكذا العقد مضافاً إلى وقت حدوثها، غير منعقد للحال في حقهما.
وهذا أولى من الذي ذهب إليه الشافعي رحمه الله فإنّ فيه قلب الحقائق، وهو جعل المعدوم موجوداً، وما ذهبنا إليه ليس فيه إلا إقامة السبب وهو العين مقامَ المسبب وهي المنفعة في حق بعض الأحكام، وهذا القدر من التغيير معهود في الشرع، ألا ترى أنَّ الشارع أقام السفر مقام المشقة ؛ لأنه سببها ، وأقام البلوغ مقام اعتدال العقل، حتى علق التكليف به ؛ لأنه سببه، وقس على هذا.
وإنما جاز الاستئجار بالدين لأنَّ العقد لم ينعقد في حق المنفعة، فلم تصر المنفعة ديناً في ذمته فلا يجب بدلها أيضاً، وعند انعقاد العقد فيها وهو زمان حدوثها تصير هي مقبوضة، فلا يكون ديناً بدين أصلاً ، ولو كان العقد منعقداً لما جازت الإجارة بالدين المؤجل أصلاً، كما لا يجوز السلم، ولو جاز أن يجعل المعدوم كالمستوفى لجاز ذلك في السّلم أيضاً، كما إذا باع العين بالدين. فإذا استوفى المنفعة ثبت الملك في الإجارة، لتحقق المساواة التي اقتضاها العقد، فصح بخلاف الإجارة المضافة إلى وقت بشرط تعجيل الأجرة، حيث يكون الشرط باطلاً، ولا يلزمه للحال شيء ؛ لأنّ امتناع وجوب الأجرة ليس بمقتضى العقد، بل بالتصريح بالإضافة إلى وقت في المستقبل، والمضاف إلى وقت لا يكون موجوداً قبل ذلك الوقت، فلا يتغير هذا المعنى بالشرط.
وفيما نحن فيه إنما يجب لاقتضاء العقدِ للمساواة، وليس بمضاف صريحاً، فبطل ذلك المعنى بالتصريح على خلافه، ألا ترى أنَّ الثمن في المبيع يجب في الحال، ولا يجب تسليم المبيع حتى يُسَلِّمَ الثمن ؛ لأنَّ العقد يقتضي المساواة، ثمّ إذا كان الثمن مؤجلاً يجب تسليمه في الحال ؛ لأنه تأخر بالقصد صريحاً.
وما قال الشافعي رحمه الله من أنَّ الشارع جعل المعدوم حقيقة موجودا حكماً ... الخ، فجوابه : أَنه مُسَلَّم، لكنَّ البحث هاهنا فيما يمكن تقدير وجوده حقيقة ؛ لأنَّ الشيء إنما يُقَدَّرُ حكماً إذا كان يمكن تصويره حقيقة، كما في المستشهد به ، فإنّ الحي يتصور موتُه ، وكذا بالعكس، وأما المنافع فلا تقبل العقد أصلاً كما لا يخفى، ذكره الزَّيْلَعِيُّ ) وغيره.
(۱) في «التبيين»(٥ : ١٠٧ - ١٠٨).
The Lawgiver made the non-existent in reality existent by legal ruling, just as He made the sperm-drop in the womb like a living person regarding rulings of bequest and inheritance, and likewise He makes the existent in reality like non-existent by legal ruling, as He makes the apostate who joins the land of war dead regarding rulings like inheritance and freeing of umm walad. Evidence that it is like existent is the permissibility of hiring with a debt, and if it were non-existent it would not be permissible because it would be debt for debt, which is unlawful by Shari'ah. Our argument: This is a commutative contract requiring equality between the two parties, which is by exchange of the two counterparts in ownership and delivery. One of the two counterparts, which is the usufruct, does not become owned by the contract itself because it is impossible to establish ownership [of a non-existent]. Likewise for the other counterpart, and if he owned the wage he would own it without a counterpart, which is not from the nature of commutative contract, so ownership is necessarily delayed. The validity of the contract is not based on the non-existent being made existent by ruling. How can that be said when the existent part of the usufruct does not accept the contract because it is an accident that does not remain for two moments, so delivery cannot be conceived, so it is not a locus for the contract. Rather, it is based on the fact that the object (al-ayn), which is the cause of the existence of the usufruct, is made to stand in place of the usufruct regarding the validity of offer and acceptance and regarding the obligation of delivery, because the object can be delivered unlike the accident. So the contract is concluded with respect to it immediately, so delivery of it becomes obligatory. And the contract becomes annexed (mudaf) and not concluded immediately with respect to the usufruct, because the utmost that can be conceived of a contract on usufruct is that the contract be annexed to the time of its occurrence, so the contract is concluded for each part of the usufruct according to its existence gradually. That is the meaning of our statement: The contract of hire is, in effect, multiple contracts whose conclusion is renewed according to the occurrence of the benefits. The object only stands in place of the usufruct to validate the contract with respect to conclusion and delivery, due to the necessity of the impossibility of these in the usufruct, and there is no necessity regarding ownership of the counterpart because what is established by necessity is established to its extent, so it does not appear regarding ownership of the counterpart, just as it does not appear regarding ownership of the usufruct. So likewise the contract, being annexed to the time of occurrence, is not concluded immediately with respect to both. And this is better than the view held by al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, for it involves inversion of realities, which is making the non-existent existent. Our view only involves making the cause (the object) stand in place of the effect (the usufruct) regarding some rulings, and this amount of modification is customary in the Shari'ah. Do you not see that the Lawgiver made travel stand in place of hardship because it is its cause, and made puberty stand in place of soundness of intellect, so He attached obligation to it because it is its cause? And analogize to this. Hiring with a debt is only permissible because the contract is not concluded with respect to the usufruct, so the usufruct does not become a debt in his liability, so its counterpart also is not obligatory. And at the time of the contract's conclusion with respect to it, which is the time of its occurrence, it becomes delivered, so it is not debt for debt at all. If the contract were concluded [immediately], hiring with deferred debt would not be permissible at all, just as salam is not permissible. And if it were permissible to treat the non-existent as if received, that would also be permissible in salam, as when one sells a specific object for a debt. When the usufruct is received, ownership becomes established in the hire due to the realization of equality required by the contract, so it is valid, unlike a hire contract annexed to a future time with a condition of immediate payment of the wage, where the condition is void and nothing is incumbent on him immediately, because the prevention of obligation of the wage is not by requirement of the contract but by explicit specification of annexation to a future time, and what is annexed to a time does not exist before that time, so this meaning is not changed by the condition. In our case, the [wage] is obligatory only by the contract's requirement of equality, and it is not explicitly annexed, so that meaning is invalidated by explicit stipulation to the contrary. Do you not see that the price in a sale is obligatory immediately, and delivery of the sold item is not obligatory until he delivers the price, because the contract requires equality. Then if the price is deferred, delivery of the sold item becomes obligatory immediately because it [the price] is delayed by explicit intent. As for what al-Shafi'i said, that the Lawgiver made the non-existent in reality existent by ruling etc., the response is that it is conceded, but the inquiry here concerns what can be estimated to exist in reality, because a thing is only estimated by ruling if its real existence can be conceived, as in the examples cited: a living person can be conceived to die, and vice versa. However, usufructs do not accept the contract at all, as is not hidden. Al-Zayla'i and others mentioned this.
Source pages p. 514

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the legal basis for the validity of deferred wages in a hire contract (ijara). The author presents the Shafi'i argument that the Lawgiver treats non-existent entities as existent by legal fiction (such as treating sperm as alive for inheritance), and then uses this to argue that hiring with a deferred debt is permissible because the non-existent benefit is treated as existent for the purpose of the contract. The Hanafi response is detailed: they argue that the hire contract is a commutative contract requiring equality, but since usufruct (manfa'a) is an accident that does not persist, it cannot be owned or delivered immediately. Instead, the contract is attached to the object (al-ayn) which is the cause of the benefit, not the benefit itself. This avoids the legal fiction of treating non-existent as existent. The contract is considered as multiple contracts renewed as benefits accrue. The Hanafis further argue that making the cause stand in place of the effect is a common principle in Shari'ah (like travel standing for hardship). The passage ends with a critique of the Shafi'i view as an inversion of realities and reaffirms the Hanafi position that it is more consistent with legal principles.

Key Terms
معدوم موجود حكماً (ma'dūm mawjūd hukman): Something that does not exist in reality but is treated as existent by legal ruling for specific purposes, as in the Shafi'i argument.
المنفعة (al-manfa'a): Usufruct or benefit derived from an asset; an accident that does not persist over two moments, hence cannot be delivered or owned at the time of contract.
العين (al-ʻayn): The actual physical asset (corporeal property) that generates the usufruct; it serves as the locus for the contract in hire.
إقامة السبب مقام المسبب (iqāmat al-sabab maqām al-musabbab): A legal principle where the cause (sabab) is made to stand in place of the effect (musabbab) for some rulings, used by Hanafis to justify attaching the contract to the asset.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is it permissible to hire with a deferred debt (al-istījār bil-dayn)?
A) Because the non-existent benefit is treated as existent by legal fiction.
B) Because the contract attaches to the existing asset (al-ayn) which is the cause of the benefit, and the benefit is considered gradually.
C) Because the wage is due immediately even if the benefit is deferred.
D) Because deferred debt is always permissible in commutative contracts.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates deferred wages in ijara by attaching the contract to the existing asset, not by treating non-existent benefits as existent.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate

Hanafi Rebuttal of Shafi'i on Ijarah with Deferred Payment
Inter-madhhab dispute: rebuttal of Shafi'i on ijarah with deferred debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rebuttal to the Shafi'i argument against ijarah with deferred payment, identifying the key usul principles involved.

Core Idea
Hiring with deferred payment is valid because the contract does not make the benefit a debt; equivalence is achieved upon receipt, not at inception.

In this passage, the Hanafi school defends the validity of ijarah (hire) when the rent is paid on a deferred basis, responding to the Shafi'i claim that this involves an inversion of realities. The argument hinges on the nature of benefits as non-existent at the time of contract and the limited scope of the Shari'ah principle that treats non-existent as existent in effect.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: ijarah with deferred payment is valid. The contract does not conclude on the benefit at the moment, so the benefit does not become a debt in the hirer's liability.
The Hanafi view is that the contract is concluded on the substance (the asset), not the benefit directly.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
The Shafi'i school argues that this involves qalb al-haqaiq (inversion of realities) by making a non-existent benefit the object of a contract, which is impermissible.
The objection is based on the principle that non-existent things cannot be subjects of contracts.
3
Follow the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'is cite the general Shari'ah principle that the Lawgiver sometimes treats non-existent as existent in effect (e.g., travel treated as hardship, puberty as sound mind).
They extend this to benefits in ijarah.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis concede the principle but limit its application: it only applies where the non-existent can be imagined as existent in reality (e.g., a living person can be imagined dead). Benefits, being non-corporeal and gradually realized, cannot be imagined as existent at contract inception.
Thus, the analogy fails, and ijarah with deferred payment remains valid.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis permit ijarah with deferred payment; Shafi'is prohibit it. This affects many rental agreements where payment is delayed.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

And this is more appropriate than the view of Imam al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, for it involves an inversion of realities, making the non-existent existent. Our view only involves establishing the cause—the substance—in place of the effect—the benefit—in respect of some rulings, and this degree of alteration is known in the Shari'ah. Do you not see that the Lawgiver has established travel in place of hardship because it is its cause, and has established puberty in place of soundness of mind, even attaching obligation to it because it is its cause. Measure similarly. Hiring with debt is permitted only because the contract is not concluded in respect of the benefit, so the benefit does not become a debt in his liability, nor is its equivalent owed. At the conclusion of the contract in respect of it—the time of its occurrence—it becomes received, so there is no debt for debt at all. If the contract were concluded, hiring with deferred debt would not be allowed at all, just as salam is not allowed. And if one were permitted to treat the non-existent as received, that would also be allowed in salam, as when selling a substance for debt. When the benefit is received, ownership is established in ijarah because the equivalence required by the contract is realized, so it is valid, unlike a contract of ijarah added to a time with the condition of immediate payment, where the condition is void and nothing is incumbent immediately; because the prevention of the obligation of rent is not by the requirement of the contract, but by the explicit addition to a future time, and what is added to a time does not exist before that time, so this meaning is not changed by the condition. Because the contract requires equivalence, then if the price is deferred, delivery of the sold item is required immediately because it is explicitly delayed by intention. Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the validity of hiring (ijarah) with deferred payment (debt). The Hanafi position, as presented, is that it is valid. The author rebuts the Shafi'i objection that it involves treating non-existent (the benefit) as existent, which would be an inversion of realities. The Hanafi response is that the Shari'ah does allow treating a cause as an effect in some contexts, such as travel being treated as hardship, or puberty as soundness of mind. However, this treatment is limited and does not extend to all cases. The Hanafis argue that in ijarah, the contract is not concluded with respect to the benefit at the moment; rather, the benefit is realized over time. Therefore, making the benefit a debt in the lessee's liability is not necessary. The key point is that equivalence (musawah) between payment and benefit is only achieved when the benefit is actually received or the lessee has the ability to receive it. The author also distinguishes ijarah from salam (forward sale), showing consistency in Hanafi rulings. The passage ends with a further response: the Shafi'i claim that the Shari' makes the non-existent existent in effect is accepted, but only where the non-existent can be imagined as existent—death of a living person, for example. Benefits, however, cannot be subject to a contract in their non-existent state, so the analogy fails. This is a classic Hanafi argument based on rational analysis and analogical reasoning (qiyas).

Key Terms
قلب الحقائق (qalb al-haqaiq): In the context of this dispute, it refers to the Shafi'i claim that hiring with deferred payment involves inverting the natural order by treating a non-existent benefit as if it were existent.
إقامة السبب مقام المسبب (iqamat al-sabab maqam al-musabbab): The Shari'ah principle of treating a cause as having the same ruling as its effect in certain contexts, e.g., travel (cause) is treated as hardship (effect) for concessions.
المعدوم (al-ma'dum): That which is non-existent; the benefit in ijarah at the time of contract is non-existent.
المنفعة (al-manfa'ah): The benefit or usufruct that is the object of the ijarah contract, which is non-existent at the time of contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi rebuttal, why is the Shafi'i objection that hiring with deferred payment involves 'قلب الحقائق' (inversion of realities) not valid?
A) Because the Shari'ah never treats a cause as an effect.
B) Because the benefit in ijarah is actually existent at the time of contract.
C) Because the Shari'ah only treats non-existent as existent when it can be imagined as existent, and benefits cannot be imagined as existent at the time of contract.
D) Because the Hanafi view is based on a stronger hadith.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates ijarah with deferred payment because the contract does not require the benefit to be a debt at inception; the Shari'ah's treatment of non-existent as existent is limited to cases where the non-existent can be imagined.

When Does Rent Become Wajib? The Four Conditions in Hanafi Ijarah
Explaining the conditions that make the rent wajib in an ijarah contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions that make rent wajib in Hanafi ijarah and apply them to determine when rent is due versus not due.

Core Idea
Rent becomes wajib upon prepayment, stipulation, actual use, or even mere ability to use.

In Hanafi fiqh, the obligation of rent in an ijarah contract is not automatic upon signing. The rent only becomes due when equivalence (musawah) between payment and benefit is realized. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains four distinct ways this equivalence is achieved: prepayment, stipulation, actual utilization, or having the ability to utilize. Understanding these conditions is critical for determining when the lessee must pay.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four conditions
Read the matn: 'بل بتعجيلها أو بشرطه أو باستيفاء النفع أو التمكن منه'. List the four ways rent becomes wajib: prepayment, stipulation, actual use, ability to use.
These are exhaustive in the Hanafi school for immediate rent obligation.
2
Understand the principle of musawah
The commentary explains that the contract requires equivalence between payment and benefit. Prepayment or stipulation of prepayment nullifies the need for equivalence, making rent due immediately.
Musawah is the key conceptual basis.
3
Distinguish actual use from ability to use
Actual use (istifa') means physically benefiting from the hired item. Ability to use (tamkin) means the lessor delivered the item without any obstruction, and the lessee could have used it. The Hanafi school treats ability as equivalent to actual use for rent obligation.
Sub-rulings: inside vs outside city hire differ because ability is not complete until the animal is taken out of the city.
4
Apply the rulings to scenarios
Consider cases: (a) prepayment of rent → immediate, non-refundable. (b) Stipulation of prepayment in contract → same effect. (c) Lessee actually rides the horse within the period → rent due. (d) Lessor delivers empty house but lessee never moves in → rent due due to ability.
Note exceptions: if lessor fails to deliver, or there is an external obstacle (usurper, ruler), rent is not due.

This is restricted to when he utilizes within the period. If he mentioned a period and distance and rode to that place after the period has passed, the rent is not obligatory. If he did not utilize but kept her in his house and the period passed, if he hired her to ride outside the city, the rent is not obligatory; if inside the city, the rent is obligatory. If she perishes in the first case, he is liable for misuse [ta'addi] by detention, unlike the second. Mentioned by 'Allamah al-Tahtawi. (3) His statement: 'Or ability to utilize' means: using the ability to take benefit from something as a substitute for that thing. So if he hands it over empty of his belongings, with no obstacle from himself or from a foreigner, ruler, or usurper, then he has the ability, and leaving utilization then is negligence, so it does not prevent the rent from being due. If he did not hand over, or it was not empty, or he handed over empty outside the period or within it, but detained it outside the place of hire or in it, and she has a valid excuse or not, and prevented by ruler or usurpation, or the hire was invalid, then no rent, as stated by al-Hamawi and others. (3) [4] His statement: 'So it becomes obligatory... etc.' means: so the rent is obligatory if the lessee took possession of the house and did not inhabit it, until the period passed; because since the delivery of the benefit itself is not conceivable, delivery of its place is established in its place, for the ability to benefit is proved by it. Mentioned in Majma' al-Anhur reporting from al-Nawazil: 'If he hires... (1) In its commentary on al-Durr al-Mukhtar (4:7). (2) See: Hashiyat al-Tahtawi (4:7).
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the conditions that obligate the rent (ujrah) in an ijarah contract. The matn states that rent becomes obligatory by four means: (1) actual prepayment (ta'jil) by the lessee, (2) stipulation of prepayment in the contract, (3) actual utilization of the benefit (istifa'), and (4) having the ability to utilize (tamkin) even without actual use. The commentary clarifies each. For prepayment: if the lessee prepays, the rent is due immediately and cannot be refunded, because prepayment nullifies the contract's requirement of equivalence (musawah) that would otherwise delay payment. For utilization: if the lessee actually uses the property within the contracted period, rent is due. The sub-ruling distinguishes between hiring an animal for travel outside the city versus inside: if the animal is not used and kept in the stable, rent is not due for outside hire because the ability to benefit is not complete until the animal is taken out; for inside hire, the ability exists simply by taking possession, so rent is due. The commentary also addresses the ability to utilize: if the lessor hands over the property empty and no obstacle exists (no usurper, ruler preventing, etc.), the lessee has the ability, and failure to use does not excuse the rent. If the lessor fails to deliver, or delivers but the lessee is prevented by external factors, no rent is due. This passage is typical of Hanafi fiqh works, showing detailed case analysis and deriving rulings from the principle of equivalence in commutative contracts.

Key Terms
تعجيل الأجرة (ta'jil al-ujrah): Prepayment of the rent by the lessee; if done, the rent becomes immediately due and non-refundable.
استيفاء النفع (istifa' al-manfa'ah): Actual utilization of the benefit (e.g., riding the hired animal, living in the house) within the contracted period.
التمكن من الانتفاع (al-tamakkin min al-intifa'): The lessee's ability to utilize the hired property without any obstruction, even if they do not actually use it.
المساواة (al-musawah): The equivalence or balance between the payment (ujrah) and the benefit (manfa'ah) required by the contract; when prepayment or ability occurs, this equivalence is achieved.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person hires a horse to ride outside the city but keeps it in the stable for the entire period, does rent become wajib?
A) Yes, because hiring a horse for outside travel implies immediate ability to ride.
B) No, because for outside hire, mere possession does not give complete ability to utilize until the animal is actually taken out.
C) Yes, because the lessee has the ability to utilize by taking possession.
D) No, because the horse was not used at all.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijarah, rent becomes wajib through four means: prepayment, stipulation, actual use, or ability to use – the latter being a distinctive Hanafi position.

When the Wage in Ijarah Becomes Due and When It Is Lost
Expansion of wage triggers and loss in ijarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions that trigger wage obligation in Hanafi ijarah and apply the rulings to scenarios involving delivery, ability to use (tamakkun), and usurpation (ghasb).

Core Idea
In Hanafi ijarah, the wage becomes due upon ability to use, not just actual use, and drops proportionally when ability is lost.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains the precise moments when the wage becomes obligatory in an ijarah contract and when it is forfeited. The Hanafi school distinguishes between ownership of the wage and its obligation, using the principle of equality (musawah) between lessor and lessee. Understanding these triggers — prepayment, stipulation, use, and especially mere ability to use — prevents errors in calculating dues and liabilities when the leased property becomes unavailable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the triggers for wage obligation
The passage lists four triggers: prepayment (ta'jil), stipulation of prepayment (shart al-ta'jil), actual use (istifa'), and ability to use (tamakkun). Note that tamakkun suffices even without actual use.
Memorize these four triggers; they are the key to the entire ruling.
2
Understand the principle of musawah
Ownership of the wage does not arise at contract because both parties are equal; prepayment or its condition breaks that equality, making the wage owned immediately.
This is a unique Hanafi reasoning based on the nature of exchange.
3
Distinguish actual use from ability to use
If the lessee receives the object and is able to use it (e.g., house delivered empty, no obstacle), the wage is due even if he does not use it. But if delivery is defective (e.g., not empty, outside period, prevented by ruler/usurper), no wage is due.
The key concept here is 'tamakkun' (ability); it is treated as equivalent to actual use.
4
Apply the rule for loss of ability (ghasb)
If a third party usurps (ghasb) the leased property, the wage drops proportionally to the loss of ability. 'Ghasb' here means any effective prevention, not the strict legal definition.
There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: some say the contract is rescinded, others say only the wage is suspended.
5
Note exceptions and proportional reduction
If the loss of ability is partial (e.g., flood, illness of slave), the wage reduces proportionately. If full, the wage drops entirely. Exception: if the lessee can remove the usurper through intercession, the wage remains due.
Proportional reduction is a manifestation of fairness in exchange contracts.

Source Text

But by its prepayment or by its condition or by using the benefit or being able to use it, so it is due for a house taken possession of but not lived in, and it is dropped by usurpation to the extent of the loss of ability. [Commentary] His statement: 'but by its prepayment' means the wage is obligatory and owned by prepaying it or by stipulating prepayment; because the prevention of ownership by the contract itself is due to the realization of equality, so if he prepaid or stipulated prepayment, he has nullified the equality that the contract required, unlike a deferred lease with a condition of prepayment because... His statement: 'or by using...' meaning by using the benefit which is the object of the contract, realizing equality between them, for the contract is a contract of exchange, and this is restricted to using within the period; if he mentioned a period and distance and rode to that place after the period elapsed, the wage is not due. If he did not use it and confined it in his house and the period passed, if he hired it to ride outside the city, the wage is not due; if inside the city, the wage is due; if it perishes in the first case, he is liable for his transgression by confinement, unlike the second case. Al-Tahtawi mentioned it. His statement: 'or being able to use it' means being able to use the benefit; he placed ability of the thing in the position of that thing; so if he handed it over empty of his belongings and there is no obstacle from a ruler or usurper, he has been able, and leaving use then is idleness, so it does not prevent the obligation of the wage. If he did not hand it over, or it was not empty, or he handed it over empty outside the period or during it but confined it in a place other than the place of lease or in its place, and there is a preventing excuse or not, and a ruler or usurper prevented him, or it was defective, then no wage; clearly stated by al-Hamawi and others. His statement: 'so it is due...' means the wage is due if the lessee took possession of the house and did not live in it until the period elapsed; because since delivery of the benefit itself is inconceivable, delivery of its place is put in its place; because ability to benefit is proven by it. It is mentioned in 'Majma' al-Anhur' quoting from 'al-Nawazil': 'If he hired an animal to Mecca and did not ride it, if there was no defect in the animal, he owes the wage; if it was due to a defect in it, no wage.' End. His statement: 'and it is dropped...' means the wage is dropped by usurpation. He said in 'al-Minh': except if it is possible to remove the usurper from the house for example by intercession and protection; thus restricted in 'al-Tatarkhaniyya' and 'al-Qunyah'. End. The reason for the drop: that delivery of the place was only put in place of delivery of the benefit for ability to benefit; so if ability is lost, delivery is lost, and the contract is rescinded to the extent of that loss, and the wage is dropped proportionately. Thus in 'al-Hidayah'. Al-Fadli and Qadi Khan mentioned in their 'Fatawa': the lease is not annulled, but the wage is dropped as long as it remains in the usurper's hand. End. The generality of the expression includes real estate and other; the meaning of usurpation here is the prevention between the lessee and the object, not its reality; so it is not objected that usurpation does not apply to real estate according to them, contrary to Muhammad—God—and their words are agreed on applying usurpation. His statement: 'to the extent of the loss of his ability'; so if his ability is lost for the entire period, the entire wage drops; if lost for part, it drops proportionately. If during the period something occurs that prevents use, such as if the leased house is usurped, or the leased land is flooded, or its irrigation is cut off, or the slave becomes ill or runs away, the wage drops proportionately. Stated clearly in 'al-Muhit' and others.
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling on when the wage becomes due in an ijarah contract and when it is forfeited. The author begins by stating that the wage becomes due and is owned by one of three means: prepayment by the lessee, stipulating prepayment in the contract, or actually using the benefit or being able to use it. The commentary explains that ownership does not arise at the contract because of the principle of equality (musawah) between the two parties; prepayment or its condition breaks that equality and triggers ownership. For a deferred lease (ijarah mugharradah), prepayment condition is discussed. Next, the ruling on using the benefit: if the lessee uses the hired item within the period, the wage is due. If he uses it after the period, it is not due. If he does not use it but confines it, the ruling depends on the location: for travel hires, confinement outside the city incurs liability if the animal perishes; for city hires, the wage is due simply by taking possession. The passage then clarifies that mere ability to use (tamakkun) suffices to obligate the wage. If the lessor delivers the property empty and accessible, and the lessee chooses not to use it, the wage is still due. However, if delivery is defective (e.g., not empty, outside period, or prevented by ruler/usurper), no wage is due. The text then addresses the case of usurpation (ghasb): if a third party usurps the leased item, the wage is dropped proportionally to the lessee's loss of ability to benefit. Some scholars say the ijarah contract is not rescinded, only the wage suspended. The passage emphasizes that 'ghasb' here means effective prevention, not the legal definition, so it applies even to real estate. Finally, it gives examples of partial loss of benefit (flood, illness, etc.) causing proportional reduction of the wage. Throughout, the reasoning is based on the principle that delivery of the object stands in for delivery of the benefit, and ability to use is the trigger for the wage.

Key Terms
التعجيل (al-ta'jil): Prepayment of the wage by the lessee, which triggers ownership of the wage for the lessor.
التمكن (al-tamakkun): The ability of the lessee to use the leased object after proper delivery, which obligates the wage even if not used.
الغصب (al-ghasb): Usurpation by a third party that prevents the lessee's ability to use the object; here it includes any effective prevention, not just legal ghasb.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a lessee hires an animal to travel to Mecca, but does not ride it because of a defect in the animal, what is the ruling on the wage?
A) The full wage is due because the lessee had the ability to use it.
B) No wage is due because the defect prevented use.
C) Half the wage is due.
D) The wage is due only if the lessee prepaid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the wage in ijarah is due upon the lessee's ability to use the object after proper delivery, and drops proportionally when that ability is lost due to usurpation or defect.

Usurpation Causes Proportional Fall of Hire
Explains that hire falls proportionally when lessee is prevented from use by usurpation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that hire falls proportionally when the lessee is prevented from use, and distinguish the two Hanafi views on whether the contract is rescinded.

Core Idea
Hire falls proportionally when lessee cannot benefit due to usurpation; contract may or may not be rescinded.

This lesson examines a critical refinement in ijarah: what happens to the hire when a usurper prevents the lessee from using the property? The passage clarifies that the hire falls proportionally to the loss of benefit, and introduces an intra-Hanafi difference over whether the contract itself is rescinded or merely the obligation to pay hire is suspended. Understanding this principle ensures just compensation for the lessee.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is an ijarah contract where the lessee is prevented from using the property by a usurper (ghasib). The ruling: the hire (ujrah) falls proportionally to the loss of the lessee's ability to benefit (tamakkun).
The amount of hire due equals the period of actual benefit; the rest is waived.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is rational (aqli): delivery of the premises (taslim al-mahal) is considered a substitute for delivery of the benefit. When the ability to benefit is lost, delivery is lost, and the contract is rescinded proportionally.
This reasoning is from al-Hidayah; it establishes a causal link between loss of benefit and fall of hire.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa (as in al-Hidayah) holds that the contract is rescinded partially. Al-Fadli and Qadi Khan hold that the contract is not rescinded, but the hire falls during the period of usurpation.
The practical result is the same: the hire falls. The disagreement is technical.
4
Understand the scope of 'ghasb'
In this passage, 'ghasb' does not mean strict legal usurpation (which applies only to movables). It means any prevention (haywalah) of the lessee from using the property, whether the property is movable or real estate.
This expansion includes flooding, illness of a slave, etc.
5
Apply to examples
If the entire period is affected, all hire falls. If only part, hire falls proportionally. Examples: flooded land, cut irrigation, sick or runaway slave, usurpation of house.
Consistent with al-Muhit and other sources.

He resides in it, and it falls due to usurpation to the extent of the loss of his ability [to benefit] (12) 517. A riding animal to Makkah, and he did not ride it: if there was no defect in the animal, then the hire is due upon him; and if there was a defect in it, then no hire [is due]. End. His statement: 'and it falls...' etc.; meaning: the hire falls due to usurpation. He said in al-Minh: except if it is possible to remove the usurper from the house, for example, by intercession and protection; thus he restricted it in al-Tatarikhaniyyah and al-Qunyah. End. The reason for the fall: that the delivery of the premises has been placed in the position of delivery of the benefit for the ability to benefit; so when the ability is lost, the delivery is lost, and the contract is rescinded to the extent of that loss, and the hire falls proportionally. As in al-Hidayah. And al-Fadli and Qadi Khan mentioned in their Fatawa: the ijarah is not rescinded, but the hire falls as long as it remains in the hand of the usurper. End. The general expression includes real estate and other things, and what is meant here by usurpation is prevention between the lessee and the property, not the reality [of usurpation]; so it cannot be objected that usurpation does not apply to real estate according to them, contrary to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him. And they all agreed on the use of the term usurpation. [2] His statement: 'to the extent of the loss of his ability'; so that if his ability is lost in the entire period, the entire hire falls; and if it is lost in part of it, it falls proportionally. Thus, if during the period something occurs that prevents benefit, such as if the leased house is usurped from the lessee, if the leased land is flooded, or its irrigation is cut off, or the slave becomes ill, or runs away, the hire falls proportionally. This is clearly stated in al-Muhit and others. (1) Meaning: if a usurper usurps the leased house from the lessee's possession during the period, the hire falls; even if the usurpation is in part of it, it falls proportionally. What is meant by usurpation here is prevention between the lessee and the property, not its reality, since usurpation does not apply to real estate according to us. See: Majma' al-Anhur (2:371). (2) From Majma' al-Anhur (2:371). (3) Minh al-Ghaffar (q2:? 1/231). (4) Al-Hidayah (3:232).
Source pages p. 517

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, a super-commentary on Sharh al-Wiqayah, discusses the effect of usurpation (ghasb) on the hire contract (ijarah). The base text states that the hire falls proportionally to the loss of the lessee's ability to benefit. The commentator explains that this is because delivery of the premises (tashim al-mahal) is effectively a substitute for delivery of the benefit (taslim al-manfa'ah), and the lessee's ability to benefit (tamakkun) is the basis. When that ability is lost, the delivery is lost, and the contract is rescinded proportionally. However, there is a difference of opinion: Abu Hanifa's view (as in al-Hidayah) is that the contract is rescinded partially, while al-Fadli and Qadi Khan hold that the contract is not rescinded but the hire falls during the period of usurpation. The commentator clarifies that 'usurpation' here means prevention (haywalah) of the lessee from using the property, not the strict legal definition of ghasb (which only applies to movable property according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; Muhammad disagrees). Thus, the ruling applies to both movables and real estate. The fall of hire is proportional to the loss of benefit: if the entire period is affected, all hire falls; if only part, then only that part falls. Examples include flooding of land, loss of irrigation, illness or running away of a slave. This ruling is found in al-Muhit and other works.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): In this context, ghasb refers to any prevention (haywalah) of the lessee from using the leased property, not the strict legal usurpation which only applies to movable goods.
تمكن (tamakkun): The lessee's ability to take benefit from the leased property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because delivery of the premises is a substitute for delivery of the benefit; loss of ability to benefit means loss of delivery.
C) Because the contract becomes void automatically.
D) Because the lessee can claim compensation from the usurper.

Key Takeaway
Hire falls proportionally to the loss of benefit due to any prevention of use, regardless of whether the contract is formally rescinded.

When Does Hire Become Due? The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains when the lessor can demand hire: daily for houses, per stage for animals, after completion for work.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the later Hanafi position on when hire is due in ijarah contracts and explain the refinement from the early view, applying the distinction between periodic and completion-based benefit.

Core Idea
Hire is due as benefit is received: daily for houses, per stage for animals, after completion for work.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah addresses a critical practical question in ijarah: when can the lessor demand payment? The Hanafi school experienced an internal refinement from an earlier view that no hire is due until the entire benefit is fully received, to a later position that hire accrues proportionally as the benefit is enjoyed. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind both views and identifies which is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the later Hanafi position
Identify the mufta bihi ruling: hire is due according to the nature of the benefit—daily for houses/land, per stage for animals, after completion for work.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa (later), Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The early view of Abu Hanifa and Zufar held that no hire is due until the entire benefit is completely received, regardless of contract type.
Their reasoning: the subject matter is the aggregate of benefits (jumlat al-manafi'), so the hire is indivisible.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the qiyas used: just as the price in a sale is not divided, and the pledge in a debt is not apportioned, the hire is not divided over parts of the benefit.
They analogized to complete, unitary subject matters.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The later Hanafi view countered by distinguishing continuous benefits (where each part is independently intended) from work benefits (where partial work is not beneficial). They used qiyas on nafaqah (maintenance), which is due daily.
Al-Uthqani added that the parties can stipulate otherwise, showing flexibility.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under the early view, the lessor gets nothing until the very end; under the later view, the lessor can demand payment as benefit accrues, preventing hardship.
The later view is the operative fatwa and is more practical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

His statement: 'And for the lessor...' etc.; meaning: the lessor may demand the hire from the lessee for the house and the leased land, if a known period is specified, for each day; because the lessee has received a intended benefit, and what is less than a day has no limit, so it becomes like maintenance (nafaqah) which is demanded at nightfall, not every hour. And this is when it is unrestricted. But if the time of entitlement is specified in the contract, it becomes determined; because it is like acceleration (ta'jil), as if he said: 'I lease this house to you for a year on the condition that you give the hire after a month, for example.' And al-Uthqani said: 'If in all respects they stipulate the acceleration or postponement of the hire, then it is upon what they stipulated, because they have turned away from the principle of equivalence.' End. [2] His statement: 'And for the riding animal...'; meaning: the lessor may demand the hire from the lessee for the leased riding animal for crossing the distance for each stage; because the travel of each stage is intended. And from Abu Yusuf: if he leases a house to reside in for a month, the hire does not become due until he completes the residence of the month; and if he traveled half the road or one-third, it becomes due proportionally. Mentioned by al-Quhustani and others. [3] His statement: 'And for the tailoring...' etc.; meaning: the lessor may demand the hire from the lessee for washing the garment, tailoring, dyeing, and other crafts when the washing, tailoring, and similar are completed for the entire work; because the work in part is not benefited from, so it does not necessitate hire in exchange for it, until he finishes the work, then the whole becomes due. And know that the supreme, most generous Imam (Abu Hanifa) used to say initially – this is also the saying of Zufar – that nothing of the hire is due except after receiving all the benefit, whether the contract is for a period, as in leasing a house or land, or for covering a distance, as in hiring a riding animal to Makkah, or for work, as in tailoring and similar. And the reasoning for that: the subject matter of the contract is the total benefits in the period, so the hire is not divided over its parts, just as if the subject matter were the work, and like the price in a sale, and the pledge in a debt. (1) In Jami' al-Rumuz (2:68).
Source pages p. 518

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah discusses the timing of when the lessor (mu'jir) can demand the hire (ujrah) from the lessee (musta'jir). The commentator explains three types of ijarah: (1) For houses and land: the lessor can demand hire daily, because each day's benefit is a distinct intended benefit; the preposition 'on' (انتصاب) of the benefit is measured by time, and what is less than a day has no legal limit. This is analogous to maintenance (nafaqah) which is due at evening. However, if the parties specify a time for payment in the contract, that governs. (2) For riding animals hired for travel: the lessor can demand hire at each stage (manzil) because each stage's journey is an intended portion. Abu Yusuf is reported to have a different view: for house lease, hire is not due until the full month is completed, but for travel, hire becomes due proportionally as stages are covered. (3) For work contracts (like tailoring, washing): hire is due only upon completion of the entire work, because partial work is not beneficial. Then the commentator notes the early position of Imam Abu Hanifa and Zufar that no hire is due at all until the entire benefit is fully received, regardless of type. The reasoning is that the subject matter of the contract is the aggregate of benefits (jumlat al-manafi'), so hire is not apportioned. As a point of intra-Hanafi dispute, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the later view: hire is due periodically as benefits are received. This is a critical clarification for practice.

Key Terms
أجر (ajr): The rental payment or hire due from the lessee to the lessor.
قصارة (qisarah): The work of washing or fulling cloth, a craft hired.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) After each stage of the work (e.g., cutting, stitching).
C) Only after complete work is finished.
D) At the time of contract signing.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the timing of hire entitlement depends on the nature of the benefit: periodic for continuous benefit (houses, travel), completion-based for work, and any contractual stipulation governs.

Timing of Wage Payment in Ijarah Contracts
Expansion of ijarah wage timing with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on when wage becomes due in ijarah for time-based, distance-based, and work-based contracts, and differentiate the final position from Imam Abu Hanifa's initial view and Zufar's position.

Core Idea
For time and distance, wage is due proportionately; for work, only after completion — practicality (istihsan) over strict analogy.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on when a hirer can demand payment in an ijarah contract. The passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute where Imam Abu Hanifa initially held that no wage is due until the entire contract term is completed, similar to a sale. However, he later retracted this due to practical hardship, adopting a position that divides continuous benefits into convenient units. This ruling demonstrates the Hanafi method of istihsan over strict qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of ijarah contracts
The passage distinguishes contracts based on time (house/land), distance (riding animal), and work (laundering/tailoring). Each type has a different rule for wage accrual.
Time-based: house/land; distance-based: animal hire; work-based: service like tailoring.
2
Understand Imam Abu Hanifa's initial view
He and Zufar held that no wage is due until all benefit is received, citing the entire subject matter as indivisible. Analogous to a sale where price is not due for part of goods.
This view considers the contract as a single unit.
3
Follow the retraction and final position
Abu Hanifa retracted, making wage due proportionately for time and distance (day by day, stage by stage) but only after completion for work.
The reasoning is istihsan: hourly payment would cause hardship.
4
Analyze the underlying reasoning
Strict analogy (qiyas) would demand hourly payment, but istihsan allows practical units. For work, the benefit is not evenly divisible, so payment is only after complete work. A nuance: if work is at hiree's premises, some sources treat it like time-based.
Al-Mabsut and others consider work at hiree's home as akin to time-based.
5
Apply the mufta bihi ruling
In practice, for a monthly rental, wage accrues daily; for a journey, per stage; for tailoring, after the garment is sewn. Zufar's view would mean no payment if the contract is terminated early.
The final position is practical and widely accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللمؤجر طلب الأجرة للدار والأرض لكلّ يوم، وللدابة لكل مرحلة، وللقصارة والخياطة إذا تمت وإن عمل في بيت المستأجر. واعلم أن الإمام الأعظم الأكرم له كان يقول أولاً: وهو قول زفر له أنه لا يجب شيء من الأجر إلا بعد استيفاء جميع المنفعة، سواء كان العقد على المدة، كما في إجارة الدار والأرض، أو على قطع المسافة كما في كراء الدابة إلى مكة، أو على العمل كما في القصارة والخياطة ونحوها. ووجه ذلك: إن المعقود عليه جملة المنافع في المدة، فلا يتوزع الأجر على أجزائها كما إذا كان المعقود عليه العمل، وكالثمن في المبيع، والرهن في الدين. ثم رجع وقال: إن وقعت الإجارة على المدة أو على قطع المسافة يجب إيفاء الأجر بحصة ما استوفى من المنافع إذا كان لما استوفى حصة معلومة من الأجر، ففي الدار يجب الإيفاء يوماً فيوماً، وفي قطع المسافة مرحلة فمرحلة. وفي الإجارة التي تنعقد على العمل ويبقى للعامل أثر في العين، لا يجب إيفاء الأجر إلا بعد إيفاء العمل، وإن كان حصة ما استوفى من العمل معلوماً سواء عمل في بيت المستأجر أو في بيته على ما في «التجريد» و«الهداية»، إلا أن يكون العمل في بيت المستأجر على ما في «المبسوط» و«الفوائد الظهيرية» وغيرهما، فإنه حينئذ كالدار والدابة. ووجه القول المرجوع إليه: إن القياس استحقاق الأجر ساعة فساعة؛ لتحقق المساواة إلا أن المطالبة في كل ساعة يقع بها الضرر؛ لأنه لا يعلم حصته إلا بمشقة، ولا يتضرع لغيره، فقدرناها باليوم والمرحلة استحساناً.
And the hirer may demand the rent for the house and land for each day, and for the riding animal for each stage, and for laundering and tailoring when completed, even if he worked in the house of the hiree. Know that the Greatest Imam, may mercy be upon him, first said – and this is the saying of Zufar – that no part of the wage becomes due except after complete enjoyment of all benefit, whether the contract is for a period, as in renting a house or land, or for covering a distance, as in hiring a riding animal to Mecca, or for work, as in laundering and tailoring and the like. The reason: that the subject matter of the contract is the total benefits over the period, so the wage is not distributed over its parts, just as if the subject matter were the work itself, and like the price in a sale and the pledge in a debt. Then he retracted and said: if the hire is for a period or for covering a distance, payment of the wage becomes due proportionately to the benefit received, if that received benefit has a known portion of the wage; so for the house, payment becomes due day by day, and for covering a distance, stage by stage. But for a hire that is contracted for work and leaves a trace in the object, payment of the wage is not due except after completing the work, even if the portion of work completed is known, whether the work is done in the hiree's house or in his own house, according to what is in al-Tajrid and al-Hidayah, except if the work is in the hiree's house, according to what is in al-Mabsut and al-Fawa'id al-Zahirah and others, then it is like the house and the riding animal. And the reasoning for the retracted opinion is that analogy would require wage to be due hour by hour, due to the equality, but demanding it every hour would cause hardship because one does not know its portion except with difficulty, and it is not oppressive to others, so we estimated it by the day and the stage as istihsan.
Source pages p. 518

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of a ruling in the chapter of ijarah (hire) about when the wage becomes due. The author first states the standard Hanafi ruling: the hirer (owner of the benefit) can demand payment for a house or land for each day, for a riding animal for each stage (e.g., each day's journey), and for piecework like laundering and tailoring only after the work is completed. This ruling reflects the final position of Imam Abu Hanifa. The passage then narrates an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa initially held a different view, which was also the view of Zufar, that no wage is due until the entire term of the contract is completed, whether the contract is for a period (e.g., renting a house for a month), for distance (e.g., hiring an animal for a journey), or for work (e.g., tailoring a garment). The reasoning was that the contract is on the total benefits, not on parts. Then Imam Abu Hanifa retracted this and adopted the position that for time-based or distance-based contracts, wage accrues proportionally (daily for a house, per stage for a journey), while for work-based contracts, it is only due after completion. The final position is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view. The passage also notes a difference among later sources: some hold that if the work is done in the hiree's premises, it is treated like time-based contracts. The underlying principle is istihsan (juristic preference) over strict analogy (qiyas), which would demand hourly payment but would cause hardship. Thus, the Hanafi school pragmatically divides the contract into convenient units.

Key Terms
إجارة (ijarah): A contract of hire or lease for a defined benefit (manfa'ah) in exchange for a fixed wage.
أجرة (ujrah): The wage or rent paid in exchange for the usufruct.
مؤجر (mu'ajjir): The person who provides the asset or service in an ijarah contract; the hirer (owner of the benefit).
قصارة (qasara): The craft of laundering and pressing cloth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the final mufta bihi position of Imam Abu Hanifa, when does the wage become due for a house rented by the month?
A) After the entire month is completed
B) Day by day as the tenant stays
C) At the end of each week
D) Only if the tenant leaves early

Key Takeaway
In ijarah, wage accrues continuously for time and distance but only upon completion for work — an application of istihsan over qiyas to avoid hardship.

When the Wage Becomes Due in Ijarah: Tailoring, Baking, and Time/Distance Hire
Commentary on rulings for wage entitlement in tailoring, baking, and time-based hire

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on when the wage becomes due in ijarah for result-based work (tailoring, baking) and time/distance-based hire, and apply qiyas and istihsan to determine wage entitlement.

Core Idea
Wage is due upon completion, but proportional payment applies when external factors disrupt work or for time/distance hire to avoid hardship.

This lesson explores a critical distinction in Hanafi ijarah law: when does the worker become entitled to the wage? The passage from Umdat al-Ri'ayah examines three scenarios—tailoring, baking, and hire for a period or distance—revealing how the school uses qiyas and istihsan to balance legal principle with practical necessity. Understanding this ruling is essential for correctly structuring hire contracts and resolving disputes over partial performance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what type of ijarah is being discussed (result-based or time/distance) and the default ruling on when the wage is due.
Result-based: wage due upon completion. Time/distance: wage due proportionally.
2
Locate the dalil: qiyas and istihsan
The text uses qiyas to argue for proportional entitlement but overrides it with istihsan in time/distance hire to avoid hardship. Trace the reasoning.
Qiyas would demand hourly payment, but istihsan groups into days/stages.
3
Analyze the exceptions
Note the exceptions: partial work due to theft, and work done in the hirer's house for trace-based contracts. These trigger proportional wage.
Theft makes partial work known; hirer's house changes delivery.
4
Compare intra-Hanafi positions
Al-Karkhi and Abu Hanifa differ on the method of estimation. Abu Hanifa's view (returned to) allows wage for any measurable portion.
The returned opinion becomes the mufta bihi.
5
Apply to a new scenario
Given a hypothetical case, determine when the wage is due using the principles from this passage.
Consider location (hirer's house vs. worker's house) and completion status.

Source pages p. 519

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on rulings regarding when the wage becomes due in different types of ijarah (hire contracts). It covers three main scenarios: tailoring, hire on time/distance, and baking. The commentary is an expansion of the base text from al-Wiqayah, explaining the legal reasoning and differences of opinion within the Hanafi school.

First, the tailoring scenario: if a tailor works in the hirer's house and sews part of a cloth, and then the cloth is stolen, the tailor is entitled to a wage proportionate to the work done. This is because the partial work is known relative to the total, so the wage is due for what was completed. However, if the work is not completed on any part (e.g., he only started but did not finish any portion), he cannot demand any wage because there is no estimation for incomplete parts. This ruling applies even if the work is done in the hirer's house, and it is based on the principle that the wage follows the work completed.

Second, the passage discusses a returned opinion regarding hire contracts based on time (e.g., renting a house) or distance (e.g., hiring a animal for travel). In such contracts, the wage is due proportionally as the benefit is received—day by day for a house, stage by stage for travel. For hire contracts where the worker leaves a trace on the object (like tailoring or baking), the default rule is that the wage is only due upon full completion of the work, even if partial work is known. However, according to some sources (al-Mabsut and al-Fawaid al-Zahiriyyah), if the work is done in the hirer's house, it is treated like time/distance hire, and the wage is due as each part is completed. The returned opinion is based on istihsan (juristic preference), preferring to avoid hardship from hourly demands, so they estimated by day/stage.

Third, the baking scenario: a baker becomes entitled to the wage immediately upon taking the bread out of the oven because that is the completion of the work. If he works in the baker's house, delivery to the hirer is not considered until the bread is handed over; if he bakes in the hirer's house, taking out constitutes delivery. The commentary also clarifies that if the bread burns after removal without any fault of the baker, the wage is still due because the work was complete. The footnotes provide additional clarifications: the estimation by day/stage is attributed to al-Karkhi, while Abu Hanifa's view is that the wage is due as soon as any measurable work is done. The passage also notes that the word 'tannur' (oven) is of Arabic origin despite some claims.

Throughout, the commentary relies on analogical reasoning and juristic preference, with references to earlier Hanafi works.

Key Terms
إجارة (ijarah): A contract of hire/lease where one party provides a benefit (service or usufruct) in exchange for a wage.
استحقاق الأجر (istihqaq al-ajr): Entitlement to receive the wage; when the wage becomes due and payable.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference used to deviate from strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a ruling that avoids hardship or conforms to custom.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to a shared effective cause ('illa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a tailor sews part of a cloth in the hirer's house and then the cloth is stolen?
A) The tailor is entitled to no wage because the work is incomplete.
B) The tailor is entitled to the full wage as if the work were completed.
C) The tailor is entitled to a wage proportionate to the part he sewed.
D) The tailor is only entitled to wage if the cloth was not stolen.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijarah, wage entitlement depends on the nature of the contract: full completion for trace-based work, but proportional payment is allowed when external factors prevent completion or for time/distance hire, based on istihsan.

Baker's Wage and Liability: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Burning After Removal
Ruling on wage and liability for burned bread with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a baker's wage is due and explain the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding liability for bread that burns after removal from the oven.

Core Idea
Wage is due upon removal from the oven, but liability for burning depends on whether delivery has occurred.

The Hanafi school agrees that a baker hired to bake bread (ajir mushtarak) earns his wage upon removing the bread from the oven—this constitutes completion and delivery if done in the customer's house. However, a dispute arises when the bread burns after removal but before the customer takes actual possession. Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), differ on whether the baker remains liable. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the proof, and the practical implications of this intra-Hanafi difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic rule on wage entitlement
The matn states that the baker gets his wage upon removing the bread from the oven. Understand why: the work is completed and delivery is effected when the bread is placed in the customer's house (if baking there).
This is the agreed-upon foundation; the dispute does not contradict this.
2
Distinguish Abu Hanifa's position on liability
According to Abu Hanifa, the baker is not liable for the bread in either case (burning before or after removal) because no injury (itlaf) came from his action.
Abu Hanifa treats the baker as a trustee (amin) who is only liable for his own fault.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's contrasting view
The Sahibayn hold that the baker is liable if the bread burns before removal (because the work is incomplete and the bread is still in his guarantee) but not after removal (because delivery has occurred). They consider the ajir mushtarak as holding a guaranteed trust (amanah mardudah) until actual delivery.
Their position introduces a distinction based on the timing of the damage relative to delivery.
4
Examine the proofs (dalil) for each view
Abu Hanifa’s proof: the baker did not cause the burning, so no guarantee. The Sahibayn’s proof: the baker is like a usurper (ghasib) until actual delivery; mere placement in the owner's house is not sufficient to transfer liability. They analogize to the tailor scenario (qiyas jaliy).
Both use analogy but differ on the condition for delivery.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical difference: if bread burns after removal but before the owner picks it up, Abu Hanifa says no liability; the Sahibayn say liability unless the owner has taken actual possession. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the Sahibayn's view, as preferred by al-Quduri and the author of al-Hidayah.
The mufta bihi aligns with the stricter view to protect the owner’s property.

وللخبز بعد إخراجه من التنور فإن احترق بعدما أخرجه فينبغي أن يكون كذلك في هذه المسألة أيضاً، لكن نقول بوجوب الأجرة عند تمام العمل هاهنا ؛ لأنّ عمل الخياط انتهى على بعض الثوب بفعل السرقة فهو معلوم بالنسبة إلى الكل فيجب الأجر بقدر عمله. بخلاف ما نحن فيه، فإنّ عمل الخياط لم ينته على بعض الثوب، ويمتنع طلب الأجرة بكل عمل قليل، ولا تقدير للأبعاض فلا جرم أن يتوقف الطلب على كل العمل، فلا يجب الأجر إلا إذا تم عمله. [1] قوله : وللخبز ... الخ ؛ أي وللمؤجر طلب الإجرة من المستأجر للخبز بعد أن يخرجه من التنور ؛ لأنَّ تمام العمل بالإخراج، فيملك المطالبة كالخياط إذا فرغ من العمل، قال الزَّيْلَعِيُّ (١) : هذا إذا كان يخبز في بيت المستأجر ؛ لأنه صار مسلماً إليه بمجرد الإخراج فيستحق الأجر، وإن كان في منزل الخباز لم يكن مسلماً إليه بمجرد الإخراج من التنور. انتهى. [٢] قوله : بعد الإخراج ؛ في إطلاق العبارة إشارة إلى أنه يستحق الأجر بإخراج البعض بقدره ؛ لأنَّ العمل في ذلك القدر صارَ مسلّماً إلى صاحب الدقيق. صرّح به في «مجمع الأنهر»، وغيره. [۳] قوله : من التنور ؛ التنور ما يخبز فيه، ووافقت فيه لغة العرب لغة العجم، وقال أبو حاتم : ليس بعربي، والجمع التنانير. كذا في «المصباح». (٤) قوله : احترق ؛ أي من غير فعله ؛ ولذا لم يقل : فإن أحرقه، فسقط ما أورد صاحب «المنح ) تبعاً لصاحب الدرر ) من أنه غير موافق للمنقول عن الأئمة الفحول ؛ لأنّ المراد في «الغاية» وغيرها ما يكون بصنعه كما يدل عليه قوله بالإجماع.
كتاب الإجارة باب الأجر متى يستحق فله الأجرة وقبله لا ، ولا غرم فيهما هذا عند أبي حنيفة له، لأنه وعندهما يضمن مثل دقيقِهِ ولا أجر، وإن شاءَ ضمنه الخبز، وأعطاهُ الأجرة. [1] قوله : فله الأجرة ؛ لأن العمل قد تم وصح التسليم لقيام يد المالك على الخبز بواسطة قيامها على منزله. (٢) قوله : وقبله لا ؛ أي وإن احترق الخبرُ قبل إخراجه من التنور لا أجر له لعدم وجود تمام العمل. [۳] قوله : ولا غرم فيهما ؛ أي في حالتي الاحتراق بعد إخراجه من التنور وقبله على الأجير؛ لأنه لم يوجد منه جناية. [٤] قوله : هذا عند...الخ ؛ قيل هذا قول الكلّ، أما عند أبي حنيفة الله ؛ فلأنه لم يهلك بصنعه، وأما عندهما ؛ فلأنه هلك بعد التسليم. وذكر القُدُوري في «شرحه»: إنّ على قولهما يجب الضمان ؛ لأنه أجير مشترك، والعين في يده أمانة عنده مضمونة عندهما ، فلا يبرأ إلا بعد حقيقة التسليم، وهو اختيار صاحب «الهداية» كالغاصب لا يبرأ عن الضمان إلا بالتسليم دون الوضع في بيته. كذا في «الكفاية». [0] قوله : وعندهما ... الخ ؛ يعني وعندهما يجب الضمان على الأجير؛ لأنه أجير مشترك، والعينُ في يده مضمونة عندهما ، ثمّ صاحب الدقيق إن شاء ضمنه دقيقاً مثل دقيقه، ولا أجر له لكونه مضموناً عليه فلا يبرأ بوضعه في بيته إلا بعد حقيقة التسليم ، والوضع في بيته ليس من حقيقة التسليم. وإن شاء ضمنه قيمة خبزه وله الأجر، ولا يجب عليه ضمان الحطب والملح ؛ لأنَّ ذلك صار مستهلكاً قبل وجوب الضمان، وحينما وجب الضمان كان رماداً.
And for the baker after removing it from the oven: if it burns after he removes it, it should be the same in this matter as well. But we say the wage is obligatory upon completion of the work here, because the tailor's work ended on part of the garment due to the theft, so it is known relative to the whole, thus the wage is due for the amount of his work. Contrary to our case, the tailor's work did not end on part of the garment, and demanding wage for every small work is not allowed, and there is no estimation for parts, so inevitably the demand depends on the whole work, so the wage is not due except when his work is completed. [1] His saying: 'And for the baker...' meaning the lessor asks for the wage from the lessee for the bread after he removes it from the oven, because the completion of the work is by removal, so he may make the claim like the tailor when he finishes the work. Al-Zayla'i said: This is if he bakes in the lessee's house, because it becomes delivered to him merely by removal, so he deserves the wage. If it is in the baker's house, it is not delivered to him merely by removal from the oven. End. [2] His saying: 'after removal' – in the absoluteness of the expression is an indication that he deserves the wage for removing part equal to it, because the work in that amount becomes delivered to the owner of the flour. This is clarified in Majma' al-Anhur and others. [3] His saying: 'from the oven' – the oven is what is used for baking, and the Arab language agreed with the Persian language, and Abu Hatim said: it is not Arabic, and the plural is tananeer. This is in al-Misbah. (4) His saying: 'burns' – meaning not by his action; therefore he did not say: 'if he burns it', so what was raised by the author of al-Minhah following the author of al-Durar falls away, that it is not in accordance with what is transmitted from the great imams, because what is intended in al-Ghayah and others is what is by his action, as indicated by his saying 'by consensus'. Book of Ijarah, Chapter on when the wage is due: So he has the wage, and before it he does not, and there is no liability in both cases. This is according to Abu Hanifa, because he [the baker] does not guarantee, and according to the two associates [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] he guarantees the like of his flour and no wage, and if he wants, he guarantees the bread and gives him the wage. [1] His saying: 'So he has the wage' – because the work has been completed and delivery is valid due to the owner's hand being established on the bread via its establishment on his house. (2) His saying: 'and before it he does not' – meaning if the bread burns before removing it from the oven, he has no wage due to lack of completion of work. [3] His saying: 'and there is no liability in both cases' – meaning in the two cases of burning after removal from the oven and before it, there is no liability on the hired worker because no injury came from him. [4] His saying: 'This is according to ...' – it is said this is the statement of all. As for according to Abu Hanifa, because it did not perish by his action; as for according to the two associates, because it perished after delivery. And al-Quduri mentioned in his Sharh: According to their statement, guarantee is obligatory because he is a shared hired worker, and the object in his hand is a trust according to him but guaranteed according to them, so he is not released except after actual delivery, and this is the choice of the author of al-Hidayah, like the usurper who is not released from guarantee except by delivery, not by placing in his house. This is in al-Kifayah. [0] His saying: 'and according to the two associates...' meaning that according to the two associates, guarantee is obligatory on the hired worker because he is a shared hired worker, and the object in his hand is guaranteed according to them. Then the owner of the flour, if he wants, he guarantees flour like his flour, and he has no wage because it is guaranteed upon him, so he is not released by placing it in his house except after actual delivery, and placing in his house is not actual delivery. And if he wants, he guarantees the value of his bread and he has the wage, and he is not obligated to guarantee the firewood and salt because that was consumed before the guarantee became obligatory, and when the guarantee became obligatory, it was ash.
Source pages p. 520

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute. It opens with the matn statement: the baker earns his wage upon removing bread from the oven. The commentator explains that completion of work is defined by removal, analogous to a tailor finishing his work. However, if the baker bakes in his own house, mere removal does not constitute delivery. The author then addresses the scenario of burning: if the bread burns after removal, the baker still gets his wage and is not liable; if before removal, no wage and no liability. The key dispute is between Abu Hanifa and the two associates (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Abu Hanifa says the baker is not liable in either case because no injury came from him. The Sahibayn distinguish: after removal, the bread is delivered (since the owner's hand is on the house), so burning is after delivery and the baker is not liable. Before removal, the baker is liable because the object is still in his guarantee as a shared hired worker; the owner may claim either the equivalent flour (no wage) or the value of bread (with wage). The commentator notes that al-Quduri and the author of al-Hidayah prefer the Sahibayn's view, comparing the baker to a usurper who is not released until actual delivery. The passage clarifies the conditions for wage entitlement and the impact of delivery.

Key Terms
أجير مشترك (ajir mushtarak): A hired worker who works for multiple employers or is paid for the work itself (not for time). Here, the baker is considered an ajir mushtarak because he is hired to produce a specific result (baked bread).
مسلم إليه (musallam ilayhi): The state of being delivered to the customer. For the baker, the bread becomes musallam ilayhi upon removal from the oven if baking in the customer's house.
تمام العمل (tamam al-'amal): Completion of the work. For the baker, this is defined as removing the bread from the oven. For a tailor, finishing the garment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, if a baker (ajir mushtarak) bakes bread in the customer's house and the bread burns after removal from the oven but before the customer takes possession, what is the ruling?
A) The baker gets his wage and is not liable for the bread.
B) The baker gets no wage and must guarantee the flour.
C) The baker gets his wage but must guarantee the bread.
D) The baker is not liable and gets no wage.

Key Takeaway
For a baker hired to bake in the customer's house, wage entitlement and freedom from liability both depend on removal from the oven, which constitutes delivery; but according to the mufta bihi (Sahibayn), if the bread burns before removal, the baker is liable and forfeits his wage unless the customer opts for the bread's value.
