Baker's Wage and Liability: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on baker's liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) on a baker's liability for burned bread and explain the practical consequence of the dispute.

Core Idea
For Abu Hanifa, the baker is free of liability once bread is removed from the oven; for the two companions, liability persists until actual delivery to the owner.

The passage addresses a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: when a hired baker's bread burns after removal from the oven, who bears the loss? Abu Hanifa holds the baker is not liable and entitled to his wage, viewing the work as complete and the bread as a trust in the baker's hand. His two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, disagree: they consider the baker a common worker (ajir mushtarak) with a guaranteed article, so he remains liable until the owner physically takes delivery. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each view and its practical outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the core issue
The case: a baker (ajir mushtarak) bakes bread for a customer. The bread is removed from the oven but before the owner picks it up, it burns. The question is whether the baker is liable for the loss and whether he is still entitled to his wage.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his reasoning
Abu Hanifa rules that the baker is entitled to his wage and not liable. His reasoning: the work (baking) is completed upon removal from the oven, and the owner has constructive possession through his house (where the bread is placed). The bread is a trust (amanah) in the baker's hand, and no tort (jinaayah) occurred.
The key concept: taslim (delivery) is achieved by the owner's hand being on the house via the baker's placement.
3
State the two companions' position and their reasoning
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold the baker liable for the value of flour (or bread) and not entitled to the wage unless he compensates by delivering bread. Their reasoning: the baker is a common worker (ajir mushtarak), and the article in his hand is guaranteed (mamunah), not a pure trust. Actual delivery (haqiqat al-taslim) is required; placing in the house is insufficient, analogous to a usurper (ghasib) who must return the item to the owner's possession.
Contrast: for a private worker (ajir khas), the item is a trust and no liability without negligence.
4
Analyze the concept of 'ajir mushtarak' and its implications
The dispute hinges on whether the baker is treated as a common worker (liable for the article in his hand) or a trustee. Understanding the classification of workers in Hanafi fiqh is crucial: ajir mushtarak is not an exclusive employee, so his liability is stricter.
The passage notes that this difference affects the ruling on wage and compensation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under Abu Hanifa, the baker is safe: he gets paid and does not pay for the loss. Under the two companions, the owner has a choice: demand the value of flour (replacing the raw material) and forfeit the wage, or demand the value of bread (compensating for the finished product) and pay the wage. The practical impact is significant for bakeries and workers.
The author of al-Hidayah preferred the two companions' view, making it the mufta bihi in the commentary's context.

فله الأجرة (1) وقبله لا، ولا غرمَ فيهما (3)، هذا عند أبي حنيفة له، لأنه أمانة عنده، وعندهما يضمن مثل دقيقِهِ ولا أجر، وإن شاءَ ضمنه الخبز، وأعطاهُ الأجرة. (4) قوله: فله الأجرة؛ لأن العمل قد تم وصح التسليم لقيام يد المالك على الخبز بواسطة قيامها على منزله. (2) قوله: وقبله لا؛ أي وإن احترق الخبرُ قبل إخراجه من التنور لا أجر له لعدم وجود تمام العمل. [3] قوله: ولا غرم فيهما؛ أي في حالتي الاحتراق بعد إخراجه من التنور وقبله على الأجير؛ لأنه لم يوجد منه جناية. [4] قوله: هذا عند...الخ؛ قيل هذا قول الكلّ، أما عند أبي حنيفة الله؛ فلأنه لم يهلك بصنعه، وأما عندهما؛ فلأنه هلك بعد التسليم. وذكر القُدُوري في «شرحه»: إنّ على قولهما يجب الضمان؛ لأنه أجير مشترك، والعين في يده أمانة عنده مضمونة عندهما، فلا يبرأ إلا بعد حقيقة التسليم، وهو اختيار صاحب «الهداية» كالغاصب لا يبرأ عن الضمان إلا بالتسليم دون الوضع في بيته. كذا في «الكفاية».
He is entitled to the wage (1) and not before, and there is no liability in either case (3). This according to Abu Hanifa, because it is a trust in his possession. But according to the two companions, he guarantees the like of his flour and no wage, and if he wishes, he guarantees the bread and gives him the wage. (4) His saying: 'He is entitled to the wage' because the work is completed and delivery is valid as the owner's hand is on the bread through his hand on his house. (2) His saying: 'and not before' meaning if the bread burned before removal from the oven, he has no wage because the work is not completed. [3] His saying: 'and there is no liability in either case' meaning in both cases of burning after removal and before, the hired worker is not liable because no injury came from him. [4] His saying: 'This according to...' Some say this is the statement of all; according to Abu Hanifa, because it did not perish by his act; according to them, because it perished after delivery. Al-Quduri mentioned in his commentary that according to their view, liability is obligatory because he is a common worker, and the article in his hand is a trust according to him but guaranteed according to them, so he is not absolved except after actual delivery. This is the choice of the author of al-Hidayah, like the usurper who is not absolved from liability except by delivery, not by placing in his house. As in al-Kifayah.
Source pages p. 521

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the liability of a hired baker (ajir mushtarak) when the bread burns after removal from the oven. The base text states that the baker is entitled to his wage after removing the bread, but not before, and there is no liability in either case. The commentator then explains that this is the position of Abu Hanifa, for whom the article is a trust (amanah) in the baker's hand, and since the work is completed (by removing the bread), the owner takes constructive possession via the baker's house, so the baker is discharged. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two companions) hold that the baker is liable because he is a common worker and the article in his hand is guaranteed (mamunah) according to them. They require actual delivery (haqiqat al-taslim) to absolve him of liability; placing in the baker's house is not sufficient, analogous to a usurper (ghasib). Therefore, the owner has a choice: he can demand the like of his flour from the baker and forfeit the wage, or demand the value of the bread and pay the wage. The passage also notes that this is the relied-upon position in al-Hidayah and al-Kifayah. The reasoning turns on the definition of 'completion of work' and 'delivery', highlighting the Hanafi usul principle that a common worker's liability differs from a private worker's because he is not exclusively contracted.

Key Terms
الأجير المشترك (ajir mushtarak): A hired worker who works for multiple people or is not exclusively contracted; his liability is higher because the article in his hand is guaranteed.
التسليم (taslim): Delivery of the object to the owner; actual physical handover removes liability from the hired worker.
الضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss or damage; here, the baker must pay the like of flour or value of bread if liable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when does the hired baker become entitled to his wage for baking?
A) Immediately upon placing the dough in the oven
B) After the bread is removed from the oven
C) Only after the bread is delivered to the owner's hand
D) After the dough is mixed

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on the baker's liability turns on the definition of 'delivery' (taslim): Abu Hanifa accepts constructive delivery, while the two companions insist on actual delivery, affecting both wage entitlement and liability.
